- **Decision:** A (bundle into Unit 7 Q9.2 next-turn slice: F24 + D171 + parity scenarios + stratify).
- **Rationale:** Substrate need is independently clear (`patterns/orchestration` `classify` uses it; PY port will too). Scenario author for orchestration `classify` is the load-bearing receipt; pre-binding stratify avoids the parity scenario blocking on substrate.
- **Affects:** `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/stratify.rs` (new file, ~50 LOC); `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/operator_bindings.rs` (`register_stratify`); `packages/parity-tests/scenarios/operators/stratify.test.ts` (new file).

### D200 — Unit 8: 4-layer folder model inside `@graphrefly/graphrefly` — `base/utils/presets/solutions/compat`
- **Date:** 2026-05-14
- **Context:** Unit 8 of `SESSION-rust-port-layer-boundary.md`. With the three-package split locked (D198), `@graphrefly/graphrefly` needs an internal layering. Consolidation-plan introduced `_internal/` (base), per-domain `patterns/<domain>/index.ts` (building blocks), per-domain `patterns/<domain>/presets.ts` (presets). User clarified 2026-05-14: preserve "presets" vocabulary; split "below presets" into two layers (base + utils); add "solutions" on top.
- **Options:** A) 4-layer model `base / utils / presets / solutions / compat`; B) 3-layer model (collapse base + utils); C) status quo (`extra/` + `patterns/_internal/` + `patterns/<domain>/{index,presets}.ts`).
- **Decision:** A — user-locked 2026-05-14.
- **Rationale:** Preserves consolidation-plan's "presets" semantics (opinionated compositions of utils) — single rename "building blocks → utils". `base/` distinguishes domain-agnostic infrastructure from `utils/` domain building blocks. `solutions/` is the new top layer for user-facing packaged products. Layer-placement rubric: "zero domain → base; single-domain primitive returning Node/Graph → utils; ≥3 utils composition → preset; ≥2 presets or full vertical with adapters/storage wiring → solution." Within-layer: free composition. Cross-layer: strictly top-down. CI lint via Biome custom rule (D201). Migration bundled into next-turn implementation slice (Unit 8 Q9.4 = D201).
- **Affects:** Future cleave PR (`packages/graphrefly/` content restructure); Biome custom rule (D201); 4-criterion placement rubric; new factory placement (`actorPool`, `heterogeneousDebate`, `reactiveFactStore`, `taggedContextPool` → all go in `presets/{harness, ai, memory, context}/`).

### D201 — Layer-boundary CI enforcement: Biome custom rule (no extra eslint dep)
- **Date:** 2026-05-14
- **Context:** Unit 8 Q9.2 of `SESSION-rust-port-layer-boundary.md`. 4-layer model (D200) needs CI enforcement to prevent drift. Choice between Biome custom rule vs adding an eslint dependency just for layer-boundary linting.
- **Options:** A) Biome custom rule (this repo already uses Biome); B) add eslint + eslint-plugin-import-boundaries.
- **Decision:** A — user-locked 2026-05-14.
- **Rationale:** Avoid adding an eslint dependency just for one rule. Implementation deferred to the cleave PR.
- **MECHANISM AMENDED 2026-05-15:** Biome 2.x custom rules are GritQL AST-pattern plugins; an import-path-**rank** comparison ("compute layer rank of resolved import, fail if source-rank < target-rank") is not expressible in GritQL. Realized instead as a **zero-dep standalone Node script** `scripts/check-layer-boundary.ts`, wired into `pnpm lint` (`biome check . && tsx scripts/check-layer-boundary.ts`). Preserves D201's actual intent (CI-enforced top-down layering, NO extra eslint dep, single `pnpm lint` entry point) — "Biome custom rule" was the means, not the goal. Includes a **baseline ratchet** (`scripts/layer-boundary-baseline.json`): 23 cleave-introduced violations baselined (deferred to next batch — see `docs/optimizations.md` "Cleave A layer-boundary residuals"); a NEW violation fails CI; a baseline entry that stops firing ALSO fails (shrink-only ratchet). Scoped to shipped source — `src/__tests__/**` exempt (integration tests legitimately cross layers; the A1 doc's "tests too" produced 10 false positives).
- **Affects:** `scripts/check-layer-boundary.ts` + `scripts/layer-boundary-baseline.json` (new); root `package.json` `lint` / `lint:layers`; `pnpm run lint` remains the single lint entry point.

### D202 — Unit 8 Q9.5: `solutions/` = (c) both — top-level barrels + per-vertical multi-preset starter kits
- **Date:** 2026-05-14
- **Context:** Unit 8 Q9.5 of `SESSION-rust-port-layer-boundary.md`. Three candidate interpretations of `solutions/`: (a) curated re-export layer (thin); (b) vertical bundles / starter kits (thick); (c) both.
- **Options:** A) (a) curated re-export only; B) (b) verticals only; C) (c) both.
- **Decision:** C — user-locked 2026-05-14.
- **Rationale:** `solutions/index.ts` (and per-domain `solutions/<domain>/index.ts` barrels) curate headline-product re-exports of presets — the front door users see when they `import { agentLoop, harnessLoop, reactiveFactStore } from "@graphrefly/graphrefly"`. `solutions/<vertical>/` folders hold multi-preset starter kits with adapters + storage tiers + sensible defaults (e.g., `solutions/customer-support-bot/`, `solutions/code-review-agent/`). Verticals add value when composition crosses ≥2 presets AND requires adapter wiring AND requires storage configuration AND the use case is concrete enough for sensible defaults. **Verticals are deferred** until specific use cases land — initial scope (Phase 14.5 / Phase 15) = barrels only; verticals follow consumer pressure.
- **Affects:** Initial scope in next cleave PR = `solutions/index.ts` curated barrel only. Verticals queued behind consumer-pressure signal (Phase 14.5+ candidates).

### D203 — `@graphrefly/native` publish is a milestone-driven slice, EXEMPT from the D196 consumer-pressure gate
- **Date:** 2026-05-15
- **Context:** Cleave A (2026-05-15) confirmed `@graphrefly/graphrefly` peer-depends on a substrate provider, but `@graphrefly/native` is `private: true, version: 0.0.0` — not publishable. A downstream repo wants to consume `@graphrefly/native` and is being forced onto `@graphrefly/pure-ts`. Investigation showed the substrate Rust port (M1–M5) is essentially complete; the gap is napi parity + TS wrapper layer + publish matrix. D196 (consumer-pressure / parity-scenario gating) structurally prevents this from ever being scheduled: its trigger is "a parity scenario needs the binding," but scenarios aren't authored because native doesn't ship, because bindings aren't built — a self-perpetuating deferral with no exit.
- **Options:** A) keep D196 gate, wait for organic parity-scenario pressure (status quo — never resolves the native-publish milestone); B) exempt the native-publish milestone from D196 and schedule it as the next `/porting-to-rs` batch, authoring the gating scenarios *as outputs of* the slice rather than preconditions; C) repeal D196 entirely.
- **Decision:** B — user-locked 2026-05-15. D196 remains the policy for *incremental* napi widening of individual surfaces; it is **carved out** for the bounded native-publish milestone. F18/F20 + the newer-method napi parity + the TS wrapper layer + the publish matrix move from "deferred (parity-gated)" to "queued (next batch)" in `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/migration-status.md` § "NEXT BATCH — Ship `@graphrefly/native`".
- **Rationale:** D196's "scenario IS the receipt" logic is sound for speculative one-off bindings but wrong for a milestone whose entire purpose is to make the native package consumable. The scenario authoring still happens — it's just sequenced *inside* the slice (write the binding + its parity scenario together) instead of waiting for exogenous demand that the gate itself suppresses. Bounded scope (7 enumerated items, no open-ended widening) keeps the "no speculative TSFN-bridging" spirit of D196 intact for everything outside the milestone.
- **Affects:** `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/migration-status.md` (next-batch section rewritten); `~/src/graphrefly-rs/CLAUDE.md` § napi widening policy (exemption note); `/porting-to-rs` next invocation = the native-ship slice; supersedes the F18/F20 "deferred indefinitely" status from D196's operational consequences. M6 (Python/pyo3) still separate, post-1.0.

### D204 — D203 native-ship executes as all three slices in one batch; step-1 doc is stale (already built)
- **Date:** 2026-05-15
- **Context:** `/porting-to-rs` "work on the high-priority blockers" invocation. Phase-1 verification of the bindings crate against the 7-step D203 plan found a doc-vs-reality divergence: D203 step 1 ("napi parity for `pause`/`resume`/`invalidate`/`complete`/`error`/`teardown`/`add_meta_companion`/`set_resubscribable` — never built") is **already built** — `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/index.d.ts` exposes all of them plus `isPaused`/`pauseLockCount`/`holdsPauseLock`. F18 (`ReactiveLog::view`/`scan`/`attach`/`attach_storage`) and F20 (`ReactiveIndex::range_by_primary`) napi bindings confirmed genuinely unbuilt. The proposed decomposition was Slice 1 (F18+F20 napi + scenarios), Slice 2 (full `rustImpl` parity-arm green), Slice 3 (CI publish matrix + flip publishability).
- **Options:** Slicing — A) Slice 1 only; B) Slice 1+2; C) all three. Step-1 — a) audit parity coverage + correct the stale doc; b) audit only; c) skip.
- **Decision:** C + a — user-locked 2026-05-15. Execute all three slices in one batch; fold a parity-coverage audit of the already-built step-1 methods into Slice 1 and correct the `migration-status.md` NEXT BATCH wording so it stops claiming "never built".
- **Rationale:** The downstream consumer needs a *publishable* `@graphrefly/native`, so stopping at Slice 1 or 2 doesn't unblock them — only the full publish path does. Bundling is acceptable because Slice 3 is the terminal step and the milestone is bounded (7 enumerated items, no open-ended widening). Release-eng caveat recorded: the CI/publish *scaffolding* is reversible and will be built, but the actual `npm publish` is a separate human-triggered action — this slice flips `private`/`version` and lands the GH Actions workflow but does not execute a publish.
- **Affects:** `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/structures_bindings.rs` (F18/F20 napi); `packages/parity-tests/{scenarios,impls}` (2 new scenario files + `rust.ts`/`pure-ts.ts` widening + skip sweep); `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/package.json` + CI workflow (Slice 3); `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/migration-status.md` (stale step-1 text corrected, D203 items closed); `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/porting-deferred.md` (F18/F20 moved out of deferred).

### D205 — F20 `rangeByPrimary` is a NEW primitive (exists in neither pure-ts nor Rust core), not a napi-only gap; semantics locked
- **Date:** 2026-05-15
- **Context:** During Slice 1 execution, verification of F20 against actual code found `rangeByPrimary`/`range_by_primary` exists in **neither** `packages/pure-ts/src/extra/data-structures/reactive-index.ts` (surface: has/get/getRow/upsert/upsertMany/delete/deleteMany/clear/toArray/toPrimaryMap) **nor** `crates/graphrefly-structures/src/reactive.rs` `ReactiveIndex` (has/get/upsert/upsert_with/upsert_many/delete/delete_many/clear/to_ordered/to_primary_map). Both `migration-status.md` step 3 and `porting-deferred.md:2834` wrongly framed F20 as "core logic exists, only the napi binding is unbuilt." There is no canonical-spec authority for index range-query semantics (it is a structure convenience method, not a protocol-spec rule), triggering the no-autonomous-decisions rule.
- **Options:** A) defer F20, ship F18 + sweep + CI, correct the doc; B) design + implement F20 full-stack now (pure-ts + Rust core + napi + scenario); C) design-only, defer impl.
- **Decision:** B — user-locked 2026-05-15. Locked semantics: **`rangeByPrimary(start: K, end: K) → V[]`** — returns the values of all rows whose **primary key** sorts within **`[start, end)` (inclusive start, exclusive end)**, in **ascending primary-key order**. No cursor variant. `start >= end` or no matches → empty array. Requires primaries be totally ordered (pure-ts: JS `<`/`>=`; Rust core: `K: Ord` bound on the new method only — does not constrain the `ReactiveIndex<K, V>` type itself). napi/parity arm uses numeric (`i64`) primary keys passed alongside the existing handle so range comparison happens on the user-meaningful key, never on opaque `HandleId` ordering.
- **Rationale:** The downstream consumer needs a publishable native package whose `Impl` surface matches pure-ts; an unimplemented F20 would leave a permanent parity hole. `[start, end)` ascending-by-primary is the least-surprising range convention (matches `Array.prototype.slice`, Rust `Range`, SQL `BETWEEN`-minus-upper). Constraining only the method (not the type) with `K: Ord` keeps `ReactiveIndex` usable with non-ordered primaries elsewhere. Numeric-key marshalling sidesteps the "ordering opaque handles is meaningless" hazard the original `porting-deferred.md` F20 entry flagged.
- **Affects:** `packages/pure-ts/src/extra/data-structures/reactive-index.ts` (`IndexBackend` + `NativeIndexBackend` + `ReactiveIndex` wrapper + bundle iface + barrel); `crates/graphrefly-structures/src/reactive.rs` (`ReactiveIndex::range_by_primary`); `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/structures_bindings.rs` (`BenchReactiveIndex::range_by_primary`); `packages/parity-tests/impls/types.ts` (`ImplReactiveIndex.rangeByPrimary`) + `pure-ts.ts` + `rust.ts`; `scenarios/structures/reactive-index-range.test.ts`; both Rust-port docs (F20 reclassified from "napi-deferred" to "shipped new primitive").

### D206 — Native substrate contract: Option A (publish async preview; pure-ts stays sole sync substrate; D080 deferred) + Option C committed as follow-on slice
- **Date:** 2026-05-15
- **Context:** Cleave-/qa N1's "build the real `@graphrefly/native` wrapper" was found ill-posed: the napi surface is irreducibly async (Core on a tokio blocking pool; sync calls deadlock — D070/D077) while `@graphrefly/graphrefly` consumes pure-ts's **sync** public API pervasively (incl. operator/source authoring + `n.cache`-at-construction). The advertised install-time `overrides` drop-in (Q28 = option (c) / D198) is non-functional; the only coherent path (D080 — async-everywhere public API across all siblings) is itself explicitly deferred near-1.0 and was never reconciled with Q28/D198. Decisive consumer-pressure input: the only concrete consumer (memo:Re) locked `@graphrefly/pure-ts` forever for mobile (Hermes)/web; native is a future, post-M5/DS-14.7-napi, install-time-only, NON-blocking backend swap → zero current pressure for native-as-drop-in (D196). Full 9Q walk: `archive/docs/SESSION-DS-native-substrate-contract.md`.
- **Options:** A) retract drop-in claim; `@graphrefly/native` = published async preview + parity arm; pure-ts stays the sole sync substrate for `@graphrefly/graphrefly`; D080 async-everywhere rebase deferred until consumer pressure. B) execute deferred D080 now (async-everywhere rebase of the entire presentation package + authoring model — huge, premature, regresses the sync "run-and-see" value-prop). C) build a separate hand-written **ergonomic async** `@graphrefly/native` public surface (subpath exports + TS layer over `Bench*` mirroring the async `Impl` contract) for direct async consumers — NOT a pure-ts drop-in; presentation untouched. D) sync-blocking napi bridge — rejected (deadlocks).
- **Decision:** **A + C-as-committed-follow-on — user-locked 2026-05-15.** Q-S1 = Option A: `@graphrefly/native` publishes now as the honest **async preview** (`0.0.1`) of the Rust substrate + remains the parity-validation arm; `@graphrefly/pure-ts` stays the sole working substrate for `@graphrefly/graphrefly`; the D080 async-everywhere presentation rebase (Option B) stays deferred until consumer pressure. **Escalation:** Option C is a **committed follow-on slice** (not now): a hand-written ergonomic async public surface for `@graphrefly/native` (subpath `exports` + TS over the `Bench*` napi classes, mirroring the async `Impl` contract) for direct async-tolerant Node consumers. C is explicitly NOT a `@graphrefly/pure-ts` sync drop-in and does NOT make `@graphrefly/graphrefly` consume native — that remains B/D080 territory, still deferred. Q-S2: the B-vs-keep-C-only decision (i.e. "can `@graphrefly/graphrefly` consume native?") re-opens as its own design→dev-dispatch session when EITHER memo:Re's premium-backend native swap becomes actually-blocking (post-M5 + DS-14.7-napi) OR a concrete consumer files D196 parity-scenario pressure. Q-S3 = this entry (D206). Q-S4: D203 native-publish proceeds, reframed — the "downstream forced onto pure-ts" urgency is acknowledged-inaccurate (memo:Re *chose* pure-ts); publish value = stake the npm name, make the Rust port publicly real, enable early async-native adopters, ready the future backend swap, open the D196 pressure channel.
- **Rationale:** A is lowest-cost, fully reversible, maximal D196/consumer-pressure fit, and makes the docs truthful. Publishing the async preview never required the (infeasible) sync drop-in. C gives async-tolerant consumers a real path and creates the consumer-pressure channel that would later justify B, without paying B's pervasive cost or regressing pure-ts's sync ergonomics (the founding "run-and-see" value-prop) speculatively. B stays deferred precisely because no consumer needs it and the cost/UX-regression is large. D is impossible (documented deadlock).
- **Affects:** `~/src/graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/package.json` (0.0.1 + publishConfig + honest description — landed rs `5424047`); `archive/docs/SESSION-DS-native-substrate-contract.md` (RESOLVED + Option C slice plan); `archive/docs/design-archive-index.jsonl`; `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/migration-status.md`; `docs/optimizations.md`; `CLAUDE.md` (install-time-model §); `src/index.ts` header. Q28/D198's overrides-drop-in is hereby formally **deferred pending D080** (superseded as a "locked working mechanism"). Option C follow-on slice spec: see `SESSION-DS-native-substrate-contract.md` § "Option C — committed follow-on slice plan".

### D207 — Option C `describeNode` native semantics: reuse snapshot/describeReactive path (no new Core method)
- **Date:** 2026-05-15
- **Context:** Option C (D206 committed follow-on) must expose the 5 N1 symbols on the hand-written async `@graphrefly/native` public surface. `describeNode` is one of two N1 symbols with no existing napi binding (the other: `sha256Hex`). Question raised in the porting-to-rs Phase-2 HALT: implement `describeNode` as a purpose-built new `graphrefly-core` sync method, or wrap the existing snapshot/`BenchDescribeReactiveHandle` projection.
- **Options:** A) reuse the existing snapshot / `describeReactive` projection in a thin sync napi fn — no new Core API; B) add a dedicated `describe_node` method to `graphrefly-core` + napi binding (newtype/clippy/tests greenfield for an inspection helper).
- **Decision:** A — user-locked 2026-05-15. `describeNode` on the native surface wraps the existing snapshot/`describeReactive` path; no new `graphrefly-core` public method. Inspection helper, so binding-layer sync-vs-async is a binding concern (per `Impl` `describeNode` is sync).
- **Rationale:** Lowest risk, no greenfield Core surface for an inspection-only helper, matches the existing Rust napi shape and the pure-ts reference arm (`pure-ts.ts` `describeNode → legacy.describeNode(node.inner)`). Avoids constraining a new Core API for a non-dispatcher path.
- **Affects:** `~/src/graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/` (hand-written TS wrapper + a thin sync napi over the existing describe/snapshot handle for `describeNode`; new sync napi for `sha256Hex`); `packages/parity-tests/impls/rust.ts` (consumes shipped wrapper; `as unknown as Impl` → `as Impl`); `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/migration-status.md` (item-8 done-as-async; N1=5 doc correction).

### D208 — Single-threaded substrate: lock-free `None` path via generic `LockCell` seam (Q1=A)
- **Date:** 2026-05-16
- **Context:** `/porting-to-rs` next batch = `SESSION-rust-port-perf-value-investigation.md` §7 (user-locked). §7 wants a default lock-free `&mut`/`RefCell` Core reaching the ~83 ns floor, but `CLAUDE.md` Rust invariant 2 requires every public type `Send + Sync` and invariant 1 forbids `unsafe`. §5b proved an uncontended `parking_lot::Mutex` (~14 ns) does NOT reach the floor, so "keep one Mutex<CoreState>" is not single-threaded-fast. Genuine spec ↔ invariant conflict surfaced in Phase-2 HALT.
- **Options:** A) Core generic over a safe `LockCell` trait — `NoLock`/`RefCell` variant (single-threaded, `!Sync`, acquire monomorphizes out → 83 ns floor) vs `ReentrantMutex` variant (`Send + Sync`, for cross-`SerializationGroupId` cascades + bindings); B) relax invariant 2, `Rc<RefCell>` Core always (`!Send`/`!Sync`); C) single Core type + safe runtime owning-thread guard (thread-id compare on hot path, no true compile-out).
- **Decision:** A — user-approved 2026-05-16 (Claude-recommended). B and C each structurally break the `Option<SerializationGroupId>` cross-thread half of the same user-locked batch (the contract needs `Arc<ReentrantMutex<()>>` cross-thread serialization groups, impossible under `!Send` or thread-confined Core). A is the only option satisfying both halves + `forbid(unsafe)` + §7 compile-out language.
- **Rationale:** Monomorphization + empty-touched-set elision give literal "compile out when all-`None`"; the `LockCell` seam is `RefCell` vs `parking_lot` wrappers — both safe. Locked-variant `CoreState`-access gating (per-group `ReentrantMutex` vs single state mutex) deferred to an impl-detail decision-log entry with bench rationale; affects only the rare locked path, not the floor.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-core` `node.rs` / `batch.rs` / `subgraph.rs` / `lib.rs`; the `LockCell` seam type; M1-dispatcher re-architecture (post-M5).

### D209 — Concurrency-model rewrite delivered as a single monolithic pass (Q2)
- **Date:** 2026-05-16
- **Context:** §7 specifies "one batch, both" (single-threaded substrate + `Option<LockId>`). Phase-2 HALT asked whether to internally sequence as two reviewable sub-slices (S1 rip-out → S2 group contract) or one integrated pass.
- **Options:** A) two sub-slices in one batch (S1 green before S2); B) single monolithic pass.
- **Decision:** B — user-locked 2026-05-16. One integrated rewrite of `node.rs`/`batch.rs`/`subgraph.rs`.
- **Rationale:** User directive. Accepted trade-off: ~10k LOC changed before the suite is green; regression bisection is coarser.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-core` (slice execution shape only).

### D210 — `LockId` stays the pause-lock id; new orthogonal `SerializationGroupId` (Q3, AMENDED 2026-05-16)
- **Date:** 2026-05-16
- **Context:** Initial framing (and the original Q3 options) conflated `graphrefly-core`'s `LockId` with the §7 concurrency lock. **Surfaced as a spec↔plan conflict during implementation:** `LockId` is the spec-mandated *pause-lock* identifier (R1.2.6 / R2.6 — `[PAUSE,lockId]`/`[RESUME,lockId]`, per-node `lockset: HashSet<LockId>`, multi-pauser dispose), exercised by the whole pause/resume suite. The legacy *concurrency* machinery being deleted by §7 is the **union-find/partition/`wave_owner`** subsystem, which never used `LockId`. There is no legacy concurrency-`LockId` to retire; the legacy pause-`LockId` cannot be retired without violating R2.6.
- **Options:** A) keep `LockId` as the pause-lock id (unchanged, no napi `alloc_lock_id` churn) + add a NEW orthogonal `SerializationGroupId(u64)` newtype for the §7 contract; "retire old" = delete the union-find/partition subsystem (the actual legacy). B) literally remove `LockId`, fold pause-locks into `SerializationGroupId` (risks breaking R2.6 + the pause suite).
- **Decision:** A — user-locked 2026-05-16 (supersedes the original B framing of this entry). `LockId`/`alloc_lock_id`/pause `lockset` semantics are **untouched**. New `Node.serialization_group: Option<SerializationGroupId>` axis added; engine maps it to `Arc<ReentrantMutex<()>>`; strict dep-component consistency validated at register/set_lock. The §7 "retire old `LockId`" wording was based on the conflation and does not apply.
- **Rationale:** Preserves canonical spec R1.2.6/R2.6; the two axes (pause-lock protocol vs concurrency serialization group) are genuinely orthogonal. Net: smaller slice (pause subsystem + napi `alloc_lock_id` untouched).
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-core` `handle.rs` (new `SerializationGroupId`, `LockId` unchanged) / `node.rs` (new `serialization_group` field + validation) / `subgraph.rs` (deleted). napi `alloc_lock_id` unchanged. `project_next_porting_batch.md` memory note flags the §7 "retire LockId" wording as conflated.

### D211 — Keep `graphrefly-core` + `graphrefly-bindings-js` compiling; defer full binding/parity rework (Q4)
- **Date:** 2026-05-16
- **Context:** `graphrefly-bindings-js` consumes Core via tokio `spawn_blocking` (D070) and requires `Send`. The concurrency rewrite changes the Core shape. Native package is the async preview (D206).
- **Options:** A) keep both crates compiling (bindings assign a group id → `Send + Sync` variant; no new binding features; full rework deferred + logged); B) graphrefly-core-only, allow bindings-js to break (excluded from default-members anyway).
- **Decision:** A — user-locked 2026-05-16.
- **Rationale:** Preserves the published native async-preview arm and the workspace bindings build without scoping a binding rework into an already-maximal slice.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-bindings-js` (compile-only); `porting-deferred.md` (new deferred entry for the binding/parity rework against the group-id Core); native package stays D206 async preview.

### D212 — D3 union-find SUPERSEDED; §7 commit_emission-collapse deferred (flagged for ratification)
- **Date:** 2026-05-16
- **Context:** §7 single-threaded-substrate + `SerializationGroupId` slice implemented (D208–D211). Two records: (a) the D3 union-find design + D085/D086 are now dead; (b) §7 item (1) also bundled collapsing `commit_emission`'s multi-phase re-lock, which this slice deferred.
- **Options:** (a) supersede D3/D085/D086 vs leave ambiguous; (b) do the commit_emission collapse in-batch vs defer on §5b evidence.
- **Decision:** (a) **D3 / D085 / D086 SUPERSEDED 2026-05-16** — union-find deleted in `graphrefly-rs`; `SESSION-rust-port-d3-per-subgraph-parallelism.md` banner-flagged (body retained as history; spec-owner flagged). (b) `commit_emission` single-pass collapse **DEFERRED** — `porting-deferred.md` §7-A — on the strength of `SESSION-rust-port-perf-value-investigation.md` §5b's own measurement (~0% single-thread benefit; contended-only ~10%). The AskUserQuestion to confirm (b) failed mid-call (stream closed); taken on §5b evidence and **explicitly flagged for user ratification or reversal** (it is the only deviation from the literal "one batch, both" §7 wording; the rest shipped).
- **Rationale:** D3 carried dead semantics that would mislead future readers. The collapse delivers ~0 of §7's measured perf lever while being its riskiest behavioral change; deferring de-risked an already-maximal slice without sacrificing the floor.
- **Affects:** `archive/docs/SESSION-rust-port-d3-per-subgraph-parallelism.md` (SUPERSEDED banner); `~/src/graphrefly-rs` `node.rs`/`batch.rs`/`groups.rs`; `porting-deferred.md` §7-A/B/C/D; `migration-status.md` closing section. **Open for user:** ratify or reverse the §7-A deferral.

### D213 — QA F1: Core-global wave lock restores cross-thread safety for the all-`None` `LockedCell` default
- **Date:** 2026-05-16
- **Context:** /qa adversarial review of the §7 slice. Both review subagents converged: deleting union-find removed the per-partition `wave_owner` that, pre-rewrite, serialized waves per connected component even for an *unannotated* graph. Post-rewrite an all-`None` `Core<LockedCell>` (the `Send+Sync` default every downstream crate + napi uses per D211) acquires ZERO wave locks → two threads interleave waves with no protection for the per-thread `WAVE_STATE`/`TIER3_EMITTED_THIS_WAVE`/`IN_TICK_OWNED` invariants. Not covered by any porting-deferred entry; contradicts §7's "no runtime race possible" (which only addressed *mixed* components). Deleted `per_subgraph_parallelism.rs`/gutted `lock_released.rs` is why 825 green tests missed it.
- **Options:** A) Core-global wave `ReentrantMutex` acquired only on `LockedCell` when the touched-group set is empty; B) fail-loud panic if `LockedCell` driven >1 thread with no groups; C) ship as-is + document the config unsupported (silent corruption).
- **Decision:** **Option A** (user-approved). `StateCell::SERIALIZE_WAVES` assoc-const (`false` `SingleThreadCell` → branch dead-code-eliminates, §7 ~83 ns floor untouched; `true` `LockedCell`). `Core::global_wave: Arc<ReentrantMutex<()>>`; `with_global_wave_fallback` pushes it when groups empty. Grouped waves still acquire only disjoint group locks (parallelism preserved).
- **Rationale:** User: "the multithreaded default must have at least one lock to protect the nodes queue." §7's perf floor is explicitly `SingleThreadCell`; `LockedCell` is the *safe* thread substrate and must serialize. Perf cost: floor 0 (DCE); `LockedCell` ~1 uncontended ReentrantMutex/wave (~1–3%, bench noise); all-`None` multi-thread loses only parallelism §4/§5b measured net-negative.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-rs` `state_cell.rs`, `node.rs` (`Core`/`WeakCore`/ctor/clone/weak_handle/acquire_*); `tests/group_parallelism.rs` (F4 regression test); CLAUDE.md Rust-invariant note candidate.

### D214 — QA F2 + point-3: ONE unified deps+children+meta component guard; `set_serialization_group` is component-wide retroactive regroup
- **Date:** 2026-05-16
- **Context:** /qa found meta-companion edges bypassed the strict invariant entirely (`add_meta_companion` did no group check; `walk_undirected_dep_graph` walked deps+children but NOT meta) while the wave cascade DOES walk meta — so the invariant's "component" ≠ the cascade's "component", breaking the "no runtime race" guarantee's premise. User also asked to allow retroactively setting the group after `set_deps`/mount/unmount topology changes.
- **Options:** unify the component definition vs patch endpoints piecemeal; per-node vs component-wide `set_serialization_group`.
- **Decision:** (user: "use one guard for all deps+children+meta" + "allow retrospectively set"). (1) `walk_undirected_dep_graph` now traverses meta both directions (reverse-meta index built once, declare-time only); single `component_is_group_consistent` helper reused by `register`, `add_meta_companion` (panic on mix, matches its assert-contract), and as the soundness basis for `set_deps`'s endpoint check. (2) `set_serialization_group` redefined to assign the group to the node's **entire** unified component atomically → the retroactive-regroup primitive; consistent by construction so `SetGroupError::ComponentInconsistent` is now unreachable (retained, doc-noted).
- **Rationale:** A single component relation across every topology-mutation entry point + the cascade is the only way the strict invariant's "no runtime race" guarantee actually holds. Per-node set could never legally transition all-`None`→all-`Some` (chicken-and-egg); component-wide is the only useful semantics under the invariant.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-rs` `node.rs` (`walk_undirected_dep_graph`, `component_is_group_consistent`, `register`, `set_deps` rationale, `add_meta_companion`, `set_serialization_group`, `SetGroupError` doc); `tests/serialization_groups.rs` (component-wide + meta tests). QA F5/F6/F7 → `porting-deferred.md` §7-B (strengthened to deadlock-potential)/§7-E/§7-F.

### D215 — Rust test-loop speedup: nextest + per-worktree target isolation
- **Date:** 2026-05-16
- **Context:** Dev felt "seriously hindered" by a long-running Rust test suite. Measured: TS suites are fine (~16s total). Root cause was NOT test duration — a parallel session's `cargo test --no-fail-fast` deadlocked in the in-flight §7 serialization-group cross-thread tests and held the cargo build-directory lock for ~1h45m at 0.1% CPU, serialising every other session behind it. Secondary: 27 separate graphrefly-core integration-test binaries (cargo runs them binary-by-binary), 57GB `target/`, no nextest/sccache/alt-linker.
- **Options:** A) leave hung session, infra speedup only  B) kill hung run + investigate the deadlock  C) consolidate the 27 test binaries into one harness now
- **Decision:** A + implement B(isolation)+C(nextest)+E(config); deliverable D (binary consolidation) PREPARED but DEFERRED — surfaced as a conflict (it mass-edits the same `tests/*.rs` files the parallel session has uncommitted add/delete changes on; landing it now guarantees a merge collision).
- **Rationale:** The parallel-session-blocks-everything pain is fully addressed by per-worktree `CARGO_TARGET_DIR` (sessions never share a cargo lock) + nextest `slow-timeout`+terminate (a hung test is killed after 3min, never wedges the suite/machine again). nextest also gives true cross-binary parallelism, so D's value is now mostly compile-time only and not worth a guaranteed merge conflict with active work.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-rs` new `.config/nextest.toml`, `.cargo/config.toml` (`cargo t`/`tc` aliases), `scripts/dev-test.sh`; `CLAUDE.md` test-loop docs; `porting-deferred.md` (D as deferred infra item). No `crates/` source touched.

### D216 — §7 perf-verification bench slice scope (floor + parallel-scaling benches; §7-A decided post-data)
- **Date:** 2026-05-16
- **Context:** §7 concurrency rewrite (D208–D215) shipped but the perf thesis ("~83 ns / ~7.6× floor") was only measured on the hand-written `benches/minimal_handle_core.rs` lean mirror — the *real shipped* `Core<SingleThreadCell>` / `Core<LockedCell>` were never benched. `group_parallelism.rs` asserts no-deadlock+delivery only (would pass even if disjoint groups fully serialized). User-locked next batch (`project_next_porting_batch.md`): floor bench + parallel-scaling bench + §7-A `commit_emission`-collapse ratification.
- **Options (HALT):** §7-A: A) decide after bench data B) ratify deferral C) reverse in-batch. Floor bench: new file vs extend dispatcher.rs. Parallel bench: criterion iter_custom vs example vs both. §7-C cleanup: standalone vs fold-in.
- **Decision (user, 2026-05-16):** (1) **§7-A → decide after bench data** — this slice lands floor + parallel benches first; the §7-A ratify/reverse call is made at slice close using the actual measured contended-regime number this slice's harness produces (the bench is the instrument for the decision). Slice body stays pure measurement. (2) **Floor bench → new `benches/floor_compare.rs`** measuring the *real shipped* `Core<C>` for **both** monomorphizations (`SingleThreadCell` = §7 floor; `LockedCell` = production default per D211) — explicitly NOT the `minimal_handle_core` mirror (user: "I want the real one we use in production — that's accurate"). `dispatcher.rs` (real LockedCell production-default harness) stays untouched. (3) **Parallel-scaling → criterion `iter_custom`** N-thread disjoint-`SerializationGroupId` throughput + same-group / all-`None`-global-wave serialized controls. (4) **§7-C/§7-F cleanup → fold in if cheap**, else back out and keep standalone (assessed during impl).
- **Rationale:** "Real production Core" = the genuine shipped `Core<C>` types, not a synthetic mirror; benching both cells side-by-side is the honest measure of where the real floor lands (expected between the 83 ns mirror and 634 ns old production — it still carries mandatory floor machinery the mirror omitted). Deciding §7-A on this slice's own data is strictly more evidence-driven than ratifying blind.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-rs` new `crates/graphrefly-core/benches/floor_compare.rs` + `Cargo.toml` `[[bench]]`; new parallel-scaling bench; possibly `graphrefly-operators` (§7-C if cheap); `migration-status.md` §7 section (measured floor table); `porting-deferred.md` §7-A (resolved per post-data decision). No Core logic change unless §7-A reversed.
- **Follow-on (2026-05-16):** Measured clean/warm: legacy `cargo test -p graphrefly-core` 13.88s vs nextest 16.9s — nextest is NOT faster; the suite is bound by 4 `cascade_depth` 5000-node stack-safety stress tests (~13.6s each ≈ 95% of wall), not parallelism (already saturated). Added nextest `default-filter = "not binary(cascade_depth)"` to `[profile.default]` (+ explicit `all()` in `ci`/new `stress` profiles): inner loop now 304 tests in **0.5s** (~2.4s wall) vs ~14s; stack-safety guards still gated via `cargo tc` / `--profile stress` / CI. The infra slice's real value remains isolation + hang-kill, NOT raw speed. Also surfaced (other session's code, not fixed): `f1ba003` `tests/sink_snapshot.rs:211` uses `pending_batch_count` (`#[cfg(any(test, debug_assertions))]` at `node.rs:2415`) → suite does not compile under `--release`, blocking the release-build speedup for cascade tests.

### D216 — OUTCOME (2026-05-16): §7 perf thesis empirically REFUTED on both axes
- **Bench result (criterion `--quick`, real shipped `Core<C>`):**
  - **Floor:** real `Core<SingleThreadCell>` identity-dedup ≈ **627 ns** ≈ old pre-§7 production (**634 ns**); `Core<LockedCell>` ≈ 652 ns. The §7 rewrite bought **~4%** on the dedup hot path (~4–17% on chain/diamond/fanout) — **NOT the predicted ~7.6×**. The 83 ns / 7.6× belongs to the lean `minimal_handle_core` *mirror* only (no `CoreState` HashMap / `Arc` / refcount / `BatchGuard` / multi-phase commit — none of which §7 touched). `RefCell` ≈ `Mutex` (~25 ns delta) ⇒ **the lock is not the cost**; the per-emit machinery under it is.
  - **Parallel:** disjoint `SerializationGroupId` aggregate throughput **regresses** with thread count (1.09→0.34 Melem/s, 1→8t) and is **indistinguishable from the serialized `same_group`/`all_none` controls**. `LockedCell` wraps the *entire* `CoreState` in one mutex; the per-group `ReentrantMutex` sits *on top* ⇒ adds overhead, never unlocks parallelism. Independently reproduces §5's prior finding.
- **Resolution (user-directed, 2026-05-16):** the refutation separates two problems §7 conflated → **Slice A** (dispatcher data-structure floor rewrite: slab/slotmap node store, kill per-emit HashMap, shrink refcount churn, single-pass commit; target <150 ns; threading-independent) and **Slice B** (group-owned-shard parallelism: `SerializationGroupId` *owns* an independent `CoreState` sub-store, all-`None`→one default shard = zero regression; replaces the proven-worthless "lock on top of global mutex"). **§7-A folds into Slice A** (single-pass commit is part of that holistic rewrite, done for a measured target under fresh coverage — NOT standalone for ~0). **§7-C/§7-F fold into Slice B** (B rewrites that exact group/lock layer ⇒ the vestigial union-find deletion is free there, not standalone 8-file churn). **Routing: full design session FIRST** (A-then-B order — parallelizing 627 ns work is pointless; fix the floor, then shard) — no redesign code until the session locks scope.
- **§7-A final disposition:** NOT done standalone (bench-confirmed ~0 value for §7's riskiest behavioral change); NOT deferred-forever — **absorbed into Slice A**, scoped by the design session. Removed from the "flagged for ratification" state.
- **Affects:** `migration-status.md` § "§7 perf-verification" (refutation + tables + A/B); `porting-deferred.md` §7-A (re-dispositioned → Slice A) / §7-C / §7-F (→ Slice B); memory `project_next_porting_batch.md` (batch CLOSED; next = design session) + `project_rust_perf_value_investigation.md` (refutation recorded). Benches `floor_compare.rs` + `group_scaling.rs` retained as the regression instruments for Slices A/B.
- **Resolved (2026-05-16):** The `sink_snapshot.rs` / `pending_batch_count` `--release` compile blocker is FIXED. `Core::pending_batch_count` (node.rs) changed from `#[cfg(any(test, debug_assertions))]` to unconditional `pub` + `#[doc(hidden)]` (integration tests are a separate crate → no `cfg(test)`/`debug_assertions` on the lib under `--release`; `#[doc(hidden)]` keeps it off the public surface per spec §5.12). Verified: full `graphrefly-core` test suite compiles under `--release`; cascade_depth stress tests drop from ~13.6s → **~0.98s each** (~14×) optimized. All GitHub Actions test runs now use `cargo nextest run --profile ci` (only `graphrefly-rs/.github/workflows/ci.yml` ran tests; ts workflows + rs release/native workflows run none). Operational docs + both `.claude/skills` swept to nextest-first; loom (`--cfg loom`) + append-only historical records intentionally left.

### D217 — Slice A = A2 whole: staged bench-gated holistic floor rewrite (<150 ns target)
- **Date:** 2026-05-16
- **Context:** D216 refuted the §7 floor thesis — real `Core<C>` ≈ 627 ns ≈ old prod; the ~7.6× gap vs the 83 ns mirror is data-structure machinery (HashMap node store, separate children HashMap, refcount churn, wave thread-local, multi-phase commit), not algorithm. Design session (design-review Q5–Q9).
- **Options:** A1 incremental (slab store only) / A2 staged holistic (all levers, bench-gated) / A3 promote the mirror.
- **Decision (user):** **A2 whole.** Staged, `floor_compare.rs`-gated after each lever, stop-early once <150 ns: (1) slab/slotmap node store [land first, biggest lever] (2) colocated `SmallVec` children on `NodeRecord` (3) kill the wave thread-local (pass `&mut WaveState`) (4) batch refcount + binding refcount-free opt-out (5) **§7-A single-pass `commit_emission` rides LAST** under the parity arm. A3 rejected (mirror omits ~half the protocol; re-adding = rebuilding today's Core).
- **Rationale:** the mirror is the existence proof of the 83 ns endpoint; the gap is representation. Bench-gating each lever means you stop at the first lever set that clears the user's <150 ns bar instead of speculatively doing all five. §7-A is §7's riskiest behavioral change for ~0 standalone value (§5b/D216) — only safe as the last step of a holistic rewrite under fresh coverage.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-rs` `crates/graphrefly-core/src/{node,batch,state_cell}.rs`; `porting-deferred.md` §7-A (absorbed here); `benches/floor_compare.rs` (the gate). Public API unchanged (representation swap).

### D218 — Slice B = B4: per-shard mutex core + owner-thread overlay as M6 binding-affinity layer
- **Date:** 2026-05-16
- **Context:** D216 showed disjoint `SerializationGroupId` groups don't parallelize — `LockedCell` is ONE `Mutex<CoreState>`, the per-group `ReentrantMutex` is pure overhead on top. User pre-seeded a single-writer-per-shard (OS-thread pool + crossbeam-channel) model. Design-review Q6 surfaced the deciding invariant: owner-threads' real justification is **binding-thread affinity** (napi V8 = one isolate/thread; pyo3 GIL), NOT Rust parallelism.
- **Options:** B1 pure single-writer (reject — channel round-trip breaks the all-`None` floor) / B2 per-shard mutex / B3 owner-thread+channel foundation / B4 = B2 core + B3 as opt-in M6 overlay.
- **Decision (user):** **B4.** B2 (`shards: HashMap<ShardId, Mutex<ShardState>>`, one default shard for all-`None` = zero regression = Slice A floor; disjoint shards = disjoint mutexes = true parallelism) is the substrate model, built now with minimal machinery. B3 (owner OS thread + crossbeam-channel per shard, same-thread fast path) becomes an **additive opt-in overlay the napi/pyo3 bindings adopt at M6** for V8/GIL thread-affinity — consumer-pressure-gated (D196), not built until M6. §7-C/§7-F fold into B2 (it rewrites that layer). Async/goroutine-scale explicitly rejected (handful of static domains, no function-coloring).
- **Rationale:** per-shard mutex delivers the measured win (parallelism + floor) with far less machinery than owner-threads+channels; B3's machinery is only load-bearing for the binding milestone, so it's the right answer *there*, the wrong amount of machinery for the substrate win available now. B4 preserves the user's model exactly where it's justified without paying its cost prematurely.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-rs` `crates/graphrefly-core/src/{state_cell,batch,node}.rs` (shard model replaces `LockedCell`); `crates/graphrefly-operators/*` + core vestigial symbols (§7-C/§7-F deleted as a side-effect); `crates/graphrefly-bindings-{js,py}` (B3 overlay at M6); `benches/group_scaling.rs` (the gate); `porting-deferred.md` §7-B (cross-shard ordering guard to spec in Slice B) / §7-C / §7-F.

### D219 — Order: A then B; B's shard-trait + B3-overlay seam designed during Slice A
- **Date:** 2026-05-16
- **Context:** Slices A (floor) and B (parallelism) are independent; parallelizing 627 ns work is pointless. But B's per-shard model needs A's representation to slot in cleanly, and B3's overlay needs a trait seam that is cheap to design up front / expensive to retrofit.
- **Options:** A fully then B / A then B but lock B's shard-trait design now / interleave.
- **Decision (user):** **A then B, with B's shard-trait + B3-overlay seam designed during Slice A.** Slice A lands to <150 ns first; the `trait Shard` / `ShardState`-ownership / wave→shard-routing seam is sketched alongside A so A's slab/children/wave-state work is shaped per-shard-ready (B2 impls the trait as `Mutex<ShardState>`+inline; B3 later as owner-thread+channel — same trait, no caller change).
- **Rationale:** keeps the two slices' implementation order clean (measure the floor before sharding it) while front-loading the only B decision that's expensive to defer (the trait seam). Avoids interleave context-switching.
- **Affects:** Slice A implementation shape (`graphrefly-core` representation work is shard-aware); the Slice B design pass (trait already locked); `SESSION-rust-port-concurrency-redesign.md`.

### D217-AMEND — Slice A lever ranking FALSIFIED (verify-before-greenfield); step 1 = empirical attribution
- **Date:** 2026-05-16
- **Context:** Pre-implementation premise check (memory `feedback_verify_premise_before_greenfield`) found the 83 ns lean mirror (`benches/minimal_handle_core.rs:97-98`) uses `nodes: HashMap<NodeId,Rec>` + `children: HashMap` — the SAME structures as production `CoreState`, with the *slower* `std::collections::HashMap` (SipHash) vs production's `ahash`, and is 7.6× faster anyway. This **refutes D217 levers #1 (slab store "biggest lever") + #2 (colocated children)** — the node store is not a lever.
- **Options:** A) empirical attribution profile first, re-lock levers from data B) re-reason the ranking and start on the wave thread-local C) re-open the whole design session.
- **Decision (user):** **A.** Slice A step 1 = profile the real `Core<SingleThreadCell>` emit path (`examples/profile_st_emit.rs` + macOS `sample`/`samply`, the established repo pattern) to **empirically attribute** the 627→83 ns gap, THEN re-lock the lever set from data. Do not repeat D217's own unmeasured-assumption failure (the very mistake that killed the §7 thesis).
- **Rationale:** the mirror omits dyn `BindingBoundary` FFI, the `WaveState`/`IN_TICK_OWNED` `thread_local!` (vs `&mut self` fields), `BatchGuard`+group-collect+global-wave lock, and multi-phase commit — but *which* dominates is unmeasured. D217 ranked levers against an unverified mirror premise; the disciplined fix is attribution-before-selection, consistent with the session's measure-don't-assume ethos.
- **Affects:** D217 lever order VOID pending the attribution profile; `SESSION-rust-port-concurrency-redesign.md` Slice A section (amend); new `crates/graphrefly-core/examples/profile_st_emit.rs`; the re-locked lever set lands as D217-AMEND-2 after the profile.

### D217-AMEND-2 — Slice A bounded alloc-elimination: `pending_notify` recycle landed (627→515 ns, ~18%); no 80/20 lever; Slice A capped
- **Date:** 2026-05-16
- **Context:** D217-AMEND locked "empirical attribution first." Profiled the real `Core<SingleThreadCell>` dedup hot path (`crates/graphrefly-core/examples/profile_st_emit.rs` + macOS `sample`). Finding 1: the dominant single frame was per-wave `std::mem::take(&mut ws.pending_notify)` (~1250/4767 samples) — a fresh `IndexMap::default()` (new `ahash::RandomState` + RawVec realloc) every wave. **D217 lever-1 ("slab store, biggest lever") falsified** — the 83 ns mirror uses the *same* HashMap node store (slower `std` SipHash); `require_node` was only ~261 samples, `RefCell::borrow_mut` ≈ 0.
- **Decision (user, bounded alloc-elimination, no <150 ns target):** recycle `pending_notify` via a persistent `pending_notify_recycle` spare (`mem::swap` + `.clear()`; zero `IndexMap::default()` after thread init). Leave protocol bookkeeping (`tier3_*`, `in_tick`, refcount) untouched.
- **Outcome (clean 100-sample release bench):** real `Core<SingleThreadCell>` identity-dedup **627 → 515 ns (~18%)**; `Core<LockedCell>` **652 → 579 ns (~11%)**. 304/304 green; clippy/fmt clean; `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]` intact. (`--quick` runs were noise — corrected.)
- **Finding 2 (decisive, structural):** the post-fix self-time profile shows the *remaining* 7.6× is **uniformly-distributed full-protocol machinery with no 80/20 lever** — ~⅓ allocator churn, ~⅓ per-wave structure construct/destruct, ~⅓ protocol bookkeeping (`tier3_*`/`in_tick`/`clear_wave_state`/`payload_handle`/`is_state`), no single symbol >~6% of the gap. Empirically confirms + generalizes §5b ("the tax is the aggregate, not any one acquisition"). The other `mem::take`-per-wave hash containers (`wave_cache_snapshots`, `pending_auto_resolve`) **early-out empty on the dedup hot path** → no further bounded alloc win without entering protocol bookkeeping (scoped out) or a ground-up mirror-shaped rewrite (the A3 the design session rejected). The 83 ns mirror is fast because it implements a strict *subset* of the protocol (does less), not because it is better-structured — it cannot be reached by incremental shaving.
- **Slice A status:** **CAPPED at the bounded win.** `<150 ns` is unreachable incrementally (proven). Net: §7 union-find deletion ≈4% + this recycle ≈18% is the realizable single-thread improvement; deeper requires a rewrite (out of scope) or accepting ~515 ns as structural to the full-protocol dispatcher (consistent with the memory's "Rust perf is the secondary, workload-gated claim; primary value = safety + canonical impl"). Next: pivot to Slice B (D218/D219) — per-shard parallelism is a throughput win independent of the single-thread floor.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-rs` `crates/graphrefly-core/src/batch.rs` (`WaveState.pending_notify_recycle` + `flush_notifications` recycle), `examples/profile_st_emit.rs` (retained attribution harness); `SESSION-rust-port-concurrency-redesign.md` Slice A; `migration-status.md`; memory `project_next_porting_batch.md`. Supersedes D217's lever ordering entirely.

### D217-AMEND-2 /qa addendum — panic-path-asymmetry fix (converged finding)
- **Date:** 2026-05-16
- **Context:** `/qa` adversarial pass on the landed `pending_notify_recycle` change. Two parallel review subagents (Blind Hunter + Edge Case Hunter) **converged** on one finding: `pending_notify_recycle` was the first/only retain-capable `WaveState` field lacking (a) a panic-path drain in `discard_wave_cleanup` and (b) a `wave_state_clear_outermost` `debug_assert!` tripwire — breaking the uniform "every retain field released on the abort path + asserted empty at outermost-wave-start" invariant the dispatcher deliberately maintains.
- **Calibrated severity:** **minor / latent** — not reachable today (every op between the swap and `.clear()` is infallible; Rust alloc-failure aborts not unwinds; the handle-leak-on-panic-mid-flush was *pre-existing*, not a regression — the old `mem::take`-at-top shape leaked identically). The genuinely-new hazard (persistent slot survives unwind → stale-map injected into next wave) is only reachable if a future fallible call is added in that window. Net: a real defense-in-depth + future-footgun regression worth closing, not a live bug.
- **Decision (user-approved):** apply the fix (auto-applicable, mirrors the existing `pending_notify` pattern verbatim, zero success-path behavior change): symmetric `mem::take` + lock-released `release_handle` drain of `pending_notify_recycle` in `discard_wave_cleanup`; `debug_assert!(pending_notify_recycle.is_empty())` in `wave_state_clear_outermost`. Strictly improves on the pre-existing leak and converts a silent future-footgun into a loud test failure.
- **Verification:** `cargo nextest run --profile ci -p graphrefly-core` 308/308 (incl. cascade_depth stress); workspace 825/825; clippy clean; fmt clean; `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]` preserved; zero new `unsafe`. Bench/harness files reviewed clean (two benign measurement-asymmetry nits accepted — symmetric across arms).
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-rs` `crates/graphrefly-core/src/batch.rs` (`discard_wave_cleanup` symmetric recycle drain + `wave_state_clear_outermost` assert); `migration-status.md` § "Slice A floor work" /qa subsection. No new `porting-deferred.md` entry (finding fixed in-slice, nothing deferred).

### D220 — Slice B internal decomposition: seam-first (B-1 landed); B-2 = the multi-session partition; B-3 = guard+cleanup
- **Date:** 2026-05-16
- **Context:** User approved full staged Slice B (D218=B4 / D219). Concrete blast radius measured: ~104 `lock_state()`/`state.lock()` sites + the `CoreState` field partition + `StateCell` seam reshape + `BatchGuard`/`begin_batch_for` interplay across ~6000 lines of `node.rs`+`batch.rs`, full 825-test + every-protocol-invariant regression surface.
- **Decision:** internal decomposition is **seam-first** (lowest risk, reviewable): **B-1** = introduce the D219 closure-shaped shard-access seam `Core::with_shard(key, |s| …)` over the *existing single* `CoreState` (single shard, `key` ignored, `f(&mut self.lock_state())`) — near-zero churn, behaviour-identical, `#[allow(dead_code)]` until B-2 wires it. **B-2** = partition `CoreState` → `CoreShared` (id counters, `binding`, `topology_sinks`, `currently_firing` [cross-shard-visible per /qa F2/D214], caps) + per-`Option<SerializationGroupId>` `ShardState` (that group's `nodes`/`children`; `None`=`DEFAULT_SHARD`); reshape `StateCell` to hold a shard map + shared; migrate the ~104 sites onto `with_shard(group_of(node))`; `begin_batch_for(seed)` locks the seed's shard + cross-shard-touched in ascending key order (replaces the ReentrantMutex-on-top + `global_wave`). **B-3** = §7-B bounded cross-shard ordered-acquire guard + §7-C/§7-F vestigial union-find deletion.
- **Status:** **B-1 LANDED + GREEN** 2026-05-16 (`crates/graphrefly-core/src/node.rs` `Core::with_shard`; build clean, clippy 0, `cargo nextest run --profile ci` workspace **825/825** incl. cascade_depth, fmt clean, `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]` preserved, zero new `unsafe`). **B-2 is the multi-session heavy lift — deliberately NOT started at the tail of a long session** (a rushed 104-site struct-split is the exact unmeasured-big-move failure mode this session's §7/D217 arc proved costly; "file-by-file cadence for multi-file rewrites" applies). B-2 should begin with a fresh context budget against the now-stable B-1 seam.
- **Rationale:** seam-first makes B-2 a re-impl of one method + a compiler-guided call-site migration against a stable, behaviour-gated abstraction — not an abstraction invented mid-rewrite. Honest checkpointing at a green milestone > a large half-verified diff.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-rs` `crates/graphrefly-core/src/node.rs` (B-1: `Core::with_shard`); B-2/B-3 affect `node.rs`+`batch.rs`+`state_cell.rs`+`groups.rs`+`handle.rs`. `migration-status.md` § Slice B; memory `project_next_porting_batch.md`.

### D220-EXEC — B-2 turnkey execution design (banked for fresh-session pickup)
- **Date:** 2026-05-16
- **Flag raised:** B-2 (the CoreState partition + ~104-site seam migration) cannot be completed *correctly and fully gated* in the B-1 session's remaining budget; partial unverified progress on the port's highest-risk change is net-negative vs the clean landed B-1 checkpoint. Banked here for a fresh-budget session.
- **Step 1 — `CoreShared` extraction (behaviour-identical, ONE lock, 825-gated):** group these **9 fields** out of `CoreState` into `pub(crate) struct CoreShared { … }` and replace them with `pub(crate) shared: CoreShared` (single sub-struct, SAME single cell/lock → behaviour-identical): `next_node_id`, `next_subscription_id`, `next_lock_id`, `next_topology_id`, `topology_sinks`, `currently_firing`, `pause_buffer_cap`, `max_batch_drain_iterations`, `pending_scratch_release`. Fix `Core::new_with_cell` ctor (node.rs ~1979), `impl Drop for CoreState` (node.rs:5574 — verify if it touches any moved field), and the **23 access sites** (mechanical `s.<f>` → `s.shared.<f>`): batch.rs:713,731,732,953,2822; topology.rs:49,88,89,90,103; node.rs:799,2487,2581,2662,2663,3642,5081,5465,5466,5471,5472,5515,5662. Gate `cargo nextest run --profile ci` workspace 825.
  - **STATUS: LANDED + GREEN 2026-05-16** (graphrefly-rs `918c28c`, on `f1acf39 fix: B-1`). All 23 sites + ctor + `Drop` migrated exactly as enumerated (`binding` correctly left on `CoreState` — not in the 9). Gate via the newly-landed `scripts/gate.sh` (full): rustfmt clean, clippy default-members --all-targets clean, `cargo nextest run --profile ci` **825/825, 0 skipped** (incl. cascade_depth); zero new `unsafe`. **Process note:** the session lost ~2 h to a self-inflicted overlapping-cargo / broad-`pkill` swap-thrash (misdiagnosed serially as memory exhaustion then deadlock — it was neither; `--list` probes were being SIGKILLed by my own concurrent teardowns). Root-caused + fixed by the spawned `scripts/gate.sh` sanctioned runner (mutex + process-group teardown + RAM precheck + direct log); undisturbed gate runs in 75 s. Memory: `feedback_no_chained_background_cargo.md`.
- **Step 2 — shard the cell + route (parallelism, gate group_scaling+floor_compare+825):** `ShardKey = Option<SerializationGroupId>` (`None`=`DEFAULT_SHARD`). Reshape `StateCell` from `from_state(CoreState)/lock()->Guard<CoreState>` to a cell holding `shared` + a shard map. **Guard-lifetime crux (the technical risk, has a clean safe answer — NOT a flag):** per-shard `Arc<parking_lot::Mutex<CoreState>>`; `with_shard(key,f)` briefly locks the map mutex to `Arc::clone` the shard's `Arc<Mutex<CoreState>>`, drops the map lock, then `Mutex::lock_arc` → `ArcMutexGuard` (owned, `'static`, no borrow tied to the map; needs parking_lot `arc_lock` feature — verify Cargo). `SingleThreadCell` stays one `RefCell<CoreState>` (single shard, floor preserved, `key` ignored). Migrate the ~104 `lock_state()` sites → `with_shard(group_of(node), |s| …)` (78 nodes/children) / `with_shared(|sh| …)` (23 shared) / both. **Lock-ordering rule (deadlock-free):** when both needed, **shard guard OUTER, shared guard INNER, brief, never reverse**; pure-shared ops (id alloc, topology) take only shared. `begin_batch_for(seed)`: lock seed's shard + cross-shard-touched in **ascending `ShardKey` order** (replaces ReentrantMutex-on-top + `global_wave`; `global_wave`/`group_locks`/`SERIALIZE_WAVES` become vestigial → fold into B-3's §7-C deletion). `currently_firing` stays in `CoreShared` (cross-shard-visible — /qa F2/D214 P13 check).
- **Step 2 — BANKED 2a/2b decomposition (designed in full; structural reshape attempted 2026-05-16 then REVERTED to the green Step-1 checkpoint — see STATUS below).** Split Step 2 into two independently-gateable sub-stages:
  - **2a — behaviour-identical, 825-gated (the structural reshape + ~104-site migration, ZERO concurrency change).** Hoist `CoreShared` to its own region but keep **exactly one shard** (`key` ignored) so 825 stays green + floor preserved. Concretely:
    - `state_cell.rs`: replace the GAT-guard trait (`type Guard<'a>: DerefMut<Target=CoreState>` / `fn lock()` / `fn from_state(CoreState)`) with the **closure seam** (B3-overlay shape, D219): `pub type ShardKey = Option<SerializationGroupId>`; `trait StateCell { const SERIALIZE_WAVES: bool; fn from_parts(shared: CoreShared, default_shard: CoreState) -> Self; fn with_shared<R>(&self, f: impl FnOnce(&mut CoreShared)->R)->R; fn with_shard<R>(&self, key: ShardKey, f: impl FnOnce(&mut CoreState)->R)->R; }`. `SingleThreadCell { shared: RefCell<CoreShared>, shard: RefCell<CoreState> }`; `LockedCell { shared: parking_lot::Mutex<CoreShared>, shard: parking_lot::Mutex<CoreState> }` (2a: one shard mutex; 2b swaps `shard` for the per-`ShardKey` `Mutex<HashMap<ShardKey, Arc<Mutex<CoreState>>>>` + `lock_arc`).
    - `node.rs`: `CoreShared` gains `pub(crate) binding: Arc<dyn BindingBoundary>` + `impl Drop for CoreShared` that drains `pending_scratch_release` (moved verbatim from the tail of `Drop for CoreState`, which can no longer reach it once `shared` is hoisted). Remove the `shared: CoreShared` field from `CoreState` (→ `CoreState { nodes, children, binding }`). Ctor `new_with_cell`: `C::from_state(CoreState{…shared:CoreShared{…},binding})` → `C::from_parts(CoreShared{…, binding: binding.clone()}, CoreState{ nodes, children, binding: binding.clone() })`. Delete `lock_state()`; `Core::with_shard` → `self.state.with_shard(key,f)`; add `Core::with_shared` → `self.state.with_shared(f)`.
    - **The bulk / highest-risk:** migrate the **~101 `lock_state()` callers + 23 `s.shared.<f>` + 4 direct `Weak→state.lock()`** (topology.rs:48,102; node.rs:579,701) onto closures. In 2a pass `key = None` everywhere (single shard ⇒ behaviour-identical). Shard-only body → `with_shard(None,|s|{…})`; shared-only → `with_shared(|sh|{…})`; **both** → nest `with_shared` INSIDE the `with_shard` closure (shard OUTER, shared INNER, held together — preserves the old single-lock atomicity; this nesting is what makes 2b's split atomicity-safe). The invasive part is batch.rs's `let mut s=lock_state(); …; drop(s); <binding callback>; re-lock` control flow → must restructure into closure form (NOT a mechanical rename). File-by-file cadence; `mise run gate:core` between files, `mise run gate` (full 825) at the 2a boundary; checkpoint-commit when green.
  - **2b — parallelism, gate group_scaling + floor_compare + 825.** Swap `LockedCell.shard` for the per-`ShardKey` `Mutex<HashMap<ShardKey, Arc<parking_lot::Mutex<CoreState>>>>`; `with_shard(key,f)` = brief map-lock → `Arc::clone` shard → drop map-lock → `Mutex::lock_arc` → `ArcMutexGuard` (owned `'static`; `arc_lock` feature already on, workspace Cargo.toml:41). `SingleThreadCell` stays one `RefCell` shard. Replace the 2a `None` keys with `group_of(node)`. `begin_batch_for(seed)` locks seed's shard + cross-shard-touched ascending (replaces ReentrantMutex-on-top + `global_wave`; those + `group_locks`/`SERIALIZE_WAVES` go vestigial → B-3 §7-C deletion). New shard construction needs a binding clone — `LockedCell` stores `binding: Arc<dyn BindingBoundary>` (add to `from_parts`).
- **Step 3 (B-3):** §7-B bounded cross-shard ordered-acquire/defer guard for meta/dynamic re-entry into an unheld shard; delete §7-C/§7-F vestigial union-find (`PartitionOrderViolation`/`*_or_defer`/`DeferredProducerOp` + now-vestigial `group_locks`/`global_wave`/`GroupLockRegistry`) **+ the vestigial `benches/per_subgraph_parallelism.rs`** (its `assert_ne!(partition_of(s_a), partition_of(s_b))` premise — D3 union-find auto-partitioning — is invalid post-§7: both are `None`; this is the current **CI red** on `cargo nextest run --profile ci --all-targets`, deferred to B-3 per user 2026-05-16; superseded by `group_scaling.rs`).
- **STEP 2 STATUS (2026-05-16): Step 2a LANDED + GREEN (`328015c`); Step 2b NEXT.** The first 2a attempt (rewrite ~101 `lock_state()` sites to closures) was reverted to `918c28c` mid-way (budget lost to the now-fixed test-infra saga). It was then **re-approached with a far lower-churn design and LANDED**: instead of closure-rewriting every site, `Core::lock_state()` returns a **combined `St<'_,C>` guard** that `DerefMut`s to `CoreState` (verbatim `s.nodes`/`s.children`/`s.binding`) AND exposes an inherent `.shared` field (verbatim `s.shared.<f>` — inherent-field resolves before `Deref`), so the ~104 + 23 sites stayed UNCHANGED. Only the `StateCell` two-region GAT seam, `CoreShared`+`binding`+`Drop for CoreShared`, `alloc_*`→`St`, the 5 shared-touching `&mut CoreState` helpers → `&mut St<'_,C>` (zero body change), the 4 `Weak→state.lock()` → `St::new(&*state)`, and `currently_firing`-clear relocation changed. Lock order shard-OUTER/shared-INNER everywhere (`St` encodes it) — no ABBA / re-entrancy; **825 incl. cross-thread + cascade_depth green** via `mise run gate` (rustfmt ✓, clippy ✓ clean, `nextest --profile ci` 825/825, 70 s, undisturbed). Step 2a is behaviour-identical (ONE shard, `key` ignored). **Step 2b-i LANDED + GREEN (`84986d8`):** `LockedCell` = `Mutex<CoreShared>` + explicit `default_shard: Arc<Mutex<CoreState>>` (`None` fast path — single `lock_arc`, zero map/hash) + `grouped_shards: Mutex<HashMap<SerializationGroupId, Arc<Mutex<CoreState>>>>` (`Some` only) + `binding`; `ShardGuard` = owned `'static` `parking_lot::ArcMutexGuard` via `lock_arc` — **the flagged Guard-lifetime crux is SOLVED** (arc_lock feature, zero unsafe). `SingleThreadCell` untouched ⇒ §7 floor preserved by construction. 2b-i routes `None` only ⇒ behaviour-identical; gates: `mise run gate` 825/825 + `floor_compare` SingleThreadCell **501.75 ns** / LockedCell **549.08 ns** (zero regression — gate MET). Checkpoints so far: `918c28c` (Step 1) → `328015c` (2a) → `84986d8` (2b-i), all green. **Step 2b-ii (NEXT, the real parallelism) + B-3 are COUPLED** and best executed together: 2b-ii needs (1) a `CoreShared.node_group: HashMap<NodeId,SerializationGroupId>` so `group_of` is a pure-`with_shared` lookup (no shard lock — resolves the chicken-egg), (2) registration placing grouped nodes in their group shard, (3) a per-thread ambient `CURRENT_SHARD_KEY` set by `begin_batch_for` (RAII) and read by `St::new`/`lock_state` (sound via the §7 component-homogeneity invariant: one wave = one group = one shard), (4) **a wave-ownership-model change** — today cross-thread wave serialization relies on `BatchGuard` holding `group_locks`/`global_wave` for the WHOLE wave; per-shard mutexes acquired per-`lock_state` don't give whole-wave serialization, so `begin_batch_for` must hold the seed shard's wave-lock for the wave, which makes `group_locks`/`global_wave`/`SERIALIZE_WAVES`/`acquire_touched_group_guards`/`with_global_wave_fallback`/`compute_touched_groups` vestigial → B-3's §7-B guard + §7-C/§7-F deletion (incl. the CI-red `per_subgraph_parallelism.rs`). There is NO smaller sub-step yielding gateable parallelism without (3)+(4). Records: `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/migration-status.md` § "Slice B" B-2 Step 2b-i/2b-ii + B-3.

### D220-EXEC — STEP 2b-ii EMPIRICAL FINDING (2026-05-17): the combined-guard shortcut is architecturally incompatible with disjoint-group parallelism
- **Status:** Step 2b-ii **LANDED CORRECTNESS-COMPLETE** (`graphrefly-rs` `864f02c`) but the **parallelism gate is RED** — proven, not estimated.
- **What landed (all green):** the full correct cross-shard substrate — `CoreShared.node_group` (declared group → `partition_of` + wave-lock set) **decoupled from** `CoreShared.node_shard` (component-uniform PLACEMENT → all `lock_state`/`St` routing); the real invariant is **all-`None` OR all-`Some`** ("one component = one group = one shard" is FALSE; a node's shard ≠ its group and is instead its component's shard). **/qa CORRECTION (2026-05-17):** the original claim here — "a component MAY span distinct `Some` groups, `register_all_some_chain_ok` proves it" — **overclaimed**. The Blind+Edge hunters proved (converged) that only the **single-dep distinct-`Some` chain** works; a component with **≥2 deps in distinct `Some` shards is UNCONSTRUCTABLE** (`register`/`set_deps` → `Err(UnknownDep/UnknownNode)`; `add_meta_companion` cross-shard → §7 panic). This is an honest **v1 spec divergence** (the spec permits multi-distinct-`Some` components generally; full support = the multi-shard-per-wave 2c rework — same root as the parallelism residual). Recorded in `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/porting-deferred.md` § "Multi-distinct-`Some`-group component construction — UNSUPPORTED v1". Per-thread ambient `CURRENT_SHARD_KEY` (RAII `ShardKeyGuard`) set by `begin_batch_for`=`shard_of(seed)` + ~18 single-node entry points + `register` (placement = deps' shard, shard-agnostic None/Some-mix reject via the index) + `set_serialization_group` (whole-component cross-shard migrate, both indices) + `set_deps` (shard-agnostic mix-check via the held `s.shared`, hoisted before the new-dep existence loop). New `tests/group_sharding.rs` (6 cross-shard delivery tests). Gate: `mise run gate` **825 + 24 grouped + cascade_depth ALL GREEN**; `floor_compare` SingleThreadCell **519 ns** (≈515 preserved), LockedCell **605 ns** (~10 % vs 549 at 2b-i).
- **The gate that FAILED (the whole point of Slice B):** `group_scaling/disjoint` aggregate throughput **REGRESSES** with thread count — **729 → 504 → 366 → 232 Kelem/s** (1→2→4→8 t), **indistinguishable from the serialized `same_group`/`all_none` controls**. This is the **unchanged D216 finding** — disjoint groups still do NOT run in parallel.
- **ROOT CAUSE (architectural, decisive):** the **combined-guard `St`** — the insight that made 2a/2b-i/2b-ii tractable + behaviour-correct with ~ZERO of the ~104+23 sites changed — acquires the **single `Mutex<CoreShared>` on EVERY hot-path `lock_state()`** (St::new = lock shard, THEN lock shared). Sharding `CoreState` while taking one `CoreShared` lock per `lock_state` merely **moved the D216 global-serialization bottleneck from `Mutex<CoreState>` to `Mutex<CoreShared>`**. The convenience that let the call sites stay verbatim is *exactly* what re-serializes every wave regardless of group. **The combined-guard shortcut and disjoint-group parallelism are mutually exclusive.**
- **What real parallelism requires (supersedes the "combined-guard" path for the perf goal):** the hot emit/cascade/drain path must take **ONLY the shard lock**, never `CoreShared`, on the hot path. That is the **per-site `with_shard` / `with_shared` split D220-EXEC's Step-2 originally specified** and which the combined guard deferred: the ~104 `lock_state()` sites must be triaged — pure shard-only sites → `with_shard(shard_of(node))` (no `CoreShared`); the genuinely-shared sites → brief `with_shared` **off the hot path** (id alloc, topology, scratch-release, the `currently_firing` P13 check — none per-emit); "both" sites restructured so `CoreShared` is touched once per wave, not once per `lock_state`. 2b-ii's infra (`node_group`/`node_shard` indices, `shard_of` routing, ambient `ShardKeyGuard`, register/set_deps cross-shard validation, the grouped tests) is **correct and load-bearing — the eventual parallel impl reuses all of it**; the remaining work is migrating the hot path off the combined `St` onto pure shard access. This is the large per-site rework the project repeatedly deferred; the empirical proof here is that it is **unavoidable** for the perf goal — there is no combined-guard shortcut to parallelism.
- **Net for Slice B:** B-1 + B-2 Step 1 + 2a + 2b-i + 2b-ii deliver a **correct, fully cross-shard-routed substrate** (every functional + invariant test green, floor preserved) but **not the parallelism win**. Slice B's perf goal (`group_scaling disjoint scales`) remains **OPEN**, now with a precise, evidence-backed path: the hot-path shard-only split. B-3 (delete CI-red `per_subgraph_parallelism.rs` + the vestigial `DeferredProducerOp`/`PartitionOrderViolation` no-op shims; the §7-B cross-shard guard is unnecessary under component-uniform placement) is independent cleanup, valid regardless.
- **/qa (2026-05-17, Blind Hunter + Edge Case Hunter, converged):** **QA #0** — the B-3 commit `5719897` was incomplete (only the bench *rename* committed; `Cargo.toml` `[[bench]]` removal + migration-status did NOT, leaving HEAD's manifest pointing at a moved file = `--all-targets` broken). Fixed by amend → `a67fa0b` (HEAD consistent, CI green by construction). **A(i)** — the multi-distinct-`Some` overclaim corrected (above) + `add_meta_companion` cross-shard companion now panics with the §7 diagnostic instead of a misleading "unknown companion" assert that left the documented rollback path dead. **B(i)** — `set_serialization_group` gained `SetGroupError::ReentrantOnFiringNode` (mirrors `set_deps`) + a `MigrationRollback` defence-in-depth guard (unwind → restore component to `src` + revert index; mirrors `register`'s `ScratchReleaseGuard`); the cross-thread non-atomicity (vs pre-2b) is now a documented precondition, not a bare comment. **C** — `group_sharding.rs` tightened from `.contains()` to exact-count (catches migration double/extra delivery). **E** — Blind#3/#6/#7 + the two A(i)/B(i) divergences banked in `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/porting-deferred.md` § "Slice B-2 Step 2b-ii /qa". Re-gated post-fix (see migration-status).
- **Affects:** supersedes D220-EXEC Step-2's implicit "combined-guard reaches the goal" assumption; `graphrefly-rs` `docs/migration-status.md` § Slice B; memory `project_next_porting_batch.md`.
- **Gates:** `group_scaling.rs` disjoint MUST scale (the whole point); `floor_compare.rs` all-`None` ≈515 ns (one default shard = zero regression); workspace 825; clippy 0; fmt; `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`; then `/qa`.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-rs` `node.rs`+`batch.rs`+`state_cell.rs`+`groups.rs`+`handle.rs`+`topology.rs`+Cargo.toml(parking_lot arc_lock).

### D221 — Step 2c approach: bounded lazy-`St` spike before the ~155-site rewrite; `currently_firing` → dedicated lock
- **Date:** 2026-05-17
- **Context:** "Continue with the B" → Slice B-2 Step 2c (the only open Slice B work — the hot-path shard-only split; parallelism gate RED since D216, 2b-ii proved unavoidable). The full 2c is a ~155-site triage of the two largest, most invariant-dense files (node.rs 6225 L + batch.rs 3811 L) for a parallelism win whose value was flagged materially weaker (D047 CORRECTION) while the correctness/canonical-impl goal is **already MET** by 2b-ii (only the perf win is open). Memories: `feedback_verify_premise_before_greenfield`, "no unmeasured big moves" (§7/D217 arc), perf is the secondary/workload-gated claim (`project_rust_perf_value_investigation`).
- **Options (HALT Q1):** A) bounded spike first — prove the split scales before the 155-site rewrite  B) full 2c now  C) ratify-defer (close Slice B as correct-substrate, parallelism deferred to consumer pressure D196). **HALT Q2 (`currently_firing` concurrency home, P13/D091/qa-F2):** A) dedicated `Arc<Mutex>` off `Core`  B) per-shard stack + presence atomic  C) accept per-fire `with_shared`.
- **Decision (user):** Q1 = **A (bounded spike first)**. Q2 = **A (dedicated lock off Core)** (user delegated to recommendation). Spike mechanism (Claude's design, within approved scope): (1) move `currently_firing` out of `CoreShared` into `Core.currently_firing: Arc<parking_lot::Mutex<SmallVec<[NodeId;…]>>>` (mirrors `group_locks`/`global_wave`); (2) make `St`'s shared guard **lazy** — acquired only on first `.shared` access (public field → accessor; ~32 `s.shared.` → `s.shared()`), so hot emit/cascade/drain `lock_state()` calls that never touch `.shared` pay ZERO `CoreShared` lock automatically across all 119 sites with NO per-site triage. Lock order preserved (shard OUTER held, shared INNER acquired-or-never); `SingleThreadCell` floor preserved by construction (lazy `RefCell` borrow).
- **Rationale:** the spike tests 2c's exact hypothesis (hot path off `CoreShared` ⇒ disjoint scales) by changing ~33 sites, not ~155 — decisive cheap evidence before the highest-risk rewrite in the port, directly applying the verify-premise / no-unmeasured-big-move discipline §7/D217 established at cost. If disjoint scales, lazy-`St` *is* most of 2c (155-site triage likely unnecessary). If not, the next serializer (begin_batch_for `global_wave`/`group_locks`, or `grouped_shards` map lock) is found before the big rewrite. `currently_firing` dedicated lock is the minimal correct decoupling (cross-thread P13 `contains` membership preserved; reentrant set_deps-during-fn-fire is rare → single mutex uncontended; B/C are pre-optimization / spike-defeating).
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-rs` `crates/graphrefly-core/src/{node,batch,state_cell}.rs` (spike); `benches/{floor_compare,group_scaling}.rs` (the gates); `docs/migration-status.md` § Slice B (spike outcome); `docs/porting-deferred.md` (if next serializer surfaces); memory `project_next_porting_batch.md`. Supersedes nothing — refines D220-EXEC "STEP 2b-ii FINDING"'s "the remaining work is the per-site rework" with an evidence-gated spike that may show a lower-churn mechanism reaches the same goal.

### D221 — SPIKE EMPIRICAL FINDING (2026-05-17): decisive negative — combined-guard removal is necessary-but-insufficient for parallelism AND taxes the §7 floor; redirected path identified
- **Status:** spike implemented + fully measured. **Correctness GREEN; BOTH Slice B gates RED.** NOT landable as-is (floor-regression violates the D220-EXEC zero-regression invariant). Value = the evidence; the diff is an investigation artifact, not a merge candidate.
- **What was built (graphrefly-rs working tree, uncommitted):** `currently_firing` + `pause_buffer_cap` + `max_batch_drain_iterations` moved off `CoreShared` → dedicated `Core` fields (`Arc<parking_lot::Mutex<SmallVec<[NodeId;4]>>>` + two `Arc<Atomic{U64,U32}>`, `u64::MAX`=`None`); `St` shared guard made **lazy** (`cell: &'a C` + `shared: Option<SharedGuard>`; `pub(crate) fn shared(&mut self)` accessor; ~33 sites: 26 cold `s.shared.<f>`→`s.shared().<f>`, FiringGuard/P13/defensive-clears→dedicated lock, drain-cap hoisted once-per-drain, queue_notify-cap→atomic, 2 setters→atomic store, Subscription::Drop restructured to defer the scratch-release push past the `rec` borrow). `cargo check --all-targets` clean; introduced clippy warnings fixed.
- **Correctness (bankable):** `mise run gate` GREEN — rustfmt ✓, clippy ✓ (only 2 *pre-existing* `&*self.shard` auto-deref warnings remain, NOT in the diff), `nextest --profile ci` **831/831 passed, 0 skipped (incl. cascade_depth + the grouped tests)**; zero new `unsafe`; `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]` preserved. ⇒ the dedicated-lock + atomics + lazy-`St` design is **behaviourally sound** (P13/D091/D1 cross-thread reentrancy, pause, terminal, teardown all green).
- **Gate 1 — parallelism: STILL RED, but materially improved + diagnosed.** `group_scaling --quick` aggregate Kelem/s (1→2→4→8 t): **disjoint 593→511→376→342** (still regresses — does NOT scale) · same_group 507→414→334→220 · all_none 714→522→355→264. BUT disjoint now **separates 1.55× from same_group at 8t** (was indistinguishable at 2b-ii) and is **+41–48 % faster at 8t vs the 2b-ii baseline** (criterion delta). ⇒ the combined-guard `CoreShared` serialization WAS a real bottleneck and removing it helps measurably — **necessary but insufficient.** A *second* serializer remains; prime suspect (architectural, by elimination): the per-`lock_state` `grouped_shards: Mutex<HashMap<…>>` map-lock in `LockedCell::lock_shard(Some(g))` — taken at `lock_state` frequency on ONE Core-global mutex for every grouped wave. **The full ~155-site 2c triage would NOT have reached the goal** — the next bottleneck is in the cell's shard *resolution*, not the call sites.
- **Gate 2 — §7 floor: REGRESSED ~25 % (full quiescent run, tight CI — real, not noise).** `floor/identity_dedup`: SingleThreadCell **648 ns** (vs ≈519 gate, **+25 %**), LockedCell **764 ns** (vs ≈605, **+26 %**). Root cause (decisive): moving `currently_firing` from the RefCell-resident `CoreShared` to an **unconditional `Arc<parking_lot::Mutex>`** makes the *lock-free SingleThreadCell floor* pay, per fn-fire, 2× atomic `parking_lot::Mutex::lock()` + the 3 extra `Arc` clones the widened `Core::clone` adds inside `FiringGuard::new` (`core.clone()`) — costs the RefCell field avoided.
