### D235 — S2b scope review /qa (2026-05-18): P1–P3 fix-before-commit, P2 = switch_epoch
- **Date:** 2026-05-18
- **Context:** Scoped adversarial /qa (Blind + Edge) on the full S2b substrate+operators diff before the user's boundary commit. Both reviewers converged on a correctness cluster introduced by the synchronous→`em.defer` shift.
- **Findings/Decisions (user-locked):**
  - **P1 (fix now):** `window`/`window_count` source sink lost the retired per-message + atomic terminal gate → batched `[COMPLETE,DATA]` emits DATA after COMPLETE (R2.6.4) + dual-sink (source-COMPLETE vs notifier-ERROR) double-terminal on `pid`. Fix: per-message `if s.terminated break` re-check + `let was = std::mem::replace(&mut s.terminated, true); if !was { defer terminal }` (restores single-flag atomicity; keeps D234 in-closure `inner_id`).
  - **P2 (fix now; design = switch_epoch):** `switch_map`/`exhaust_map` fast double-switch within one wave — cancel `inner_sub.take()` reads a slot the prior subscribe-defer hasn't populated → both inners live. Fix: monotonic `switch_epoch: u64` in `SwitchState`/`ExhaustState`; bumped at outer-fire, captured into the subscribe-defer; inside the defer post-`try_subscribe`, if `s.switch_epoch != captured` drop the new `SubGuard` immediately (unsubscribe) instead of installing.
  - **P3 (fix now):** the D-reflect F1 fix conflated mailbox-drain iterations with the fire-cascade `cap` → heavy producer drain (merge_map buffer / window_time rotations) trips `assert!(guard<cap)` (prod panic). Fix: only count *no-progress* iterations against `cap` (don't count an iteration that drained a non-empty mailbox / made forward progress).
  - **P4/P5 (fix now):** clean 13 unused-`core_s`/`binding` warnings (clippy-clean gate); tighten the `is_runnable` same-thread-vs-cross-thread comment.
  - **P6 (defer):** `panic!` partition-order arms — behaviour-equivalent to the retired deferred `core.subscribe()` (which also panicked; `push_deferred` ran immediately per D211), so not a regression; verify whether an in-wave drain inside a seed-routed `BatchGuard` can legitimately `try_subscribe` an untouched serialization group → `porting-deferred.md`.
  - **P7 (defer):** Blind #6 re-entrant `drain_mailbox` FIFO interleaving — the porting-deferred "verify-when" trigger is now met (Defer restructure landed); obligate the nested-wave-reorder test in the next slice.
  - **P8 (defer):** ~7 `let _ = em.defer(...)` `#[must_use]` suppressions — all verified handle-free (no leak); add guard-comments next slice.
  - **F4 (reject):** `default_producer_deactivate` stale-id reuse — `alloc_sub_id` is monotonic-never-recycled; close with an invariant comment.
- **Decision (user):** apply P1+P2(switch_epoch)+P3+P4+P5 before commit; P6/P7/P8 → `porting-deferred.md`; F4 reject+comment.
- **Affects:** `buffer.rs` (window/window_count terminal gate), `higher_order.rs` (switch/exhaust epoch), `batch.rs` (cap accounting + comment), operators warning cleanup, `producer.rs` (F4 invariant comment), `porting-deferred.md` (P6/P7/P8).

### D234 — Windowing + higher-order: both sinks route through `em.defer`; shared routing state read INSIDE the (FIFO, owner-serialized) closures
- **Date:** 2026-05-18
- **Context:** `window`/`window_count`/`switch|merge|concat|exhaust_map` need sink-side topology mutation (`create_window_node` / dynamic inner `subscribe`). Old code did it synchronously under the state lock so `s.inner_id` was consistent at the exact boundary. Under D233 a sink reaches `CoreFull` only via `em.defer` (applied later in the drain loop). Surfaced as a HALT (semantics-affecting; 6th-vindication territory).
- **Options:** A) route BOTH source-forward and notifier/count-roll (and higher-order inner-sub mgmt) through `em.defer`, read shared routing state (`s.inner_id`) INSIDE the closures so mailbox FIFO = arrival order preserves "create-before-later-forwards"; B) pursue a synchronous-create escape (reopens the D232/D233 no-sync-&Core-in-sinks lock); C) split windowing/higher-order to its own focused slice.
- **Decision (user):** **A**. Critical implementation rule: **every read of routing state that selects the target node (`s.inner_id`) must happen INSIDE the defer closure**, never at sink-fire time — otherwise a source-DATA firing between a notifier-DATA and its roll-defer would read the stale `inner_id`. With both forward and roll deferred and the selector read in-closure, mailbox FIFO (= arrival order, owner-serialized drain) yields correct window boundaries. Incidentally resolves Blind #6's ordering concern for these ops (FIFO *is* the order).
- **Rationale:** only correctness-preserving option that respects the D232/D233 locks + offline/forbid(unsafe); uniform across windowing + higher-order; the FIFO argument is the proof. Cost: these ops shift from synchronous-in-sink to in-wave-FIFO-deferred; obligation: a window-boundary correctness test (notifier-DATA interleaved with source-DATA must not mis-route across the boundary) + higher-order inner-lifecycle test.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-operators` `buffer.rs` (`window`/`window_count` source_sink + notifier/count sink → `em.defer`, `s.inner_id` read in-closure), `higher_order.rs` (all 4; inner subscribe/unsubscribe via `em.defer`, triple-weak removed), new window-boundary + inner-lifecycle tests; `porting-deferred.md` S2b windowing entry; mirrors into Blind #6 resolution.

### D233 — Sink-side register/subscribe re-entry: `MailboxOp::Defer(FnOnce(&dyn CoreFull))` drained in-wave
- **Date:** 2026-05-17
- **Context:** Phase-1 sixth producer sub-fork: windowing operators (`buffer.rs` `create_window_node` from sinks) + higher-order operators (`higher_order.rs` `switch/merge/concat/exhaust_map` sinks dynamically `subscribe` to runtime-created inner sources) perform **value-returning topology mutation (`register_*`/`subscribe`) from inside long-lived sinks** — not covered by D232-AMEND's fire-and-forget `MailboxOp{Emit,Complete,Error}`. Surfaced as a HALT (6th vindication of the "producer pattern = own focused slice" conclusion); user chose to design it now + continue fused.
- **Options:** Defer-closure mailbox variant (`FnOnce(&dyn CoreFull)`) drained in-wave [chosen]; make `Defer` the sole mailbox payload; distinct producer-sink kind carrying `&dyn CoreFull` through Core dispatch (narrow-C).
- **Decision (user):** add **`MailboxOp::Defer(Box<dyn FnOnce(&dyn CoreFull) + Send>)`**, keeping the explicit `Emit/Complete/Error` fast-path variants. New object-safe **`trait CoreFull`** (`register_state`/`register_computed`/`subscribe`/`try_subscribe`/`unsubscribe`/`emit`/`complete`/`error` — all by `NodeId`/`HandleId`/`Sink`, no `C`/`T`), blanket-impl'd for `Core<C>`. The `BatchGuard` drain-to-quiescence loop (owner holds `&Core`) applies `Defer` via `f(self as &dyn CoreFull)` — **in-wave, synchronous, cascade-ordering-preserved** (identical placement to A′). Windowing/higher-order sinks post a `Defer` closure that performs the create-node / dynamic-inner-subscribe **inside the closure**, consuming the returned `NodeId`/`SubscriptionId` to drive the operator's existing captured `Arc<Mutex<state>>` (never returned to the type-erased `Sink`). `create_window_node` generalized to `&dyn CoreFull`.
- **Rationale:** one uniform mechanism (one variant + one object-safe trait) covering all sink-side Core re-entry incl. topology; offline + `forbid(unsafe)`-clean; D225 untouched; in-wave/ordering-preserved; the value-return problem dissolves because results are consumed inside the owner-side closure, not handed back across the `Sink` boundary.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-core::mailbox` (`MailboxOp::Defer` + `post_defer`), new `graphrefly-core` `CoreFull` trait + blanket impl, `Core::drain_mailbox` (apply `Defer`), `ProducerEmitter` (add `defer(FnOnce(&dyn CoreFull))`), `buffer.rs` windowing + `higher_order.rs` sinks restructured to post `Defer`, `create_window_node`→`&dyn CoreFull`; cross-track-ledger + migration-status/porting-deferred.

### D232-AMEND (A′) — scoped-TLS infeasible offline; producer sinks post to an in-wave-drained `CoreMailbox` producer-op queue
- **Date:** 2026-05-17
- **Context:** D232(A)'s implementation hit a hard wall: `scoped-tls 1.0.1` (only offline-available; `scoped-tls-hkt`/`better-scoped-tls` not in registry cache, network sandboxed) stores `Cell<*const ()>` requiring `T: Sized` — `dyn CoreReentry` won't compile through it; the sized-newtype workaround hits scoped-tls's `'static`-variance wall (producer-sink borrow is shorter than `'static`); a hand-rolled thin-pointer round-trip needs `unsafe` (invariant #1 `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]` blocks). Surfaced as a HALT, not silently substituted.
- **Options:** A′) producer sinks post `Emit/Complete/Error` to the (already-`Arc`/`'static`/`Send+Sync`) `CoreMailbox`; the `BatchGuard` drain-to-quiescence loop drains it **in-wave, immediately** (NOT post-wave → behaviourally identical to A, NOT the rejected post-wave B); narrow-C) producer-specific sink type carrying `&dyn CoreReentry`; vendor `scoped-tls-hkt`.
- **Decision (user):** **A′**. Amends **D227** ("`CoreMailbox` = timer Emit + S4 wake **only**") → "+ an in-wave-drained producer-op queue (`Emit/Complete/Error`)". **D225 untouched** (`unsubscribe` stays synchronous owner-invoked). **D232's `reentry`/`CoreReentry`/scoped-TLS is dropped entirely** — unnecessary under A′: producer sinks capture `Arc<CoreMailbox>` (exactly like `timer.rs` already does) and post ops; no ambient/TLS needed. The added `scoped-tls` dep is reverted.
- **Rationale:** offline-safe, `forbid(unsafe)`-clean, reuses the D227/D230 mailbox infra, preserves A's properties (in-wave, synchronous-to-quiescence, cascade-ordering-identical — it is just another pending-work source in the existing quiescence loop, consistent with the pre-S2b deferred-producer-op-drained-at-wave-end behaviour). Strictly simpler than A (no new module/dep/trait).
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-core::mailbox` (generalize to a `MailboxOp{Emit,Complete,Error}` queue; `post_emit`/`post_complete`/`post_error`); `Core::drain_mailbox` (apply all op kinds); the wave drain-to-quiescence loop (`batch.rs` `drain_and_flush`) drains the mailbox each iteration; producer factories capture `ctx.core().mailbox()` for sinks (D231 build still uses `ctx.core()`); revert `scoped-tls` from `Cargo.toml`s; supersedes the D232 `reentry`-module plan in `migration-status.md`/`porting-deferred.md`.

### D231 — Producer build/teardown run owner-side with `&Core` (no stored/cloned Core)
- **Date:** 2026-05-17
- **Context:** Phase-1 fourth finding (during S2b consumer churn): `graphrefly-operators::producer` stores a cloned `Core` in `ProducerCtx`, captures `Core::clone()` into operator-factory closures + wave-end callbacks, and holds `Vec<Subscription>` RAII. D227's `CoreMailbox` is timer-`Emit`-only (D225 lock); it does NOT cover a producer build closure that subscribes sinks to *upstream* sources + emits. So removing `Core: Clone`/RAII left an unmade design decision: how does a producer build closure reach a relocatable non-`Clone` `Core`? Surfaced as a HALT (40 operators errors hinge on it), not silently picked.
- **Options:** a) producer build/teardown run owner-side with `&Core` passed per-invocation — `ProducerCtx`/`register_producer_build` stop storing a `Core`; the producer-build `BindingBoundary` surface is widened to receive `&Core` (parallels D229's `producer_deactivate` widening); `ProducerNodeState.subs: Vec<(NodeId,SubscriptionId)>` unsubscribed via the D229 owner-driven chain; b) widen `CoreMailbox` to a general producer op-channel (reopens D225/D227); c) defer producer pattern to its own focused slice (revert to gated discipline).
- **Decision (user):** **a** — producer build/teardown owner-side with `&Core`; no stored/cloned `Core` anywhere in the producer pattern; `Vec<Subscription>`→`Vec<(NodeId,SubscriptionId)>` cleaned via D229's `producer_deactivate(&self, node_id, &unsub)`. Then finish all ~70 consumer fixes, gate, commit S2b, continue S2c/S3/S4 fused.
- **Rationale:** consistent with D221 (Core relocates; the borrow checker is the lock — pass `&Core` in the synchronous owner context, never store it) and with D229 (same owner-driven widening pattern already chosen for `producer_deactivate`). Avoids reopening the D225/D227 mailbox lock. No `Weak<C>`, no `unsafe`, no parameterless-`Drop`.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-operators::producer` (`ProducerCtx` no longer stores `Core`; `register_producer_build`/build+activate/teardown closures take `&Core`; `ProducerNodeState.subs`), the producer-build `BindingBoundary` surface (substrate contract widening — cross-track-ledger + `migration-status.md` § Slice B + `porting-deferred.md`), all producer-consuming operators (`source.rs`/`higher_order.rs`/`temporal.rs`/`buffer.rs`/`control.rs`/etc.), `graphrefly-graph`, `graphrefly-core` producer tests, napi `core_bindings.rs` producer wiring.

### D230 — Minimal timer-Emit mailbox drainer pulled into S2b (bounded mini-M6)
- **Date:** 2026-05-17
- **Context:** Phase-1 third hard coupling: removing `Weak<C>` from `timer.rs`'s autonomous `tokio::spawn` task needs a `CoreMailbox` *drainer* to deliver posted `Emit`s; D225 deferred the mailbox drain/bridge to M6, which "finish s2–s6" scoped OUT. `Weak<C>`-removal (S2b) and the drainer (M6) are not separable without either a `Weak<C>` regression (violates D223) or a timer delivery-timing regression. Surfaced as a HALT.
- **Options:** A) pull a minimal timer-Emit drainer (mini-M6) into S2b; B) owner-pumped mailbox + accept/doc a timer-timing change; C) re-sequence M6 before S2b; D) abandon fused run, S2b-only + /qa + reassess.
- **Decision (user):** **A** — bounded mini-M6 in S2b. **Design:** `Arc<CoreMailbox>` (`Send+Sync`) = `Mutex<VecDeque<(NodeId, Vec<Message>)>>` (timer Emit queue) + a wake primitive + the S4 per-group runnable wake-bit field (D227 full shape). `timer.rs`'s task holds `Arc<CoreMailbox>`, posts `(node_id, msgs)` + signals on fire (no `Weak<C>`, no `&Core`). New owner-invoked sync `Core::drain_mailbox()` pops the queue and applies each via the existing sync `Core::emit` (no async in Core; honors "Core never async"). The drain point is the **existing** test-harness advance/yield helper (`TestRuntime`) + the napi pump — tests already MUST advance the tokio runtime for timer tasks to fire, so draining there is **behaviour-identical from the test's observable contract** (advance → timers post → drain delivers). No Core relocation, no ~50-file test churn, no `Weak<C>`.
- **Rationale:** the only resolution that keeps `Weak<C>`-removal behaviour-identical without dragging in full M6 (Core-relocation worker pool + ~50-file harness rewrite). The drainer is the minimal owner-invoked sync method; the wake-bit field lands now (D227) but its host-executor wiring stays M6. Bench `group_scaling` re-measure stays S4.
- **Affects:** new `graphrefly-core::mailbox` (`CoreMailbox`), `Core` (owns `Arc<CoreMailbox>`; `drain_mailbox()`), `timer.rs` (`WeakCore`→`Arc<CoreMailbox>`; task posts not upgrades), test harness `tests/common/mod.rs` advance helper (+`drain_mailbox`), napi pump (`core_bindings.rs`), `porting-deferred.md` (mini-M6 banked: full host-executor wake wiring still M6). Scope note in `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/migration-status.md` § Slice B.

### D247 — S2c graph-tree single-owner realization: `Rc<RefCell<GraphInner>>` (not owned-`&mut`)
- **Date:** 2026-05-19
- **Context:** D246 r7 says S2c drops `Mutex<GraphInner>`→`RefCell`/owner-`&mut` but does not pin which for the namespace tree. The tree inherently needs shared interior nodes for parent (`ancestors()`)/child navigation; `Graph` is today `Arc<Mutex<GraphInner>>`, `#[derive(Clone)]`, compile-asserted `Send+Sync+'static` (boundary-1 QA-A4), captured into `Send+Sync`-bounded `NamespaceChangeSink`/`DescribeSink`/observe sinks. Fork surfaced at S2c HALT.
- **Options:** A1) `Rc<RefCell<GraphInner>>` + `Weak` parent — minimal correct single-owner shape; `Graph` becomes `!Send+!Sync`; delete A4 `Graph` assertion + relax sink bounds. A2) owned `Box`-children `&mut` tree — keeps `Graph: Send` but a large M2 API reshape (D242's rejected Option-B `ancestors()`/subgraph-handle/mount rewrite).
- **Decision (user, via D246 reaffirmation — "completeness, correctness, simplicity; pre-1.0, no legacy ergonomics"):** **A1.** The `Arc<Mutex>`+`Send+Sync` shape IS the "shared-Core-era legacy" D246 r7 names; `Rc<RefCell>` is the literal "RefCell" realization. A2 would *increase* complexity (against "simplicity").
- **Rationale:** Under D246 the owner thread owns Core+Graph together; S4 = independent per-worker Cores (nothing moves a Graph across threads), so `Graph: Send` was a shared-Core-era defensive assertion, not an actor-model requirement. Sinks fire owner-side with `&Core` on the one owner thread → no `Send+Sync` needed. `Core` itself becomes `Send+!Sync` (RefCell regions); `OwnedCore` A4 assertion relaxes `Send+Sync`→`Send`-only (Core `!Sync` by D221/D223 design).
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-graph` (`GraphInner` tree `Arc<Mutex>`→`Rc<RefCell>`, parent `Weak<Mutex>`→`Weak<RefCell>`, `Graph` no longer `Send+Sync`, delete A4 assertion); `NamespaceChangeSink`/`DescribeSink`/observe sink bounds relaxed; `graphrefly-core` `OwnedCore` A4 assertion → `Send`-only; pairs with S2c `StateCell` collapse (D246 r7). Canonical: this entry + D246.

### D248 — S2c Opt-1: relax substrate `Sink`/`TopologySink` Send+Sync (full consistent single-owner)
- **Date:** 2026-05-19
- **Context:** Implementing D247-A1 (`GraphInner`→`Rc<RefCell>`) surfaced that reactive describe/observe capture `Weak<RefCell<GraphInner>>` (`rc::Weak` = `!Send`) into closures registered via `core.subscribe_topology`/`register_ns_sink`, which must satisfy the **substrate** types `graphrefly_core::{Sink,TopologySink}` = `Arc<dyn Fn(..) + Send + Sync>`. The graph-tree single-owner conversion is inseparable from relaxing the substrate Sink Send+Sync contract. Surfaced as a HALT (substrate-contract + napi + cross-track-ledger, design-bearing — `feedback_no_autonomous_decisions`).
- **Options:** Opt-1) relax substrate `Sink`/`TopologySink` (+ graph `NamespaceChangeSink`/`DescribeSink`) to drop `Send+Sync` now — `Core`/`OwnedCore` become `!Send` (the `Arc<CoreMailbox>` stays the only cross-thread bridge); ripples to napi `BindingBoundary`, `timer.rs`, operators/structures/storage, reverses the A4 `Core/OwnedCore: Send` invariant. Opt-2) keep `GraphInner` as `Arc<Mutex<>>`, scope r7-graph + the Sink relaxation into a dedicated coupled follow-on slice before S3.
- **Decision (user):** **Opt-1** — relax the substrate Sink contract now; full consistent single-owner.
- **Rationale:** the `Sink: Send+Sync` bound is *also* shared-Core-era legacy (S4 = independent per-worker Cores ⇒ a Core never `Send`-moves with live sinks; the actor's only cross-thread inbox is `Arc<CoreMailbox>` for id-only timer posts). Matches D246 "single-owner pushed all the way down." `CoreMailbox`/`MailboxOp::Defer` `Send` coupling (timer cross-thread post path) that collides with capturing the `Rc` graph tree into an in-wave `Defer` is the **D246 rule-8 / S4 typed-`MailboxOp` reshape** explicitly scoped to S4 by migration-status ("don't churn the mailbox twice") — record-and-skip per the D246 protocol where it genuinely requires the S4 reshape.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-core` (`Sink`/`TopologySink` aliases, `Core`/`OwnedCore` Send asserts, possibly `DeferFn`/`CoreMailbox`), `graphrefly-graph` (`GraphInner`→`Rc<RefCell>`, `NamespaceChangeSink`/`DescribeSink`, A4 `Graph` assert), `graphrefly-operators`/`-structures`/`-storage` sink constructions, napi `BindingBoundary`/`timer.rs`; `docs/cross-track-ledger.md` (substrate-contract widening); `migration-status.md` S2c; `porting-deferred.md` "D246 record-and-skip". Canonical: this entry + D247 + D246.

### D249 — S2c-Opt-1: minimal owner-side Defer queue split off CoreMailbox (pre-empts part of S4)
- **Date:** 2026-05-19
- **Context:** D248/Opt-1 (relax substrate Sink) made `Sink`/`TopologySink`/graph tree `!Send`; operators (`ProducerEmitter::defer`) + reactive describe/observe capture those `!Send` values into `MailboxOp::Defer` closures, but `DeferFn = Box<dyn FnOnce(&dyn CoreFull) + Send>` and `CoreMailbox` must stay `Send+Sync` (graphrefly-core `default = [std, tokio]` ⇒ `timer.rs` shares `Arc<CoreMailbox>` into a `tokio::spawn` task). The full D246-rule-8 typed-`MailboxOp` reshape is migration-status-fenced to S4 ("don't churn the mailbox twice"). Surfaced as a sequencing HALT.
- **Options:** A) pull the minimal Defer/mailbox split into S2c now (accepts touching the mailbox twice: minimal now + S4 per-group-wake/typed-snapshot). B) keep `DeferFn:Send`, record-and-skip the `!Send`-capturing tail (GraphInner Rc<RefCell> reactive path + operators defer-with-sink) to S4.
- **Decision (user):** **A** — minimal split now.
- **Design:** `DeferFn = Box<dyn FnOnce(&dyn CoreFull)>` (drop `+Send`). Delete `MailboxOp::Defer`; `MailboxOp = Emit|Complete|Error` (id-only, `Send`) — `CoreMailbox` stays `Send+Sync` (timer bridge unchanged, `mailbox.rs` assert holds). New owner-only `DeferQueue { Mutex<VecDeque<DeferFn>>, closed }` (`!Send`); `Core` owns `Rc<DeferQueue>`; `ProducerEmitter` carries `Rc<DeferQueue>` (via `for_core`). `Core::drain_mailbox` drains the id-mailbox AND `deferred.take_all()` (each `f(self)`); the in-wave `BatchGuard` drain mirrors. Reactive describe/observe topo sinks capture `Rc<DeferQueue>` instead of `Arc<CoreMailbox>`. S4 still does the per-group-wake + typed snapshot/prune reshape (the acknowledged second touch).
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-core` (`mailbox.rs` MailboxOp/DeferFn/new DeferQueue, `node.rs` Core field + drain), `graphrefly-operators` (`ProducerEmitter`), `graphrefly-graph` (describe/observe topo-sink capture), napi/test harness drain sites; `docs/cross-track-ledger.md`; `migration-status.md` S2c + S4 (note the pre-empted scope); `porting-deferred.md`. Canonical: this entry + D248/D247/D246.

### D250 — S4: retire the in-wave pause/resume/set_deps synchronous-re-entry stubs as deleted-model (no new substrate seam)
- **Date:** 2026-05-19
- **Context:** S4 must resolve 3 still-`#[ignore]` core stubs whose record-and-skip notes say the invariant "stays LIVE": `lock_released::fn_can_reenter_core_pause_resume_during_invoke_fn`, `lock_discipline::sink_can_reenter_core_via_pause_and_resume`, `slice_f_corrections::a6_set_deps_from_firing_fn_rejected_with_reentrant_error`. Their ONLY historical trigger was the binding-holds-cloned-`Core` synchronous re-entry mechanism (`ReentrantBinding { core_slot }`), structurally deleted by move-only single-owner Core (D221/D246). Under the actor model `invoke_fn` carries no `&Core`; `pause`/`resume`/`set_deps` are absent from `CoreFull` and are not `MailboxOp` variants. Surfaced as a `/porting-to-rs` full-mode HALT (substrate-contract-bearing; never locked — D246 explicitly punted "S4 owner-side seam — *when* it lands"). `feedback_no_autonomous_decisions`.
- **Options:** A) widen object-safe `CoreFull` with `pause`/`resume`/`set_deps` (every `BindingBoundary` impl + napi must add them; cross-track-ledger row; vtable + FFI-adjacent surface growth for zero consumer). B) add typed id-only `MailboxOp::{Pause,Resume,SetDeps}` variants (larger hot-drain enum; still an imperative re-entry surface, no consumer). C) retire as deleted-model: the synchronous in-wave re-entry path was a shared-Core legacy artifact; keep `#[ignore]` with a "retired" reason + this decision entry (never delete, never rewrite intent — same treatment as the §7 cross-thread group tests); the β-valid path (emit → controller node → owner-side `pause`/`resume`) already exists and is exercised by other tests; the `SetDepsError::ReentrantOnFiringNode` guard *code* stays live as defensive cover for a future owner-side seam.
- **Decision (user-delegated — "which is most clean, decision-consistent, performant, ignore legacy/backward compat"; recommendation accepted):** **C — retire as deleted-model.** **AMENDED 2026-05-20 (S6 close):** the 3 `#[ignore]` stubs were **DELETED outright** per `feedback_no_backward_compat` ("if a test stub can't be driven, it's dead code"). Original D250-C decision kept the stubs as `#[ignore]` with verbose retirement prose; user pushback at S6 close — "why do we still keep the tests if we retired stubs?" — surfaced that the "intent preserved, never deleted" hedge was a legacy-preserving compromise contradicting the no-backward-compat directive. The structural invariant is fully covered by the live mailbox-reentry tests in the same files (`sink_can_complete_another_node_from_callback`, `custom_equals_can_reenter_core_during_emission`, `handshake_sink_can_reenter_core_emit_on_other_node`); the `ReentrantOnFiringNode` guard code stays live in `node.rs` as defensive cover for a future owner-side seam (commented inline at the guard site). If a future slice widens `CoreFull`/`MailboxOp` with `pause`/`resume`/`set_deps` for a real consumer, write FRESH tests for the new seam — don't resurrect the deleted stubs. Net effect: gate count drops 810/3/0 → 810/0/0 on `--profile ci`.
- **Rationale:** A and B both spend substrate surface (trait/FFI vtable resp. hot-path enum) to preserve a *deleted* capability with zero consumer scenario — contradicts D196 consumer-pressure and D246 "ignore legacy ergonomics." A synchronous fn/sink re-entry into `pause`/`resume` is precisely the imperative-from-reactive-layer anti-pattern design invariant #2 forbids (`feedback_no_imperative`); the spec-correct path is reactive (emit → controller → owner-side pause/resume), already covered. C is the only option with zero substrate growth, zero cross-track-ledger event, no hot-path cost — cleanest, most decision-consistent, most performant. The "invariant stays LIVE" record-and-skip wording was a conservative legacy-preserving hedge; the no-legacy directive resolves it toward retirement. Reverses that hedge for these 3 stubs only; the §7 cross-thread group/`lock_discipline::concurrent_subscribe`/`group_parallelism` tests remain S4 one-Core-per-worker *rebuilds* (genuinely-deleted *model*, but the parallelism invariant is reachable via independent Cores — distinct from this imperative-re-entry retirement); `lock_released::late_subscriber…` remains the D246-r6 producer-based rewrite (unchanged).
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-rs` `crates/graphrefly-core/tests/{lock_released,lock_discipline,slice_f_corrections}.rs` (3 stubs → `#[ignore = "retired (D250): …"]`, intent preserved); `node.rs` `set_deps` `ReentrantOnFiringNode` guard gains an invariant comment (code stays live); `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/porting-deferred.md` § "D246 record-and-skip" (move the 3 entries to retired-resolved) + `migration-status.md` S4 closing block. No `CoreFull`/`MailboxOp`/substrate-contract change ⇒ **no `docs/cross-track-ledger.md` event.** Canonical: this entry + D246.

### D251 — S4: D246 rule-8 = reusable coalescing slot; D246-r8's "typed MailboxOp / fuse-with-mailbox-reshape" premise reconciled post-D249
- **Date:** 2026-05-19
- **Context:** D246 rule 8 ("hot-path alloc discipline: typed mailbox variants **(or a reusable slot)** for describe/observe/storage snapshot+prune instead of `post_defer(Box<dyn FnOnce>)` per emission") was written pre-D249 assuming ONE mailbox and a *pending S4 `CoreMailbox` per-group-wake reshape to fuse the typed variants into* (migration-status: "fuse with the per-group-wake reshape — don't churn the mailbox twice"). **D249 already executed the relevant split:** the 3 rule-8 observation paths (`graphrefly-graph` observe `NodeTornDown` prune + reactive-describe re-snapshot; `graphrefly-storage` `graph_integration` snapshot+persist) capture `!Send` state and now post to the owner-only **`!Send` `DeferQueue`**, NOT the `Send` `CoreMailbox`. So "typed `MailboxOp` variants on `CoreMailbox`" no longer fits (wrong queue), and the "mailbox reshape to fuse with" was already spent by D249 (acknowledged second-touch). A genuine stale premise (`feedback_verify_premise_before_greenfield`) surfaced during S4 implementation; resolved within D246-r8's own stated latitude rather than re-opening the locked decision.
- **Options:** A) add typed `DeferQueue` op variants (a `DeferQueue`-layer enum reshape — re-introduces a queue-type churn D249's "don't churn twice" lock guards against, for a perf-only item with no consumer pressure). B) reusable per-handle coalescing slot: an owner-thread-only `Cell<bool>` "scheduled" gate (+ a pending buffer where the op is not idempotent, i.e. observe-prune's torn-id set) so exactly ONE `Box` is posted per wave and the work is coalesced/deduped at drain. C) defer rule-8 to a dedicated post-S4 slice (violates D246 "finish each S fully — don't defer the big chunk").
- **Decision (within D246-r8 latitude; user operating directive "clean, decision-consistent, performant, ignore legacy" — same mode as D250):** **B — reusable coalescing slot.** D246-r8 explicitly authorizes "(or a reusable slot)"; choosing it post-D249 is staying inside the locked decision, not a new fork.
- **Rationale:** B is the cleanest/most-performant/most-consistent: one alloc + one snapshot|prune per wave instead of per emission, AND a free dedup win (multiple `DepsChanged`/tier3-5 emissions in a wave → one re-snapshot; deferred-snapshot is already acceptable per D243/D244, so behaviour-equivalent). Zero queue-type churn (honours D249's "don't churn the mailbox twice"), zero public-API change ⇒ internal refactor, **no parity-surface widening / no cross-track-ledger event**. A spends substrate surface for a perf-only item with no consumer (D196). Observe-prune is not idempotent, so it additionally carries an owner-thread-only `Rc<RefCell<Vec<NodeId>>>` torn-id buffer drained as the exact union (set-equivalent to per-event unsubscribe).
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-rs` `crates/graphrefly-graph/src/{observe.rs,describe.rs}` + `crates/graphrefly-storage/src/graph_integration.rs` (per-handle `scheduled` `Cell` + observe-prune pending buffer; one Box/wave); `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/{migration-status.md S4 block,porting-deferred.md "D246 rule 8" entry → resolved}`. No `graphrefly-core` mailbox/`CoreFull` change. Canonical: this entry + D246 (rule 8) + D249.

### D252 — S5: collapse `IN_TICK_OWNED` to `Cell<bool>` + lock "one Core per OS thread" as a hard invariant
- **Date:** 2026-05-19 (locked post-S4 /qa reflection — user directive: "ignore legacy or backward compat; clean/correct/simple/performant/memory-efficient/less-maintenance-burden")
- **Context:** S2c-S4 /qa reflection (Part 2 of the post-S-sequence honest-feedback exchange) surfaced that `IN_TICK_OWNED: thread_local!(RefCell<AHashSet<u64>>)` keyed by `Core::generation` was kept post-D248 single-owner to defend against "one OS thread owns Core-A and Core-B and nests waves between them owner-side." That defense is **theoretical** — no current code path produces it (would require a `DeferFn` closure on Core-A's `DeferQueue` to capture & call into `&Core-B`; under D248 `Core: !Send` the closure is owner-side but no in-tree consumer does this). The set hashing + allocation cost is paid on every `BatchGuard` claim/release for a use case nobody can enumerate. Per `feedback_no_backward_compat` + the post-S4 reflection directive, the stronger invariant "one Core per OS thread, no nested cross-Core driving on a single thread" is preferable.
- **Options:** A) collapse to `thread_local!(Cell<bool>)` + add a `BatchGuard` claim-time `panic!` if a non-matching Core's generation is observed (lock the invariant, fail-loud on violation). B) keep the AHashSet (status quo; defensive). C) audit-first — enumerate every plausible cross-Core same-thread call site before deciding.
- **Decision (user-locked):** **A — collapse + hard invariant.**
- **Rationale:** Real simplification (no hashing, no allocation, one bit per OS thread); commits to the stronger contract permanently; aligns with the actor model's "one worker = one Core" framing; D196-consistent (the defended use case has no consumer). The panic-on-violation guard makes the contract structurally enforced rather than relying on convention. Reverses the D047 per-(Core,thread) keying, which itself was a fix for the now-deleted shared-Core cross-thread model.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-rs` `crates/graphrefly-core/src/batch.rs` (replace the `IN_TICK_OWNED: AHashSet<u64>` thread-local + the per-generation `contains`/`insert`/`remove` paths with a `Cell<u64>` storing the active `Core::generation` or `0` for "no active Core" — bool isn't enough because we still need to detect cross-Core nesting attempts to panic). `BatchGuard::is_owning` checks the slot, claims via `compare_exchange`-equivalent (single-thread Cell::replace), panics on a non-matching non-zero observation. `BatchGuard::drop` clears the slot. Documents the invariant in module-doc. Decision: this entry. Canonical: this entry + D246 + D047.

### D253 — S5: delete `SchedulingGroupId` + the whole declared-group-identity API surface until M6 needs it
- **Date:** 2026-05-19 (locked post-S4 /qa reflection)
- **Context:** S3 renamed `SerializationGroupId` → `SchedulingGroupId` (~59 refs) while S2c deleted the §7 cross-thread group-lock machinery the type used to gate. Post-S4 the type + `CoreShared.node_group` HashMap + `partition_of`/`group_of`/`set_scheduling_group` + the `scheduling_group` field on `NodeOpts` exist as **identity-only scaffolding** for a consumer that doesn't exist: M6's per-binding group executor is explicitly post-1.0 and may not consume per-`SchedulingGroupId` sub-bits at all (D250-style reasoning: M6 schedules at the Core/worker grain). Per strict D196 consumer-pressure reading + the post-S4 reflection directive ("ignore legacy"), keeping the surface is speculative substrate carry.
- **Options:** A) delete entirely (the type, the HashMap, the 3-method API, the `scheduling_group` field on `NodeOpts`, the `scheduling_groups.rs` + `group_sharding.rs` test files, the field in `NodeRegistration`/`NodeOpts`, any flow.rs test that asserts it; ~60-100 refs). When M6 lands, re-introduce with M6's actual needs in view. B) keep as identity-only scaffolding. C) `#[doc(hidden)] + #[deprecated]` now, delete at M6 start.
- **Decision (user-locked):** **A — delete (D196-pure).**
- **Rationale:** Strict consumer-pressure reading is decision-consistent (D196, D250-r-logic); a future M6 design pass is **better** than "wire up the existing surface" because it can encode M6's actual scheduling needs without the legacy shape constraining it. Reverses S3's rename effort by ~60 lines of deletion — small cost. Removes a class of "speculative substrate" the rest of the codebase would otherwise route around (e.g., `NodeOpts.scheduling_group: Option<SchedulingGroupId>` would force every test setup to think about it). Net code REMOVED.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-rs` `crates/graphrefly-core/src/{handle.rs (SchedulingGroupId newtype + impl + lib.rs re-export removal),node.rs (CoreShared.node_group HashMap, NodeOpts.scheduling_group field, set_scheduling_group/group_of/partition_of methods, group-dep-consistency RegisterError variant + dispatch_consistency check at register/set_deps), batch.rs (any group-touched-from-seed walks)}`; `crates/graphrefly-core/tests/{scheduling_groups.rs, group_sharding.rs, group_parallelism.rs (DROP the `g: SchedulingGroupId` parameter on the worker fn — the actor-model-rebuild tests don't need it anyway), lock_released.rs/lock_discipline.rs/slice_f_corrections.rs (anywhere that imports SchedulingGroupId)}`; `crates/graphrefly-core/benches/group_scaling.rs` (rename `group_scaling/independent_cores` bench label; it doesn't actually use group ids); `crates/graphrefly-operators/tests/flow.rs` (any group refs). `migration-status.md` S5 closing block + `porting-deferred.md` archive the S3 closing block as superseded. **No napi/cross-track-ledger event** (was never bound). Decision: this entry. Canonical: this entry + D196 + D250-r-logic.

### D254 — S5: Tier A bundle (DeferQueue Mutex/Atomic relaxation + typed MailboxOp::TimerEmit + doc-sweep + process-discipline memory)
- **Date:** 2026-05-19 (locked post-S4 /qa reflection; "we just have to do them all eventually")
- **Context:** /qa reflection items #1, #2, #7, #10, and process-discipline items #4 #6 #8 #9 are pure mechanical cleanups carrying no design fork (the user explicitly delegated scope — "you pick. We just have to do them all eventually."). Bundled into S5 alongside D252/D253 as one coherent gated commit to avoid commit-noise from sequencing them as separate slices.
- **Decision (user-delegated; locked):** include ALL the following in S5:
  - **#1+#2 — `DeferQueue` Mutex → RefCell, AtomicBool → Cell<bool>.** Owner-thread-only by D248-D249 construction; the lock + atomic are unused capacity. Drops the lock acquire on every owner-side defer post/drain (the hottest D251 path).
  - **#7 — typed `MailboxOp::TimerEmit(NodeId, HandleId)` variant.** Audit `timer.rs` `window_time`/etc. + every `mailbox.post_defer(SendDeferFn)` call site. For SendDeferFn payloads whose body is `core.emit(n, h)` (most timer-task closures by inspection), introduce a typed variant + a `post_timer_emit` method, dropping the Box alloc + dyn dispatch per timer fire. `MailboxOp::Defer(SendDeferFn)` stays as the rare-escape-hatch for genuinely non-emit timer closures (if any survive the audit; if none, delete the variant entirely — keep audit honest).
  - **#10 — test-file module-doc sweep.** `crates/graphrefly-core/tests/lock_discipline.rs:1-27` module-doc header still claims "Core::subscribe acquires wave_owner (re-entrant) first"; grep + fix any other test-file headers with similar wave_owner / partition_wave_owner / "Cross-thread emits block" prose.
  - **#4+#6+#8+#9 — process-discipline memory.** Write `feedback_pre_design_full_decision_set.md` (memory-track) capturing: (i) pre-design the FULL decision-set before slicing — avoid the D232→D232-AMEND→D233→D243→D244→D245→D246-r8-stale-premise pattern; (ii) design facade traits (CoreFull-shape) with full method surface once, not via accretion; (iii) cite spec rule IDs (R-x.y.z) in test expectation vectors — the S4 4-of-4 first-commit failures (forgetting push-on-subscribe cached-initial replay, R1.3.5.a / spec §2.2) are the cost of intuition-anchored tests; (iv) at design time audit user-visible semantics encoded by per-emission behavior (the M2 compact_every cadence regression masked by D251's "internal refactor, unchanged public API" framing).
- **Rationale:** Tier A items are all "owner-thread-only by D248 construction ⇒ no cross-thread primitive needed" or "typed-variant the hot path" — net code REMOVED + perf wins. The process memory is the "lessons captured" deliverable from the S2c-S4 reflection so future slices don't recur the pattern.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-rs` `crates/graphrefly-core/src/mailbox.rs` (DeferQueue RefCell+Cell, MailboxOp variant, post_timer_emit, doc updates), `src/node.rs` (drain_mailbox match arms), `src/lib.rs` (re-exports), `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/temporal.rs` + any other SendDeferFn callers (switch to post_timer_emit), test-file module doc(s); `~/.claude/projects/-Users-davidchenallio-src-graphrefly-ts/memory/feedback_pre_design_full_decision_set.md` (new) + `MEMORY.md` pointer; `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/{migration-status.md S5 block, porting-deferred.md (resolve the doc-sweep residue + any §10 items D254 covers)}`. Decision: this entry. Canonical: this entry + D246 + D248 + D249 + D251.

#### D254-AUDIT — #7 typed `MailboxOp::TimerEmit` outcome (2026-05-19, S5 implementation)

- **Audit done** at S5 start (grep + read of every `em.defer(...)` and `mailbox.post_defer(...)` call site in `graphrefly-operators` + `graphrefly-graph` + `graphrefly-storage`). The premise "most timer-task closures' body is `core.emit(n, h)`" does not hold on actual inspection: every surviving `SendDeferFn` payload is non-emit or non-static-NodeId.
  - `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/temporal.rs:1408` — `c.emit(*cur.lock(), h)` (NodeId dynamic via `Arc<Mutex<NodeId>>` — window-rotation routing selector resolved at drain time, NOT a static `(NodeId, HandleId)` capture).
  - `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/temporal.rs:1416` — `c.complete + c.complete` (2 ops).
  - `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/temporal.rs:1430` — `b2.retain_handle + c.error + c.error` (3 ops).
  - `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/temporal.rs:1452` — window rotation: `c.complete + c.register_producer + b.intern_node + c.emit` (multi-op + topology mutation).
  - `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/producer.rs:379` — `c.unsubscribe(n, s)` (not emit).
  - `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/higher_order.rs:186 / 189 / 1054` — `c.invalidate` / `c.teardown` / inner subscribe (not emit).
- Per-timer-tick **DATA** emits already take the **typed `MailboxOp::Emit`** fast path via `em.emit_or_defer(pid, h)` → `mailbox.post_emit` (zero `Box` alloc, zero dyn dispatch). The Box+dyn savings #7 targeted are already captured by the existing typed `Emit` variant; there is no untapped budget for `TimerEmit` to convert. Test sites (`tests/lock_released.rs:103/299/446`, `tests/lock_discipline.rs:163/282`) all post non-emit `SendDeferFn`s as well.
- **Outcome (within D254's own "keep audit honest" gate, user-confirmed at S5 HALT):** do NOT add `MailboxOp::TimerEmit` / `CoreMailbox::post_timer_emit`. `MailboxOp::Defer(SendDeferFn)` SURVIVES as the legitimate escape hatch for the multi-op / dynamic-routing / topology-mutation closures the design predicted. Process shape: same as D251's "rule-8 = reusable slot" reconciliation within D246-r8's stated latitude — staying inside the locked decision, NOT a new fork (the audit was an in-slice reconciliation; the next decision number, D255, is reused by the S6 HALT below).
- **Affects:** zero code delta for #7 in the S5 commit. The rest of D254 (#1+#2 `DeferQueue` Mutex/Atomic relaxation, #10 doc-sweep, #4/#6/#8/#9 process memory) lands as originally scoped.

### D255 — S6: napi binding `Core`-access shape under post-S2c `!Send + !Sync` Core
- **Date:** 2026-05-19 (S6 HALT)
- **Context:** Post-S2c (`0182c18`, D247/D248/D249) `Core` is `!Send + !Sync`; `impl Clone for Core` is deleted (D221/D246). `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/core_bindings.rs` (~1860 LOC) + 5 sibling binding files (operator/graph/storage/structures, ~5900 LOC total, 209 `core.clone()` sites + 18 `spawn_blocking(move || { core... })` captures + all 6 `Bench*` structs storing `core: Core` by value) fail to compile against the post-S2c substrate. The S6 lock (`~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/migration-status.md` § "S6 — PLANNED") surfaced three credible Core-access shapes (α / β / γ) and explicitly marked the choice as a design-bearing HALT trigger.
- **Options:** A) **α — owner-thread-pinned worker** (dedicated `std::thread::spawn` per `BenchCore` owns `Core` by value; napi methods send `FnOnce(&Core) + Send + 'static` closures via channel + oneshot reply). B) **β — mailbox-only async API** (every method posts a `MailboxOp` / `MailboxOp::Defer` reply-closure; no dedicated owner thread; napi method runs on whatever thread receives the JS call). C) **γ — sync owner-thread API via `spawn_blocking` onto a pinned thread** (per S6 lock step 4 wording — but `napi::tokio_runtime::spawn_blocking` routes to tokio's general blocking pool with no thread-affinity guarantee, so a strict reading of γ collapses to either γ.i `LocalSet` (blocks runtime worker) or γ.ii dedicated thread + channel, the latter of which is mechanically identical to α).
- **Decision (user-locked):** **A — α/γ-converged actor.** A new `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/core_actor.rs` module exposes `CoreActor { sender: crossbeam_channel::Sender<Box<dyn FnOnce(&Core) + Send + 'static>>, join: Mutex<Option<JoinHandle<()>>>, generation: u64 }` + `Arc<CoreActor>::run<F, R>(f) -> impl Future<Output = R>` (oneshot reply via `std::sync::mpsc::sync_channel(1)`, mirroring the existing `bridge_sync` style) + `dispatch_detached<F>(f)` (fire-and-forget for `Drop` paths). Every `Bench*` wrapper drops `core: Core` and stores `actor: Arc<CoreActor>` instead. The actor worker thread owns `Core` by value (single-owner invariant preserved end-to-end); when all `Arc<CoreActor>` clones drop, the channel `Sender` count hits zero, the worker's `recv()` returns `Err`, the loop exits, and `Core` drops on the worker stack.
- **Rationale:** **β is structurally dead** — [`operator_bindings::bridge_sync`](`~/src/graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/operator_bindings.rs:210`) blocks the calling thread on `sync_channel::recv` while the JS callback is dispatched as a libuv microtask; under β the napi method *itself* runs on the libuv thread, so the wave runs on libuv, `bridge_sync` blocks libuv, libuv never pumps the TSFN microtask, deadlock. This is exactly the deadlock D070/D077 documented when async was introduced; β re-creates the pre-async state. **γ collapses to α** at the implementation level — `napi::tokio_runtime::spawn_blocking` has no thread-affinity guarantee, so a real "pin Core to one tokio worker" requires either `LocalSet` (blocks the runtime worker for its lifetime — defeats napi's tokio integration) or a dedicated `std::thread::spawn` + channel (mechanically α). The wrapper.js Option C async public surface (D206/D207, already shipped) abstracts the choice from JS callers — they see Promises either way, so async-fn-vs-sync-fn at the napi surface is not load-bearing. The actor shape gives a clean owner-thread invariant Core can be reasoned about, eliminates the `current_core()` thread-local hot-swap on every `run_blocking` call, and structurally resolves the D252 pre-claim handle-leak (the panic invariant cannot fire when each BenchCore has its own actor thread — though folding that into S6 vs a follow-on is a separate decision, D258).
- **Affects:** `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/core_actor.rs` (NEW, ~200 LOC); `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/{core_bindings,operator_bindings,graph_bindings,storage_bindings,structures_bindings}.rs` (drop `core: Core` field, route every method through `self.actor.run(...)`); `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/Cargo.toml` (add `crossbeam-channel` workspace dep); `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/lib.rs` (module add). `.github/workflows/ci.yml` `bindings-js` + `napi-build-matrix` jobs revert from `if: false` to the prior bot/release `if:` condition. **No graphrefly-core change** (S6 stays a binding-only slice — D256 commits to that). **No cross-track-ledger event for the actor itself** (`Impl` contract surface unchanged; `@graphrefly/native` async public surface unchanged). A `cross-track-ledger.md` §2 row WILL be added at S6-close documenting the napi-side D248/D249 reconciliation completion + rust-arm parity-tests runtime activation (`packages/parity-tests/impls/rust.ts` typecheck-only failures resolve to runtime-green). Canonical: this entry + D247 + D248 + D249 + D252 + S6 lock text in `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/migration-status.md`.

### D256 — S6: `BindingBoundary::invoke_fn` producer-dispatch `current_core()` mechanism
- **Date:** 2026-05-19 (S6 HALT)
- **Context:** `BindingBoundary::invoke_fn` ([`graphrefly-core/src/node.rs:1848`](../graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-core/src/node.rs)) does not receive `&Core` directly — its producer-dispatch branch in `core_bindings.rs:362` reads a thread-local `Core` (set by `CoreThreadGuard` inside `run_blocking`) to construct a `ProducerCtx`. D255's α/γ-actor moves the Core off the tokio blocking pool onto a dedicated worker thread; the `current_core()` mechanism needs to be rebuilt on that thread.
- **Options (as originally framed):** A) **Keep `thread_local!(RefCell<Option<Core>>)`** — install on each actor-closure entry via the existing `CoreThreadGuard` pattern, just moved from `run_blocking` to the actor worker loop. Smaller blast radius; S6 stays binding-only; the actor worker thread becomes the new "current Core" host. B) **Widen `BindingBoundary::invoke_fn` to receive `&Core` directly** — `fn invoke_fn(&self, &Core, node_id, fn_id, dep_data) -> FnResult`. Cleaner long-term shape — eliminates the thread-local hot-swap entirely, makes the binding contract structurally aware of the Core borrow it's serving. But touches `graphrefly-core/src/node.rs` (BindingBoundary trait) + every `impl BindingBoundary` across operators/storage/structures + every test-crate binding. Cross-track-ledger event — substrate-trait widening.
- **Decision (user-locked, original):** **A — keep `thread_local!(RefCell<Option<Core>>)`.**
- **Premise-check reconciliation (S6 implementation start, 2026-05-19, [feedback_verify_premise_before_greenfield](.claude/projects/-Users-davidchenallio-src-graphrefly-ts/memory/feedback_verify_premise_before_greenfield.md)):** at S6 implementation start a grep of the substrate surface surfaced that **`BindingBoundary::invoke_fn_with_core(node_id, fn_id, dep_data, core: &dyn CoreFull)` already exists on the substrate trait** ([`crates/graphrefly-core/src/boundary.rs:230`](../graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-core/src/boundary.rs:230)), added by **D245/D246-r5**, with a **default delegating impl** (`fn invoke_fn_with_core(&self, …, _core) { self.invoke_fn(node_id, fn_id, dep_data) }`) so every existing `impl BindingBoundary` (operators/storage/structures test harnesses, etc.) is **completely unaffected**. The doc on the method explicitly states: "the build path receives a Core facade explicitly **without** a thread-local / `Core` clone / stored back-reference (all β-invalid under the actor model — `Core` is move-only)." `Core::batch::pick_next_fire`'s producer dispatch already calls `invoke_fn_with_core` ([batch.rs:1233](../graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-core/src/batch.rs:1233)), and `ProducerCtx::new` takes `&dyn CoreFull` (not `&Core`). The substrate was already designed for the actor model; the `current_core()` / `CoreThreadGuard` plumbing on the binding side is **pre-D245 legacy** that nobody had reason to delete yet. **Original D256 Option B's "trait widening" framing was wrong** — the trait *was* widened, but as an *additive override with a back-compat default*, so taking it changes nothing for other bindings.
- **Decision (re-locked at premise reconciliation, 2026-05-19):** **C (corrected) — override `invoke_fn_with_core` in `BenchBinding`; DELETE `CURRENT_CORE` / `CoreThreadGuard` / `current_core()` entirely.** Build `ProducerCtx` from the passed `&dyn CoreFull` directly. The actor worker loop just runs `closure(&core)` — no thread-local install dance per closure dispatch.
- **Rationale:** strictly better than the original Option A — less code, no thread-local hot-swap per call, structurally matches the actor model the substrate was already designed for. No substrate change (the trait was widened back in D245); no other-binding impacts (every other `impl BindingBoundary` keeps the default delegating shape and is unaffected); no cross-track-ledger event (`invoke_fn_with_core` was already in the public surface). Reconciled in the same shape as the D254-AUDIT inline reconciliation: stays inside the D256 decision number, records the premise correction, no new D-number minted. The original Option A wording is preserved above for historical traceability.
- **Affects:** `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/core_bindings.rs` — DELETE the `CURRENT_CORE` thread_local + `CoreThreadGuard` + `current_core()` (lines 58–98); add `fn invoke_fn_with_core(...)` override on `impl BindingBoundary for BenchBinding` (mirrors the existing `invoke_fn` body but reads `core: &dyn CoreFull` directly for the producer-dispatch branch); the original `invoke_fn` impl stays in place (Core's non-producer dispatch paths still call the parameterless variant). No graphrefly-core change. No cross-track-ledger event. Canonical: this entry + D255 + D245 + D246-r5.

### D257 — S6: GLOBAL_CORE singleton retention
- **Date:** 2026-05-19 (S6 HALT)
- **Context:** [`static GLOBAL_CORE: OnceLock<Arc<BenchCore>>`](`~/src/graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/core_bindings.rs:1822`) + 6 `global_*` napi entry points provide a singleton `BenchCore` for the cross-Worker bench harness. The S6 lock step 5 wording — "Drop the global; per-binding instantiation. If a singleton-like pattern is needed, use `thread_local!(RefCell<Option<BenchCore>>)` on the owner thread" — argued for deletion.
- **Options:** A) **Keep** — D255's new `BenchCore` (Arc<CoreActor> + Arc<Mutex<Vec<…>>> + Arc<BenchBinding>) is Send+Sync; `OnceLock<Arc<BenchCore>>` works unchanged; the 6 `global_*` entry points keep routing through the actor. B) **Drop entirely** — per the S6 lock; costs ~30 LOC of `global_*` entry-point removal + whatever parity harness calls them. C) **Keep behind `#[cfg(feature = "global-core")]`** — compromise; adds Cargo feature plumbing.
- **Decision (user-locked):** **A — keep.**
- **Rationale:** New `BenchCore` is Send+Sync by construction; the `OnceLock` is non-blocking; the singleton is convenient for the existing bench harness and parity-tests scaffolding. The S6 lock's "drop the global" wording was written assuming the cross-Worker model needed deletion; under D255's actor the singleton works structurally without disrupting the cross-Worker pattern (all callers route through the same actor). Reverses S6 lock step 5; flagged as a scope-shrink from the original lock.
- **Affects:** zero code delta beyond the actor-storage swap (`Arc<BenchCore>` was already Send+Sync and still is). Canonical: this entry + D255.

### D258 — S6: D252 binding-layer fold-in sequencing
- **Date:** 2026-05-19 (S6 HALT)
- **Context:** Two D252-flagged binding-layer items deferred from S5 /qa to S6 (`~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/porting-deferred.md:151` "D252 record-and-skip"): (a) pre-claim handle-leak when a hypothetical out-of-tree cross-Core same-thread `BenchCore::emit` panics in `claim_in_tick`; (b) `cfg(napi)`-friendly panic message that mentions `BenchCore` instead of internal Rust docs.
- **Options:** A) **End of S6 in the same gate** — reconcile structurally first (actor lands; pre-claim handle-leak becomes structurally impossible since each BenchCore has its own actor thread); then in the same slice soften the panic message under cfg(napi). Single gate, single commit, one /qa pass. B) **Separate post-S6 follow-on** — keep S6 strictly to the lock's 1–8 steps. The D252 fold-in becomes a separate small /porting-to-rs slice once S6 is green. Cleaner commit history; two gates.
- **Decision (user-locked):** **B — separate post-S6 follow-on.**
- **Rationale:** Cleaner commit history + tighter S6 scope. The α/γ-actor change is already substantial (~5900 LOC touched); folding D252 into the same commit makes the S6 diff harder to review and conflates "substrate reconciliation" with "binding-layer hardening." Separate slice lets each gate cleanly verify a single intent.
- **Affects:** S6 scope strictly limited to lock steps 1–8 sans D252 items. A new follow-on `/porting-to-rs` slice (call it S7 once S6 closes) handles the D252 pre-claim handle-leak + cfg(napi) panic-message softening. Canonical: this entry + S6 lock + D252.

### D259 — S7: TSFN-bridged parity regression — debug-first slice shape (instrument → fix-as-evidence; D258 folded in)
- **Date:** 2026-05-20
- **Context:** S6 /qa closing surfaced 35 parity failures across 6 scenario files, all using `bridge_sync`/`bridge_sync_unit` (Blocking TSFN dispatch from the post-S6 actor worker thread). Failure pattern uniform "emissions lost." Carried to S7 (`~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/porting-deferred.md:92` § "S7 follow-on"). Premise-check ruled out TS-side `/dev-dispatch` work as the cause: pure-ts arm passes uniformly across all 35 scenarios; none of the failing scenarios are new since the last green parity (Option C close, 2026-05-15); the TS substrate changes since green (`01d687f` pause-buffer +127, `2d6b70c` setDep widening +94, `4613987` public node options +127) are gated by either `skipIf(nativePending)` or are entirely new scenarios not in the failure list; `ReactiveMap.get/has` async widening (`4613987`) is the **TS-side of S6/QA F3**, not a precursor. The regression is structurally the post-S2c→S6 binding rebuild (~3,400 LOC delta in bindings crate, new `core_actor.rs` 586 LOC, every `bridge_sync` site now dispatched from a pinned `std::thread::spawn` worker vs the pre-S6 tokio blocking pool).
- **Options (Q1 — debug protocol):** A) Phase A instrumentation traces first (eprintln! at bridge_sync entry/exit, bridge_sync_unit, invoke_tap_fn dispatch sites, core_actor worker closure boundary); fix-as-evidence in Phase B. B) Skip straight to H4 (M1 `catch_unwind` + BatchGuard panic-discard interaction); instrument only that path. **(Q2)** If H4 turns out to be the bug, the fix changes M1's contract — HALT and let user decide. **(Q3)** D258 (cfg(napi) panic-message softening + pre-claim handle-leak — the latter structurally moot under per-BenchCore actor thread) folds into S7 or stays separate. **(Q4)** Slice shape light (debug + fix) vs full (design).
- **Decision (user-locked, 2026-05-20):** **Q1 = A** (Phase A instrumentation first, fix-as-evidence). **Q2 = escalation rule** — if Phase A/B traces show H4 (M1 `catch_unwind` swallows the unwind that `Core::BatchGuard::Drop` relies on for panic-discard semantics; actor caller sees `Ok(())` while wave was discarded), HALT before fixing — the fix changes M1's "worker panic isolation" contract and needs explicit user approval. **Q3 = fold in** (D258 binding-layer items land in S7's closing commit). **Q4 = light/debug shape** with explicit HALT-on-structural-fix gate (Q2).
- **Rationale:** Phase A is cheap, surfaces evidence without commitment, and disambiguates H1–H4 in one cycle. H4 specifically is the highest-prior hypothesis but its fix tradeoffs (worker liveness vs panic-discard) deserve a fresh decision, not autonomous resolution. D258 fold-in matches its original "fold into S6 → fold into S7" trajectory and the pre-claim handle-leak is now structurally moot under D255's per-BenchCore actor thread. Light shape because debug + likely-small-fix is the realistic surface; HALT gate (Q2) prevents drift if the bug turns out to need a larger seam.
- **Affects:** `~/src/graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/{operator_bindings,core_bindings,core_actor}.rs` (instrumentation + fix sites); `~/src/graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-core/src/batch.rs:2593,2633` (invoke_tap_fn dispatch trace sites if read-side instrumentation needed); regression test at `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/tests/` or `~/src/graphrefly-ts/packages/parity-tests/scenarios/` pinning the panic-discard-vs-actor-catch interaction; `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/{migration-status.md S7 close block, porting-deferred.md delete S7 entry}`; D258 fold-in. Canonical: this entry + D255 + D258 + porting-deferred § S7.

### D261 — S7 follow-on within slice: `try_subscribe` handshake-fire mailbox drain (Option D)
- **Date:** 2026-05-20
- **Context:** D260 (wave-end re-drain loop in `BatchGuard::Drop`) fixed 34/35 parity failures. The remaining one (`scenarios/messaging/subscription.test.ts > view(slice) emits [start,stop)` — rust arm) surfaced the **same root mechanism at a different boundary**: `Core::try_subscribe`'s handshake-fire phase (R1.3.5.a per-tier `[Start]/[Data(cache)]?/[Complete]?/[Error(h)]?/[Teardown]?` slices, [`crates/graphrefly-core/src/node.rs:3437-3458`](../graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-core/src/node.rs)) fires sinks **lock-released, outside any `BatchGuard`**. If those sinks post to `CoreMailbox` (e.g. `graphrefly_structures::reactive::SinkEmitter::emit`'s `mailbox.post_emit`), the post sits stranded until the next external wave entry. Specifically: the `view(slice)` test does `appendMany` → `log.view(slice,…)` → `view.subscribe(js_sink)`. `log.view(…)` internally calls `core.subscribe(log.node_id, internal_sink)` — push-on-subscribe replay fires `internal_sink` inline with log's cached `[10,20,30,40]`; the internal_sink computes `[20,30]` and posts `MailboxOp::Emit(view_node, packed)`. **No wave drains.** When `view.subscribe(js_sink)` runs, `view_node.cache == NO_HANDLE`, push-on-subscribe replay omits `[Data]` from the handshake → JS sub never sees `[20,30]`. Same bug class as D260, different boundary. `view(tail)` test passes purely because its setup is `view→subscribe→THEN append` (steady-state via wave drain), not push-on-subscribe replay.
- **Options:** D) Drain mailbox at end of `try_subscribe` (smallest, ~10 LOC, mirrors D260's shape). E) Generic "post-handshake-drain" helper covering every site that fires sinks outside a wave (~30 LOC, speculative — only one such site currently). F) Carry as a separate S7.1 follow-on slice (close S7 with D260's 34/35 fix; spawn view(slice) standalone).
- **Decision (user-locked, 2026-05-20):** **D**. Implement post-handshake-fire mailbox drain in `try_subscribe`: after the per-tier-slice fire loop, before returning `Ok(sub_id)` (so before `run_wave_for` if any activation is needed), check `mailbox.is_runnable() || deferred.is_runnable()` and enter a brief `BatchGuard` to drain. D260's existing loop in `BatchGuard::Drop` handles any fire_deferred-induced subsequent posts (drain-to-quiescence).
- **Rationale:** same bug class, same shape of fix, well-understood. Localized; doesn't touch `try_subscribe`'s Slice X4/D2 `subscribers_revision` freeze semantics. Mirrors D260's "drain-to-quiescence past the boundary" framing. Cost when no mailbox post happens (push-on-subscribe replay with no SinkEmitter): one `runnable` atomic load. **Q7 sidecar** (user 2026-05-20): the pure-ts-arm `switchMap completes when outer completes with no active inner` bug surfaced post-D260 (35 → 2 fails, the 2nd being pure-ts higher-order semantics, unrelated to D260's Rust-only path) is **out of S7 scope**; carried to the next `/dev-dispatch` batch (memory `project_next_optimizations_batch.md` updated 2026-05-20).
- **Affects:** `~/src/graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-core/src/node.rs` `Core::try_subscribe` (post-handshake-fire mailbox drain block); D260 in `BatchGuard::Drop` unchanged (the existing loop handles post-fire_deferred posts from the new subscribe-time drain). No new substrate symbol; no `Impl` widening; no cross-track-ledger event. Canonical: this entry + D260.

### D262 — S7 /qa: outer-loop cap + panic-isolation hardening + Rust-canonical timing lock
- **Date:** 2026-05-20 (S7 /qa)
- **Context:** S7 /qa surfaced three converged findings from Blind Hunter + Edge Case Hunter parallel review (full audit transcript in agent outputs at /qa-time): (A1) D260's outer `loop { drain+extract+clear+fire_deferred+release; if !runnable break; claim_in_tick }` lacks an outer iteration cap — `drain_and_flush` is internally capped per-call by `max_batch_drain_iterations`, but a sink emit-loop (sink posts MailboxOp on every fire) would silently livelock vs pre-S2b's stack overflow (loud crash). (P1) `fire_deferred`'s internal `last_panic` + `resume_unwind` discipline propagates a sink panic *out* of the call; the new D260 loop body didn't wrap `fire_deferred` in `catch_unwind`, so a panic in iteration N escapes the loop bypassing `snapshot_releases` retain-release + the wave-end `tier3_clear` / `drain_deferred_producer_ops`. (P2) The secondary-pass `claim_in_tick` followed by `debug_assert!(owns, …)` is a no-op in release builds; if `claim_in_tick` ever silently returned `false` (slot held by this Core's generation — should be impossible under D255 actor-model + D248 single-owner, but defense-in-depth), the next `drain_and_flush` would run without ownership, possibly silently corrupting wave state. Plus the cross-arm-timing question (A2) and the canonical-shape question (A3).
- **Options (Q1 — outer-loop cap):** A1.a) Reuse `s.shared.max_batch_drain_iterations` as outer cap (consistent unit; risks N² total work). A1.b) Dedicated `max_wave_end_redrain_passes` Cargo-feature/config knob (cleaner separation, new tunable to maintain). A1.c) Hard-coded constant 32 (simplest, no new tunable, 10× headroom over realistic legit cascades ≤3). A1.d) Defer to follow-on (pre-D260 had same hazard shape, just stack-shaped).
- **Decision (Q1, user-locked 2026-05-20):** **A1.c — hard-coded 32.** Trivial to bump if a real consumer hits it; no config-surface burden; loud `assert!` panic on exceed names the suspect cycle.
- **Options (Q2 — A2 cross-arm timing):** A2.a) Add cross-track-ledger row recording the post-D260 timing semantic (Defer-applied-in-same-wave vs pre-D260's next-wave-application). A2.b) +preventative `runIf` skip-marker on any future parity scenario asserting on this timing. A2.c) Decide one impl canonical + adjust the other. **A2.alt (user counter-proposal, locked):** verify-first — the premise of "TS↔Rust divergence" is *hypothesized*; D260 is the structural completion of D232-AMEND's "drain-to-quiescence in-wave, immediately" contract (Rust under-delivered pre-D260, Rust IS now spec-compliant). Pure-ts has no mailbox indirection (direct-call sink path), so its observable behavior matches the spec naturally — no divergence to document **until verified by an actual parity-arm divergence**. The empirical evidence already exists: 34/35 parity scenarios that flipped rust-arm-failing → cross-arm-passing post-D260+D261 (`buffer`, `view(slice)`, `stratify`, `higher-order`, `subscription`, `control`, `messaging`) ARE the cross-arm-convergence verification. The public `Impl` contract doesn't expose `postDefer` (Rust-internal seam used by `lock_released.rs` test), so an exhaustive Defer-driven late-subscribe-during-fire_deferred parity scenario isn't easily expressible without surface widening — and the user-visible observable shape is already covered by the producer-build operator scenarios that exercise the same code path.
- **Decision (Q2, user-locked 2026-05-20):** **A2.alt — no cross-track-ledger row, no `divergence-*` entry, no preventative skip-marker.** The 34 cross-arm-passing parity scenarios ARE the documentation. A minimal porting-deferred note (under "Behavioral timing observations verified by existing parity scenarios") records the convergence shape + the empirical evidence + the verification path for future re-validation; promote to `cross-language-notes.jsonl` `divergence-*` ONLY if a future scenario surfaces verified divergence.
- **Options (Q3 — A3 canonical):** A3.a) Mint R1.3.6.d in canonical spec (`docs/implementation-plan-13.6-canonical-spec.md`) — "Wave-end mailbox quiescence" rule. A3.b) Document as implementation invariant in D260/D261 entries only — defer formal spec amendment. A3.c) Full defer.
- **Decision (Q3, user-locked 2026-05-20):** **Rust IS canonical for this drain-to-quiescence shape; TS/PY MUST converge if/when they expose an equivalent mailbox-posting sink seam.** Pure-ts today implements the same observable behavior via direct-call sink dispatch (no mailbox indirection → naturally quiescent at wave-end → no "stranded post" hazard); the existing parity scenarios verify the observable-shape agreement. PY (post-1.0) MUST satisfy the same invariant when ported. Folded into the D260/D261 inline doc comments + the S7 LANDED block in `migration-status.md`. Spec R-ID minting (A3.a) is the right long-term home (R1.3.6.d) but deferred to the next spec amendment session — current entries document the invariant as the canonical-Rust shape pending that mint.
- **/qa patches landed (P1–P6, user-approved batch):** P1 — wrap `fire_deferred` in `catch_unwind` inside D260's loop; release `snapshot_releases` defensively + run `tier3_clear()` + `drain_deferred_producer_ops()` on panic, then `resume_unwind`. P2 — secondary-pass `claim_in_tick` followed by explicit `if !owns { break; }` after the `debug_assert!`, so release builds gracefully exit the loop if the assumption ever silently fails. P3 — tighten D261 regression test `source_sink_fires >= 1` → `== 1` (pin handshake-replay-single-fire invariant). P4 — downgrade D258 binding-friendly framing in S7 LANDED block + porting-deferred entry: the polished panic message reaches Rust's panic hook → stderr, but `core_actor.rs` M1 `catch_unwind` swallows the panic value before it crosses napi → JS users see a sync_channel disconnect, not the message. D258 is a Rust-dev clarity improvement; binding-friendly framing is aspirational pending a panic→JS bridge slice. P5 — polish D260 doc comment to mention same-thread sink case as primary (matching the actual 35-failure bug surface), not just "cross-thread autonomous-timer-task case." P6 — polish D261 inline doc nit ("`BatchGuard` here enters a fresh wave whose `drain_and_flush` applies the queued mailbox ops" → reword: construction doesn't drain, Drop does; add nested-subscribe doc note).
- **Rejected as false-positive / verified-no-issue:** D258 panic-message-string asserts (grep verified — no tests rely on the string); no new `unsafe` / refcount / lock-discipline issues introduced; gate-math `812 = 810 + 2` verified; D261 ordering vs activation (R1.3.5.a verified non-violated by code-trace); nested-`try_subscribe` via Defer (non-owning `BatchGuard::Drop` is correctly a no-op).
- **Rationale:** A1.c chosen for simplest-correct-bounded-iteration; A2.alt + A3 chosen jointly because the spec-convergence framing of D260 (Rust *is* canonical; D260 closes the gap to canonical) makes preemptive divergence-recording incoherent — the convergence IS the news. The patches harden the slice against panic-window growth (P1) + release-build silent-corruption (P2) + regression-test loosening (P3); the doc patches (P4 / P5 / P6) align prose with code semantics so future readers don't inherit misleading framing.
- **Affects:** `~/src/graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-core/src/batch.rs` (D260 loop cap + `fire_deferred` catch_unwind + secondary-pass `!owns` break + doc rewrites; **+ inline panic-message comment at `batch.rs:3480-3506` reframed per P4** — AMENDED 2026-05-21 to include this site, originally missed in the P4 patch); `~/src/graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-core/src/node.rs` (D261 inline doc polish); `~/src/graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-core/tests/d260_d261_wave_end_mailbox_drain.rs` (assertion tightening); `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/migration-status.md` S7 LANDED block (D258 framing downgrade + Rust-canonical lock); `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/porting-deferred.md` (minimal A2 verification note in new "Behavioral timing observations verified by existing parity scenarios" section); this entry. Canonical: this entry + D260 + D261.

### D263 — Next-batch slice scope: A = `setDeps`/`addDep`/`removeDep` trio + B = `terminalAsRealInput` substrate flag

- **Rationale:** A closes the cross-track-ledger §1 D5 row; B closes the DS-2.7.A Rust-side flag-surfacing residual without speculative Impl widening (D196-aligned).
