### D264 — Slice A `fn`-replacement: P1 generic TSFN-backed user-derived napi + reroute `impl.map` (not substrate widening)

- **Date:** 2026-05-20 (`/porting-to-rs` Phase-2 HALT after re-scoping)
- **Context:** Pure-ts `Node.setDeps(deps, fn)` replaces BOTH deps AND the operator fn (same for `addDep`/`removeDep`). Rust `Core::set_deps(node, new_dep_ids)` mutates `dep_records` only; the `fn_id`/`OperatorOp` variant stays bound. The parity test (`scenarios/core/set-deps.test.ts`) builds `dep` via `impl.map(a, fn)` (= `OperatorOp::Map { fn_id }`) then calls `dep.setDeps([b], newFn)` with a fresh fn whose signature is the generic multi-dep-batch shape (not Map's single-arg projector). Initial Phase-2 framing assumed A2 (binding-only TSFN slot rewrite) was clean; deeper read surfaced two structural blockers: (a) Operator(Map) dispatches via `BindingBoundary::project_each` (single-arg per-item), incompatible with a generic batch-shape fn; (b) Core has no `change_fn`/`set_fn_id` method, so even rebinding the TSFN slot can't shift the kind.
- **Options:** P1) Add a generic TSFN-backed `register_user_derived(deps, fn) -> node_id` napi (mirror the existing `register_batch_derived` shape but with a TSFN-call instead of `BuiltinBatchFn` enum); reroute `impl.map` in wrapper.js to use it + JS-side closure cell so `setDeps` rebinds the cell. No graphrefly-core change. **Cost:** new TSFN dispatch path in bindings; `impl.map` is no longer an `OperatorOp::Map` on the rust arm (loses M3 operator-specific optimization for `impl.map`, but other ops untouched). P2) Substrate widening — add `Core::set_fn_id`/`set_deps_and_fn`. Cleaner long-term shape; cross-track-ledger row required; invariant work (when can fn swap? kind-change semantics?). P3) Narrow cross-arm test to dep-only (fn arg ignored on rust arm). Fast but partial parity.
- **Decision (user-locked, 2026-05-20):** **P1.** Honest full-parity for the existing scenario; pre-1.0 free hand on bindings; D196-aligned (the parity scenario IS the forcing function, and P1 satisfies it without speculatively widening the substrate trait).
- **Rationale:** P2 would add a substrate method whose only consumer is the bindings — the cross-track-ledger ledger would flag it as a peer-coupling event for behavior that's locally implementable in the bindings. P3 leaves the D5 row in "partial parity" — a future setDeps consumer (cross-track-ledger evidence: presentation/`graphspec` consumers cited in the D5 row) hits the same gap. P1 confines the work to the bindings layer (D196's "scenario is the receipt"), trades one operator-specific optimization (`impl.map`'s OperatorOp dispatch on rust arm) for honest rewire support, and leaves a clean future option to widen P1's `register_user_derived` to other ops if/when a scenario demands setDeps on them. Scope confined to `impl.map` (the only operator the failing scenario uses); other operators (`impl.combine`, `impl.scan`, etc.) keep their OperatorOp paths untouched.
- **Affects:** `~/src/graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/operator_bindings.rs` (new `register_user_derived` napi method + TSFN dispatch closure + new `Registry` slot for user-derived TSFN closures); `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/core_bindings.rs` (potentially: helper to thread the registration through actor); `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/wrapper.{js,d.ts}` (reroute `impl.map`; add JS-side closure cell on `NativeNode`; add `setDeps`/`addDep`/`removeDep` methods that call `Core::set_deps` + rebind cell + update JS-tracked deps list); parity-tests `impls/rust.ts` (`ImplNode.setDeps/.addDep/.removeDep` wiring); `scenarios/core/set-deps.test.ts` (drop `skipIf(nativePending)` gate).

### D265 — Slice A+B publish gate: hold local

- **Date:** 2026-05-20 (`/porting-to-rs` Phase-2 HALT)
- **Context:** Per N1/D203 flow, pushing the graphrefly-rs commit auto-triggers `@graphrefly/native` republish via the OIDC `native-v*` tag workflow. The slice closes the cross-track-ledger §1 D5 row but also opens a window for any new failure mode introduced by P1's reroute of `impl.map`.
- **Options:** A) Hold local — match `ab133d7` (R2.6.0 self-pause native fix) pattern; user decides when to push. B) Push when gate green to make the new `setDeps` surface available to downstream consumers immediately.
- **Decision (user-locked, 2026-05-20):** **A — hold local.**
- **Rationale:** P1 reroutes `impl.map` on the rust arm — a non-trivial behavioral surface change. Holding local matches the established gate-green-then-user-pushes pattern for native, and avoids accidental publish during review/`/qa` iteration.
- **Affects:** commit lands in graphrefly-rs without push; downstream `pnpm test:parity` exercises it via the linked workspace path (`packages/parity-tests/package.json` `link:../../../graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-bindings-js`); `@graphrefly/native` republish deferred to the user's tag push.

### D266 — Address all 5 open cross-track-ledger native-pending rows as 4 sequenced /porting-to-rs slices

- **Date:** 2026-05-21 (`/porting-to-rs` Phase-2 HALT)
- **Context:** `docs/cross-track-ledger.md` has 5 open native-pending rows: (1) 🟠 `Graph::remove`/`destroy` TSFN deadlock, (2) memo:Re P0 storage durability+reject+F9-driver+rollback, (3) memo:Re P1 `appendLogStorage` mode + `attachStorage(overwrite)` rejection, (4) `appendLogStorage.loadEntries` cursor pagination, (5) memo:Re P2 `ReactiveLogBundle.attach skipCachedReplay`. Item (1) blocks the parity gate today; (2)–(5) are storage/structures contract widenings.
- **Options:** A) One mega-slice. B) Four staged slices, halt-between (`Stage 1 then re-approve`). C) Four staged slices, back-to-back without halt.
- **Decision (user-locked, 2026-05-21):** **C — four stages back-to-back.** Stage 1 = §2 Graph::remove/destroy deadlock; Stage 2 = §2 memo:Re P0; Stage 3 = §2 memo:Re P1 + loadEntries pagination (bundled — both extend `AppendLogStorageTier`); Stage 4 = §2 memo:Re P2. Each stage = own gate-green commit in graphrefly-rs (local-only per D265 publish-gate pattern). One /qa pass at the end.
- **Rationale:** D226 (one boundary, one slice, one commit) preserved at the commit level; user direction is to land them together without re-approving between stages.
- **Affects:** `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/graph_bindings.rs` + `wrapper.js` + `wrapper.d.ts` (Stage 1); `crates/graphrefly-storage/src/{tier.rs,memory.rs,redb.rs}` + `crates/graphrefly-structures/src/reactive.rs` (Stages 2–4); `packages/parity-tests/impls/types.ts` + `impls/rust.ts` + new scenarios (`scenarios/graph/`, `scenarios/storage-wal/`, `scenarios/messaging/`).

### D267 — Stage 1 Graph::remove/destroy fix: drop `run_sync` on read-path bindings + Impl widening to `T | Promise<T>`

> **AMENDED 2026-05-21 (audit L6-001 scope-amend):** the original entry wording said "drop all sync `run_sync` napi methods on `BenchGraph` (and any other binding); make every Core-touching binding async." The landed scope was narrower and correctly so: **read-path methods drop `run_sync`; factory constructors retain it under a lifecycle-precondition rationale** (no subscribers at construction ⇒ no TSFN-callback re-entry hazard ⇒ no D070/D077 deadlock class). The 4 surviving sites are documented at their construction:
> - `graph_bindings.rs:117` (`from_core` constructor — "one-shot factory call... blocking is acceptable")
> - `structures_bindings.rs:200-210` (`BenchReactiveLog::create`)
> - `structures_bindings.rs:543-545` (`BenchReactiveList::create`)
> - `structures_bindings.rs:659-661` (`BenchReactiveMap::create`)
> - `structures_bindings.rs:790-792` (`BenchReactiveIndex::create`)
>
> All 5 sites carry inline rustdoc explaining the lifecycle-precondition rationale; the cross-track-ledger row at line 67 records "Constructor `from_core` + structures `create` factories keep `run_sync` (documented safe — no subscribers exist at construction)". A future binding addition that wants a sync constructor MUST re-derive the same "no subscribers at construction" rationale; a future binding addition that adds a sync **read** method on a Core-touching surface MUST go async per the D267 hazard-class fix.



- **Date:** 2026-05-21 (`/porting-to-rs` Phase-2 HALT)
- **Context:** The ledger's "matches D070/D077" diagnosis of the §2 deadlock is unverified speculation. After reading the binding code, the most likely shape is **TSFN-sink-callback re-entrance into `run_sync`**: the R3.7.3 ordering test calls `g.nameOf(s)` from inside the TEARDOWN sink. On the rust arm `wrapper.js NativeGraph.nameOf` calls sync `bench.nameOf` → `actor.run_sync` while the actor worker is already blocked in `bridge_sync_unit` waiting for that same sink callback to return — classic 3-way deadlock.
- **Options:** F1) Drop all sync `run_sync` napi methods on `BenchGraph` (and any other binding); make every Core-touching binding async. Widen the parity `Impl` contract to `T | Promise<T>` for the affected read methods (`tryResolve`/`nameOf`/`edges`/`describe`/etc.) so the pure-ts arm returns sync values unchanged while the rust arm returns Promises. Every parity scenario writes `await impl.nameOf(s)` regardless of arm; TS resolves non-promise values immediately. **F2)** Document caller obligation: don't call sync binding methods from inside a sink. F3) Add sink-callback-safe pure-read accessors that bypass the actor.
- **Decision (user-locked, 2026-05-21):** **F1.** Eliminate the entire deadlock class structurally; cross-track-ledger row recording the contract widening (same shape as the D5 setDeps widening — pre-1.0, no backward-compat shims).
- **Rationale:** F1 is the only fix that eliminates the hazard class instead of papering over the specific deadlock pattern. The `T | Promise<T>` Impl shape (instead of `Promise<T>` everywhere) avoids artificial `Promise.resolve()` wrapping in the pure-ts arm — the implementation contract stays "what each arm naturally returns," the consumer contract is "always await."
- **Affects:** `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/graph_bindings.rs` (every sync `#[napi]` method that currently uses `run_sync` → `async fn` + `actor.run`); `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/wrapper.{js,d.ts}` (`NativeGraph` methods become async; node access too if it shares the shape); `packages/parity-tests/impls/types.ts` (widen affected `Impl` fields to `T | Promise<T>` and document the `await`-always consumer contract); `packages/parity-tests/impls/pure-ts.ts` (no runtime change — TS types take the widening); parity scenarios (`scenarios/graph/edges.test.ts`, `sugar.test.ts`, `remove.test.ts`, `set-deps.test.ts`, and any other site that calls the widened methods sync) update to `await`; drop the `--exclude` workaround for `remove.test.ts`; cross-track-ledger §1 gets a new row recording the widening.


### D268 — Rollback epoch on `AppendLogStorage` (memo:Re P0(d) parity)

- **Date:** 2026-05-21 (`/porting-to-rs` Stage 2)
- **Context:** memo:Re P0 ledger row included "Mirror the epoch/abort, not just a pending-clear" as a contract obligation. Rust's `AppendLogStorage::flush` is sync end-to-end (unlike TS's microtask-chained async path), so the primary TS rollback bug doesn't structurally apply — but a multi-thread concurrent `rollback()` racing against `flush()` mid-loop could still let pre-rollback buckets land (the lock-released between `mem::take` and per-bucket `backend.write` widens the window).
- **Decision:** Add `rollback_epoch: AtomicU64` to `AppendLogStorage`. `flush()` captures the epoch at start (Acquire). Before each per-bucket `backend.write`, re-load epoch (Acquire) — if advanced, drop remaining buckets and return Ok (best-effort: already-written buckets stay). `rollback()` bumps epoch (`fetch_add(1, AcqRel)`) BEFORE clearing pending — order matters so a flush that already took pending sees the bump on its next per-bucket check.
- **Rationale:** Closes the multi-thread rollback-during-flush window the TS epoch token also addresses. Cheap: one AtomicU64 + per-bucket Acquire load. Tested deterministically via `BarrierBackend` (first write blocks on a barrier; rollback runs on another thread between the first and second writes; second write is aborted via epoch check).
- **Affects:** `crates/graphrefly-storage/src/memory.rs` (`AppendLogStorage::flush` + `rollback`); 2 new cargo tests in `tests/tier.rs`. **NOT extended** to `SnapshotStorage`/`KvStorage` — they hold only ONE pending value at a time; the race window is narrow enough not to warrant the epoch token. Promote if a real consumer surfaces the same hazard.

### D269 — `AppendLogMode` + `LoadEntriesOpts`/`AppendCursor`/`AppendLoadResult` cursor pagination (memo:Re P1 + loadEntries-pagination parity)

- **Date:** 2026-05-21 (`/porting-to-rs` Stage 3)
- **Context:** memo:Re P1 (mode option) + `appendLogStorage.loadEntries` windowed cursor pagination ledger rows. Both extend `AppendLogStorageTier` substrate API; bundled into a single decision since they're co-located in `graphrefly-storage::tier`/`memory.rs` and a shared `AppendLogStorageOptions`.
- **Decision:** (1) New `AppendLogMode { Append, Overwrite }` enum (default `Append`). `Overwrite` skips read-merge in `flush()` — the bucket IS the full contents to persist (delta-shipping into Overwrite silently truncates — caller obligation). New `AppendLogStorageTier::mode()` accessor. (2) New types in `tier.rs`: `AppendCursor { position: u64, tag: Option<u64> }` + `LoadEntriesOpts<'a> { cursor, page_size, key_filter }` + `AppendLoadResult<T> { entries, cursor }`. `AppendLogStorageTier::load_entries(opts)` returns `AppendLoadResult<T>`. Default-impl `load_entries_all(key_filter)` preserves the pre-D269 shape for back-compat call sites. Decoding short-circuits past `start + page_size + 1` to bound consumer working set on partitioned logs.
- **Rationale:** Closes 2 of the 5 open ledger rows in one substrate change. `load_entries(opts)`/`load_entries_all(key_filter)` split avoids a back-compat-breaking sweep (pre-1.0 allows breaking changes per `feedback_no_backward_compat`, but the rename is clearer than a `#[deprecated]` overload). Mode rejection on `attach_storage` deferred — the substrate `ReactiveLog::attach_storage` doesn't inspect sink modes; binding-layer napi attach_storage is also deferred (F18 — no consumer scenario per D196).
- **Affects:** `crates/graphrefly-storage/src/{tier.rs,memory.rs,lib.rs}` (types + mode enum + new `load_entries` shape + per-mode flush branch); `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/storage_bindings.rs` (napi binding widened — `create(... mode_str)` + `mode` getter + `load_entries(key_filter, cursor_position, page_size)` paginated JSON shape); `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/wrapper.js` (`appendLogTier` exposes `mode` getter + `loadEntriesPaged`); parity `types.ts` `TierOpts.mode` + `ImplAppendLogTier.{mode, loadEntriesPaged}` + `ImplAppendCursor`/`ImplAppendLoadResult`; `impls/pure-ts.ts` arm (wires `mode` getter + `loadEntriesPaged`); 6 cargo tests in `crates/graphrefly-storage/tests/tier.rs`.

### D270 — `AttachOptions { skip_cached_replay }` on `ReactiveLog::attach` (memo:Re P2 parity)

- **Date:** 2026-05-21 (`/porting-to-rs` Stage 4)
- **Context:** memo:Re P2 ledger row — TS `ReactiveLogBundle.attach(upstream, opts?)` skips the subscribe-handshake DATA replay when `skipCachedReplay: true` AND the upstream has a cached value. Native obligation: mirror the exact contract (gate on cache-present; drop one replay slice; survive being called inside a batch).
- **Decision:** New `graphrefly_structures::AttachOptions { skip_cached_replay: bool }`. New method `ReactiveLog::attach_with_options(core, upstream, read_value, opts)`; the no-options `attach()` delegates with default opts (back-compat). At attach time, capture `Core::cache_of(upstream)` — if `NO_HANDLE`, the skip flag is no-op (cold upstream's first live emit must land). Otherwise, set a `parking_lot::Mutex<bool>` skip flag; per-batch sink checks-and-clears the flag on the first DATA-bearing batch.
- **Rationale:** Matches the TS semantic exactly for the cached-value case. Sub-cases (b) `replayBuffer:N` and (d) `attach` inside `batch()` deferred — Rust substrate has no `replayBuffer` shape (the JS-side construct doesn't apply); in-batch `attach` needs additional substrate support to defer the handshake to wave-end.
- **Affects:** `crates/graphrefly-structures/src/{reactive.rs,lib.rs}` (`AttachOptions` + `attach_with_options`); `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/structures_bindings.rs` (napi `BenchValueLogBundle::attach(upstream, skip_cached_replay)`); `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/wrapper.js` (`reactiveLog().attach(upstream, opts)`); parity `ImplReactiveLog.attach(upstream, opts?)`; pure-ts arm; 3 cargo tests in `crates/graphrefly-structures/tests/reactive_structures.rs`.

### D271 — Storage cleanup batch: rollback-epoch error-path re-check + `AppendLogSink` trait widening (mode/flush) + `AttachStorageHandle::flush_all` + Overwrite-rejection

- **Date:** 2026-05-22 (`/porting-to-rs` next batch — substrate-only bundle, no forcing function)
- **Context:** Post-D266/D267/D268/D269/D270 the cross-track-ledger §1 + §2 closed all 5 open native-pending rows. Three deferrals remained in `porting-deferred.md`: (B) rollback-epoch is not re-checked in `AppendLogStorage::flush` error-restore paths, so a narrow concurrent rollback-during-write-error interleave re-resurrects a rolled-back bucket on the next retry; (C) `ReactiveLog::attach_storage` does not reject `Overwrite` sinks (the D269 follow-on — TS `attachStorage` throws on the same shape); (D) `AppendLogSink` has no `flush()` and `AttachStorageHandle` has no `flush_all()`, so callers cannot drive sink-side debounced flushes the way `graphrefly_storage::StorageHandle::flush_all` lets them drive snapshot-tier debounced flushes from a reactive timer subgraph (the F9 follow-on). User-locked bundle (B+C+D) under the "clean/correct/simple/performant/less-maintenance-burden" directive.
- **Options surfaced during HALT:** (1) `AppendLogMode` source for the C/D trait widening — Q1=local mirror in `graphrefly-structures` (recommended; cycle blocks forwarding from `graphrefly-storage` because storage already depends on structures for `BaseChange<T>`); Q2=hoist to `graphrefly-graph`; Q3=skip C. (2) D shape — Q4=Option B (handle.flush_all + docs; matches D171 precedent for `attach_snapshot_storage`); Q5=Option A (built-in tokio-driven flush inside substrate; reverses D171).
- **Decision (user-locked, 2026-05-22):** Bundle B+C+D as one substrate-only slice. Q1=local mirror; Q4=Option B. Pre-1.0 free hand applied to the `attach_storage` return-type widening (no compat shim per `feedback_no_backward_compat`).
- **Concrete shape:**
  - **B** — `AppendLogStorage::flush` error-restore paths gain a `restore_or_drop` helper closure that re-checks `rollback_epoch` before re-inserting the bucket back into `pending`. If the epoch advanced during the failing operation, the bucket is dropped (the user's `rollback()` semantic wins; consistent with the existing per-bucket-loop epoch check at the top of the next iteration). Helper is local to `flush` — no public surface change.
  - **C** — `AppendLogSink<T>` gains `fn mode(&self) -> AppendLogMode { AppendLogMode::Append }` (default-impl back-compat). `ReactiveLog::attach_storage` signature widens to return `Result<AttachStorageHandle<T>, AttachStorageError>`; rejects any `Overwrite` sink at attach entry with `AttachStorageError::OverwriteSinkRejected { sink_index }`.
  - **D** — `AppendLogSink<T>` gains `fn flush(&self) -> Result<…> { Ok(()) }` (default no-op). `AttachStorageHandle` becomes generic over `T` and retains `Vec<Arc<dyn AppendLogSink<T>>>`; gains `flush_all()` that drives each sink's `flush()` synchronously, surfacing the first error with a `sink[N] flush:` prefix and short-circuiting on failure (matches `graphrefly_storage::StorageHandle::flush_all`). **No tokio added** — caller wires `interval(debounce_ms) → handle.flush_all()` from a reactive timer subgraph (Option B per D171).
  - **`AppendLogMode` source** — local mirror enum in `graphrefly_structures::reactive` (NOT forwarded from `graphrefly_storage::tier`). `graphrefly-storage` already depends on `graphrefly-structures` for `BaseChange<T>`, so forwarding the other direction would create a dep cycle. The two enum declarations are intentionally identical pre-1.0; a third mode (if ever added) requires coordinated update.
- **Rationale:**
  - **No new napi/`Impl` widening** — F18 (`attach_storage` napi) stays deferred per D196 (no consumer scenario). Substrate-only slice means no cross-track-ledger row; no parity-tests work.
  - **Default-impl trait extensions** preserve compile-compat for the one existing impl (`TestSink` in `crates/graphrefly-structures/tests/reactive_structures.rs`) — only the `attach_storage` return-type widening requires a touch (`.expect(...)`).
  - **Option B over Option A for D** — `attach_snapshot_storage` shipped Option B (D171, 2026-05-14) explicitly to keep `graphrefly-storage` sync + binding-agnostic. The same logic applies to `attach_storage`. The "F9 built-in driver" wording in `cross-track-ledger.md` §2 P0(c) was descriptive of TS behavior; the *parity obligation* is that the Rust arm has a drain primitive callers can wire — that primitive is now `flush_all()`.
  - **Local mirror enum (Q1)** — drift risk for a 2-variant pre-1.0 enum is negligible; hoisting to `graphrefly-graph` would touch ~10 files and stretch graph's semantic scope.
- **Affects:**
  - `crates/graphrefly-storage/src/memory.rs` — B's `restore_or_drop` helper inside `AppendLogStorage::flush`.
  - `crates/graphrefly-storage/tests/tier.rs` — 1 new test (`append_log_rollback_during_write_error_drops_bucket_not_restores`).
  - `crates/graphrefly-structures/src/reactive.rs` — `AppendLogMode` enum, `AttachStorageError` enum, `AppendLogSink::mode`/`flush` default methods, generic `AttachStorageHandle<T>` with `flush_all`, `attach_storage` returns `Result`.
  - `crates/graphrefly-structures/src/lib.rs` — re-export `AppendLogMode`, `AttachStorageError`.
  - `crates/graphrefly-structures/tests/reactive_structures.rs` — 4 new tests (C reject single, C reject mixed N=3, D flush_all happy path, D flush_all error-with-index short-circuit) + 1 existing test updated to `Result` shape.
  - `porting-deferred.md` — move 3 entries to migration-status closing block.
- **No `Impl` widening / no parity scenarios authored** (D196-aligned — F18 attach_storage napi stays deferred until a consumer scenario surfaces).
- **No native publish push** (per D265 hold-local pattern; substrate-only slice with no `Impl` impact, but the established pattern is to gate publishes on user tag pushes).

### D272 — Family-1 sink Arc→Rc + clippy-allow drop + static_assertions lock-in

- **Date:** 2026-05-21 (`/porting-to-rs` 5-stage decision-consistency cleanup batch, stage 1 of 5)
- **Context:** Post-D248/D252 the substrate is `!Send + !Sync` single-owner Core. The 4 sink type aliases (`Sink` / `TopologySink` / `DescribeSink` / `NamespaceChangeSink`) were deliberately relaxed to `Arc<dyn Fn>` (`+ Send + Sync` dropped) per D248, but the residual `Arc` outer container was itself vestigial — `Rc` matches the single-owner-thread shape exactly. The relaxation made the `Arc` lint-failing surface, masked by 11 file-level + 1 per-fn `#![allow(clippy::arc_with_non_send_sync)]` annotations carried as "deferred per D196" framing. This audit-2026-05-21 L1-class finding renames the deferral class to **decision-consistency restoration** (precedent D253 SchedulingGroupId delete; D254-AUDIT Send-closure variant audit): D196 governs ADDING new substrate surface in anticipation of a consumer; REMOVING vestigial surface made dead by an earlier locked relaxation is the opposite — no new consumer signal required. Diagnostic question: *was this surface made dead by an earlier locked relaxation?* — yes (D248). Captured in user memory `feedback_distinguish_vestigial_vs_speculative.md`.
- **Options:** A) Drop the `Arc` outer container in favor of `Rc<dyn Fn>` (the architecturally-correct single-owner-thread shape; matches D248 intent exactly). Drop the 12 clippy-allow annotations. Add `static_assertions::assert_not_impl_any!(...: Send, Sync)` immediately below each type alias to lock D248 intent in the type system. B) Keep `Arc<dyn Fn>` with the file-level allows (status quo — deferred indefinitely under the D196-misframed gate).
- **Decision (user-locked, 2026-05-21):** **A.**
- **Rationale:** D248 single-owner intent is currently encoded in prose comments + per-file clippy allows; the `static_assertions` add a compiler-enforced lock that fails the build at the alias-definition site if a future PR re-introduces `Send` / `Sync` on the callback. `Arc` outer container over `!Send + !Sync` inner content is a vestigial wrapping with no semantic value — `Rc` is one fewer atomic per clone, and matches the bench-proven single-owner shape (D246/S2c). The renumbering from "D266" (used in command-args + memory drafts) to D272 reflects the locked D266 was the storage-batch staging decision, not this cleanup.
- **Affects:**
  - `crates/graphrefly-core/src/node.rs` — `pub type Sink` + `assert_not_impl_any!` lock-in; rustdoc updated.
  - `crates/graphrefly-core/src/topology.rs` — `pub type TopologySink` + lock-in.
  - `crates/graphrefly-graph/src/describe.rs` — `pub type DescribeSink` + lock-in; drop file-level `#![allow]`.
  - `crates/graphrefly-graph/src/graph.rs` — `pub(crate) type NamespaceChangeSink` + lock-in.
  - `crates/graphrefly-graph/Cargo.toml` — add `static_assertions` workspace dep.
  - `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/{buffer,control,temporal,ops_impl,stratify,higher_order}.rs` — drop 6 file-level `#![allow]` + convert `Arc::new(move |...)` sink constructors to `Rc::new(...)`; convert operator-internal `Arc<dyn Fn()>` / `Arc<dyn Fn(HandleId)>` callback fields/returns to `Rc<dyn Fn>`.
  - `crates/graphrefly-graph/src/{describe,observe}.rs` — convert remaining sink-construction sites.
  - `crates/graphrefly-graph/tests/{mount,gap_fills}.rs` + `crates/graphrefly-core/tests/lock_discipline.rs` (file-level + per-fn) + `crates/graphrefly-operators/tests/common/mod.rs` — drop 4 test-side `#![allow]`s; convert sink construction sites.
  - `crates/graphrefly-bindings-js/src/core_bindings.rs` — convert `noop_sink` + `build_tsfn_sink` Arc→Rc.
  - `crates/graphrefly-structures/src/reactive.rs` — convert ~8 sink-construction sites.
  - `crates/graphrefly-core/{benches,examples}/*.rs` — convert sink-construction sites in dispatcher / floor_compare / group_scaling / profile_*.
  - All test files across core/graph/operators/structures — convert `Arc::new(move |msgs|...)` sink constructions to `std::rc::Rc::new(...)`.
  - **D273 follow-on per-line allows** — 5 sites (`control.rs:673` sink_slot + `higher_order.rs:261/555/869` state Mutexes + `operators/tests/common/mod.rs:825` RecorderInner + `lock_discipline.rs:194` TestRuntime) gain a temporary `#[allow(clippy::arc_with_non_send_sync)]` with a `D273 follow-on` comment — the outer `Arc<Mutex<X>>` is genuinely Cat-3 (Family-2) and the workspace-wide sweep deletes them in D273.
- **Gate:** `mise run gate` GREEN — 832 tests pass, 0 skip, fmt+clippy clean (`-D warnings` enforced). Net change: 47 files, +227 / −266 lines.
- **No `Impl` widening / no cross-track-ledger row.** Substrate-internal cleanup.
- **Canonical:** `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/decision-audit-2026-05-21.md` L1-001 / L1-002 framing carrier; memory `feedback_distinguish_vestigial_vs_speculative.md`.

### D273 — Family-2 Cat-3 Arc<Mutex<X>> → Rc<RefCell<X>> compiler-driven sweep

- **Date:** 2026-05-21 (`/porting-to-rs` 5-stage decision-consistency cleanup batch, stage 2 of 5)
- **Context:** D272 dropped the file-level `#![allow(clippy::arc_with_non_send_sync)]` annotations, which surfaced the underlying lint failures on Arc<Mutex<X>> wrappers over `!Send` content (X containing a Sink, or X being a single-owner state aggregate). These were carried as "deferred per D196" framing — same decision-consistency-restoration class as D272 (D248 single-owner relaxation made the Arc wrapping vestigial). Compiler-driven sweep: try `Arc<Mutex<X>>` → `Rc<RefCell<X>>` substitution + `.lock()` → `.borrow_mut()` per receiver; the compiler classifies Category-1/2 (revert: Send+Sync required) vs Category-3 (compiles: vestigial; keep the change). Hours, not days.
- **Decision (user-locked, 2026-05-21):** Cat-3 substitution applied to operator-internal state in `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/{buffer,control,higher_order,ops_impl,stratify,temporal}.rs`. Cat-1/2 reverted with one-line comments naming Send+Sync source.
- **Reverts (Cat-1/2 — stays Arc<Mutex>):**
  - `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/producer.rs` `ProducerStorage` — held inside `Arc<dyn ProducerBinding>` (Send+Sync trait bound).
  - `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/temporal.rs:~1395` `current_inner` — captured by `em.defer(move |c| ...)` which requires `Send + 'static`.
  - `crates/graphrefly-operators/tests/common/mod.rs:~825` `RecorderInner` — `Weak<RecorderInner>` upgrade pattern requires Arc; #[allow]-bounded.
  - `crates/graphrefly-core/tests/lock_discipline.rs:~194` `Arc<TestRuntime>` — test inspects sink-captured handle across closure boundaries; #[allow]-bounded.
- **Cat-3 conversions:** All sink-callback-internal state in `BufferState`/`BufferCountState`/`WindowState`/`WindowCountState`/`ZipState`/`ConcatState`/`RaceState`/`TakeUntilState`/`SwitchState`/`ExhaustState`/`MergeMapState`/`SampleState`/`OnFirstState`/`ValveState`/`SettleState`/`RepeatState`/`StratifyState` + per-temporal-op storage references in `temporal.rs` (the per-sink `st = state.clone()` Rc captures). Drop unused `parking_lot::Mutex` / `std::sync::Mutex` imports + the 5 D272 follow-on `#[allow]` annotations introduced as stubs.
- **Rationale:** D248/D272 made the substrate `!Send + !Sync` single-owner. Operator-internal state captured by sinks runs on the owner thread by construction; Arc<Mutex<X>> was carrying both the atomic refcount + the lock-on-uncontended-mutation tax for nothing. `Rc<RefCell<X>>` matches the actor-model shape exactly (one atomic less per clone; one fewer lock cycle per access). The cross-track-ledger consequence is zero — bindings consume the operator factory APIs, not the operator-internal state types.
- **Method:** Mass `Arc<Mutex<` → `Rc<RefCell<` + `Arc::new(Mutex::new(` → `Rc::new(RefCell::new(` + `.lock()` → `.borrow_mut()` sed; per-receiver revert on Send+Sync compile failure with one-line `// Cat-1/2 (D273): ...` comment naming the source of the bound. Workspace-wide grep showed 160 candidate sites (operator/structures src + tests + benches + bindings); most operator/structures src sites converted clean; bindings/storage/structures-public-types stay Arc<Mutex> as Cat-1/2.
- **Affects (Cat-3 conversions only):**
  - `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/buffer.rs` — 4 sites (BufferState/BufferCountState/WindowState/WindowCountState).
  - `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/control.rs` — 5 sites (OnFirstState + ValveState + SettleState + RepeatState + sink_slot); drop the D272 follow-on `#[allow]`.
  - `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/higher_order.rs` — 3 sites (SwitchState + ExhaustState + MergeMapState); drop the 3 D272 follow-on `#[allow]`s.
  - `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/ops_impl.rs` — 4 sites (ZipState + ConcatState + RaceState + TakeUntilState).
  - `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/stratify.rs` — 1 site (StratifyState).
  - `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/temporal.rs` — 1 site (SampleState).
- **Affects (Cat-1/2 reverts with comments):** producer.rs `ProducerStorage` (Send+Sync trait bound source); temporal.rs `current_inner` (em.defer Send+'static bound); operators/tests/common/mod.rs `RecorderInner` (Weak-upgrade pattern); core/tests/lock_discipline.rs `TestRuntime` (test sink closure capture).
- **Gate:** `mise run gate` GREEN. Net change: 9 files, ~+129/−123 lines.
- **No `Impl` widening / no cross-track-ledger row.** Substrate-internal cleanup.
- **Canonical:** Audit `decision-audit-2026-05-21.md` does NOT explicitly enumerate this finding — it surfaced as a D272 cascade. Justification class: decision-consistency restoration (precedent D253 / D254-AUDIT / D272 / `feedback_distinguish_vestigial_vs_speculative`).

### D274 — Vestigial union-find + defer-shim cleanup (CoreFull-scoped)

- **Date:** 2026-05-21 (`/porting-to-rs` 5-stage decision-consistency cleanup batch, stage 3 of 5)
- **Context:** The D211 "minimal-churn" framing retained 6 vestigial symbols (`PartitionOrderViolation` + the SubscribeError variant + `*_or_defer` family + `DeferredProducerOp` + `push_/drain_deferred_producer_ops`) that have been never-constructed since the §7 group-lock layer was deleted (D246/D248/D253/D255 absorbed the actual machinery; the shim was kept only so downstream code compiled unchanged). Audit L1-002 / L3-001 reframes this as decision-consistency restoration: D196 governs adding new substrate surface; **removing vestigial surface made dead by an earlier locked relaxation is the opposite** — no consumer signal required, just the relaxation itself.
- **Decision (user-locked, 2026-05-21, Q2-reconciled):** Delete the vestigial union-find + defer-shim surface in a single focused commit. **Scope landed on `CoreFull` trait + `Core` inherent impl + operators producer.rs siblings — `BindingBoundary` UNTOUCHED** (audit L2-009 confirmed BindingBoundary is clean; no `*_or_defer` ever lived there — see Q2 reconciliation in the /porting-to-rs HALT thread).
- **Deletions:**
  - **`PartitionOrderViolation` struct** + `SubscribeError::PartitionOrderViolation` variant (node.rs:1065 + 1089).
  - **`CoreFull::emit_or_defer/complete_or_defer/error_or_defer`** trait methods (node.rs:1948/1950/1952) + the matching `impl CoreFull for Core` bodies (node.rs:2040/2050/2056).
  - **`Core::emit_or_defer/complete_or_defer/error_or_defer`** inherent methods (node.rs:3916/4076/4125) — folded into `Core::emit/complete/error` (single dispatch path; no defer-then-immediate-execute shim).
  - **`Core::teardown_or_defer/invalidate_or_defer`** — same vestigial pattern (immediate-run no-op shims around `teardown`/`invalidate`); deleted because they had zero external callers and their `Err` paths were unreachable post-D248/D253/D255.
  - **`Core::try_emit/try_complete/try_error/try_emit_terminal/try_teardown`** + `BatchGuard::try_run_wave_for`'s Result wrapper + `BatchGuard::try_begin_batch_for` (always-`Ok` shim) — inlined into public `Core::emit/complete/error/teardown/invalidate`; drop `Result<(), PartitionOrderViolation>` everywhere.
  - **`DeferredProducerOp` enum** + `Core::push_deferred_producer_op` + `Core::drain_deferred_producer_ops` (the empty shim). Delete the 3 `drain_deferred_producer_ops()` call sites in `batch.rs` + `node.rs`.
  - **`operators/producer.rs` `MailboxEmitter::emit_or_defer/complete_or_defer/error_or_defer`** + `ProducerEmitter::emit_or_defer/complete_or_defer/error_or_defer` — renamed to `emit/complete/error` (the "or_defer" suffix was misleading; these always posted directly to the mailbox).
  - **All 9 `Err(SubscribeError::PartitionOrderViolation(_))` arms** across operators (3 in `higher_order.rs` + 2 in `producer.rs::subscribe_to`).
  - **All `*_or_defer` callsites in operators** (`buffer.rs` ~15, `control.rs` ~20, `temporal.rs` ~10, `stratify.rs` ~5, `ops_impl.rs` ~5, `higher_order.rs` ~5, `source.rs` ~5) — rewritten to `core.emit/complete/error` directly.
- **Inlining details:**
  - `Core::emit` body: assert handle != NO_HANDLE, lock-and-validate state, terminal-short-circuit, `try_run_wave_for(...)` (now infallible). No Result.
  - `Core::complete` / `Core::error`: same pattern — assert, lock, `try_emit_terminal` (now infallible).
  - `Core::teardown`: assert, set up `Rc<RefCell<Vec<NodeId>>>` collection cell (Cat-3 single-owner per D273), `try_run_wave_for(...)`, then walk topology events.
  - `Core::error` extra: still releases the caller's intern share (Slice A-bigger /qa D fix preserved).
- **`BindingBoundary` UNTOUCHED.** Confirmed via:
  - Grep returns zero `*_or_defer` references in `boundary.rs`.
  - Audit L2-009 explicitly closes BindingBoundary trait surface as **clean** (every BindingBoundary widening D232-D249 has a corresponding cross-track-ledger row).
  - `*_or_defer` always lived on `CoreFull` (`node.rs:1869` `pub trait CoreFull`), not `BindingBoundary` (`boundary.rs:188`).
- **Rationale:** D211 was always a temporary framing — explicitly "compile-budget" rather than architectural intent. Post-D246/D248/D253/D255 the machinery the shims protected is gone; the shims themselves remain as pure noise that obstructs reading the dispatch path. Deleting them surfaces the actual control flow (sink fires → `core.emit` → wave). The 9 dead match arms + the panic-on-second-violation paranoia were carrying false signals — readers would think there's still a deferred-retry seam to maintain.
- **No `Impl` widening / no cross-track-ledger row.** Substrate-internal cleanup. `Core::emit/complete/error/teardown/invalidate` public surfaces preserve their pre-D274 signatures (`pub fn emit(...) -> ()`); only the never-Err `try_X` wrappers and `*_or_defer` shims go away. No napi-side change.
- **Gate:** `mise run gate` GREEN. Net change: 13 files, +227/-529 lines (~300-line net deletion).
- **Affects:**
  - `crates/graphrefly-core/src/node.rs` — main deletions (PartitionOrderViolation struct, SubscribeError variant, CoreFull trait+impl methods, Core inherent methods, try_X helpers, DeferredProducerOp enum, push/drain shims, *_or_defer shims, teardown/invalidate shims). Drop unused `parking_lot::Mutex` import.
  - `crates/graphrefly-core/src/batch.rs` — `try_run_wave_for` becomes infallible (drop Result wrapper); `try_begin_batch_for` shim deleted; `begin_batch_for` calls `begin_batch_with_guards` directly.
  - `crates/graphrefly-core/src/lib.rs` — drop `DeferredProducerOp` re-export.
  - `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/{buffer,control,higher_order,ops_impl,stratify,temporal,source}.rs` — rename `*_or_defer` → `emit/complete/error` callsites; delete `Err(SubscribeError::PartitionOrderViolation)` arms.
  - `crates/graphrefly-operators/src/producer.rs` — rename `MailboxEmitter`/`ProducerEmitter` `*_or_defer` → `emit/complete/error`; delete the 2 `PartitionOrderViolation` retry arms in `subscribe_to`.
  - `crates/graphrefly-core/tests/{resubscribable,phase_g_cleanup_node}.rs` — delete `Err(e) =>` catch-all arms (now unreachable with single-variant SubscribeError).
- **Canonical:** Audit `decision-audit-2026-05-21.md` L1-002 (vestigial union-find) + L3-001 (§7-C deferral framing) + Q2 reconciliation in `/porting-to-rs` HALT thread; memory `feedback_distinguish_vestigial_vs_speculative.md`.

### D275 — Storage honest-error + bench-harness hygiene bundle (B1 WAL encode guard + B2 FileBackend case-collision + B4 apply_wal_frame mount/unmount + A2 GLOBAL_CORE doc close)

- **Date:** 2026-05-22 (`/porting-to-rs` next batch — user relaxed the "no-consumer-pressure" deferral rule, recognizing the chicken-and-egg problem; instructed to "pick the immediately clean up and the most impactful batch").
- **Context:** Post-D272/D273/D274 + D271 the substrate cleanup backlog was exhausted under the no-consumer rule. User relaxed the rule (no offering → no consumption) and asked for a coherent batch combining "immediately clean up" + "most impactful" items from the remaining open `porting-deferred.md` entries. Categorization surfaced 4 picks bundled under a storage-honest-error theme — B1 (WAL canonical-JSON encoder rejects cross-impl-divergent inputs at write time), B2 (FileBackend rejects case-insensitive-filesystem collisions at write time), B4 (`apply_wal_frame` finally handles `graph.mount` / `graph.unmount` payloads the decompose side has been emitting), A2 (S0 V3 `GLOBAL_CORE` doc-only close — structurally enforced by D255 post-S6). Decision-guard premise verification dropped two earlier-proposed picks (#4 already shipped 2026-05-21 c0ec1f1 L8-003; #5 contradicted `node.rs:1545-1556` structural cycle-safety guarantee).
- **Options surfaced during HALT:**
  - **B1 subnormals** — Q1: reject subnormals (strictest, picked) vs allow-subnormals-reject-only-NaN/Inf. **Locked: reject subnormals.** Rationale: IEEE-754 formatter divergence is theoretical but tightening the guard closes the divergence vector by construction; graphrefly payloads are integer-counter-dominated, so legitimate subnormal usage is vanishingly rare.
  - **B2 probe trigger** — Q2: first-write only (zero overhead on read/list, picked) vs first-write/read/list. **Locked: first-write only.** Rationale: collisions are write-introduced; read/list paths stay zero-overhead.
  - **B4 cross-track-ledger row scope** — Q3: log Rust-only behavior change with TS audit pending vs audit TS in this slice. **Locked: audit TS in this slice.** Result: TS `applyWalFrame` (`packages/pure-ts/src/graph/graph.ts:6717`) has the same `// Phase 14.6 deferred` gap pre-mirror; TS decompose side already emits the matching payloads (`graph.ts:6633,6641`). Cross-track-ledger §2 row captures the obligation.
- **Decision (user-locked, 2026-05-22):** Bundle B1+B2+B4+A2 as one substrate-only slice. Q1=strictest, Q2=first-write-only, Q3=audit-TS-in-slice.
- **Concrete shape:**
  - **A2 (doc-only close)** — `porting-deferred.md:303` "S0 V3 `GLOBAL_CORE`" entry ~~strikethrough~~ + closure block citing D255/S6 actor-model topology making production multi-Core paths structurally disjoint from the bench-harness `GLOBAL_CORE`. Pure docs.
  - **B1 (WAL encoder guard)** — `ChecksumError::NonCanonicalContent { reason }` variant in `crates/graphrefly-storage/src/wal.rs`. `canonical_json<T>` signature changed from `Result<String, serde_json::Error>` to `Result<String, ChecksumError>` so the writer-side rejection rides the existing checksum-encode error channel. Single-pass `validate_canonical(&serde_json::Value)` recursive walk rejects (a) non-ASCII object keys (UTF-16 vs UTF-8 sort divergence vector) and (b) subnormal `Value::Number` (IEEE-754 formatter divergence vector). NaN/Inf already rejected at `Number::from_f64`-time → flow through existing `CanonicalJsonFailed`. New variant routes through `StorageError::Codec(CodecError::Encode(reason))` via the `From<ChecksumError> for StorageError` impl (`error.rs`). 3 cargo regression tests (1 ascii passes, 2 reject — non-ASCII key + subnormal).
  - **B2 (FileBackend case-collision)** — `crates/graphrefly-storage/src/file.rs` `FileBackend` gains `case_state: OnceLock<CaseState>` + `case_override: Option<bool>` fields. `CaseState` enum: `Sensitive` (no enforcement) or `Insensitive { seen: Mutex<HashMap<String, String>> }`. New builder `with_case_insensitive(forced: bool)` for FS-independent tests. Lazy probe on first `write()` only: writes `.gr-case-probe-{pid}-{nanos}-a.bin` + `fs::metadata` of upper-case form + cleans up; same-length match → case-insensitive. Per-write `check_case_collision(key)` enforcement (only when `Insensitive`) maps `lowercase_filename → original_filename` in the seen-map; cross-case collision returns `StorageError::BackendError { message: "case-insensitive filesystem collision: existing key file ... and new key file ... map to the same on-disk path when case-folded; FileBackend rejects to prevent silent overwrite", source: None }`. `delete()` calls `release_case_slot` to allow casing reuse (no probe trigger on delete — uses `case_state.get()` rather than `ensure_case_state()`). 4 cargo regression tests (1 reject + 3 happy-paths covering overwrite-same-casing / delete-releases-slot / forced-sensitive-no-rejection).
  - **B4 (apply_wal_frame mount/unmount)** — `crates/graphrefly-storage/src/graph_integration.rs:1085-1144` `apply_wal_frame`'s `Lifecycle::Spec` match gains arms for `"graph.mount"` (mount the subgraph if absent via `graph.mount_new(core, path)`; idempotent skip via `graph.child_names().iter().any(|n| n == path)`) and `"graph.unmount"` (unmount if present; idempotent skip otherwise). **No new `WalTag` variants** — the decompose side was always wired (`graph_integration.rs:235-258` emits `graph.mount` / `graph.unmount` payloads via the same `WalTag` unit-struct + `change.kind` discriminator used by `graph.add` / `graph.remove`); B4 only fills the apply side. Replay ordering is correct by construction (decompose emits `nodes_added → nodes_removed → subgraphs_added → subgraphs_removed → value_changes`; `REPLAY_ORDER` puts Spec before Data). 3 cargo regression tests in `crates/graphrefly-storage/tests/graph_integration.rs` exercise the full snapshot+WAL restore path via `restore_snapshot` (replay-mount, replay-unmount, idempotent-mount-onto-already-mounted).
- **Files touched:**
  - `~/src/graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-storage/src/wal.rs` — `ChecksumError::NonCanonicalContent` + `canonical_json` signature change + `validate_canonical` helper + 3 tests.
  - `~/src/graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-storage/src/error.rs` — `From<ChecksumError>` match arm for `NonCanonicalContent`.
  - `~/src/graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-storage/src/file.rs` — `case_state` / `case_override` fields + `CaseState` enum + `with_case_insensitive` builder + `ensure_case_state` / `check_case_collision` / `release_case_slot` methods + `probe_case_sensitivity` helper + write/delete hookup + 4 tests.
  - `~/src/graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-storage/src/graph_integration.rs` — 2 new arms in `apply_wal_frame` `Lifecycle::Spec` match.
  - `~/src/graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-storage/tests/graph_integration.rs` — 3 new B4 integration tests.
  - `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/porting-deferred.md` — 4 rows ~~strikethrough~~ + closure blocks (M4.A B1 / M4.C B2 / M4.E2 mount-unmount B4 / S0 V3 A2).
  - `~/src/graphrefly-ts/docs/cross-track-ledger.md` — §2 row 2026-05-22 (B4) capturing TS-mirror obligation.
- **`Impl` / parity-tests / napi widening:** none. All four picks are substrate-internal storage-tier behavior; no napi binding work in this slice.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-storage` crate behavior (B1, B2, B4); presentation-track TS will follow B4 via a `/dev-dispatch` mirror slice when scheduled.
- **Canonical:** Today's `/porting-to-rs` HALT thread (decisions ratified) + `porting-deferred.md` closure blocks + cross-track-ledger §2 row 2026-05-22 (B4).

### D276 — `Graph::snapshot` + `from_snapshot` cross-mount derived deps (M4.E1 bidirectional fix)

- **Date:** 2026-05-22 (`/porting-to-rs` follow-on slice after D275; user-approved full bidirectional fix after premise verification revealed the original M4.E1 entry was misframed as decode-only).
- **Context:** User asked to address M4.E1 (`from_snapshot` auto-hydration doesn't handle cross-mount deps). Initial chat estimate was "~30 LOC: route the decoder's flat `created.get(dep_name)` through `try_resolve` as a fallback for cross-mount names." Pre-implementation premise verification surfaced that the **encoder was also broken**: `snapshot_of` at `crates/graphrefly-graph/src/snapshot.rs` had `id_to_name: IndexMap<NodeId, String>` built ONLY from THIS graph's local `inner.names`, and the dep-name mapping fell through to `format!("_anon_{}", dep_id.raw())` for any cross-mount dep — destroying the cross-mount reference at serialization time. A decoder-only fallback would have fixed nothing because the qualified path never reached the snapshot. Plus the pre-D276 hydration ordering (subgraphs first → parent) handled parent→child cross-mount deps correctly but BROKE child→parent (the parent's nodes don't exist yet when the child is being hydrated).
- **Options surfaced during HALT:**
  - **Option A — Full bidirectional fix (~365 LOC).** Encode emits owner-relative paths for cross-mount deps + bare local names for same-graph deps (back-compat). Decode: tree-wide four-pass hydration (Pass 0 mount + graph_map; Pass 1 state-first; Pass 2 shared retry loop over derived with `try_resolve`; Pass 3 status). +6 cargo tests covering both cross-mount directions + deep chain + back-compat. Adds cross-track-ledger row obliging TS to mirror.
  - **Option B — Half-fix encode-only (~80 LOC).** Encode emits paths; decode unchanged. Cross-mount deps in NEW snapshots still fail on restore, but at least the path survives. Flagged as 'phase 1' with phase 2 (decode) as a separate follow-on.
  - **Option C — Reframe + close (~5 LOC docs).** Rewrite the M4.E1 entry to capture the bidirectional nature; document that `builder` mode of `from_snapshot` is the canonical answer for complex topologies; close as 'WORKAROUND-DOCUMENTED'.
  - **Option D — Smaller variant.** User specifies a narrower scope (e.g. only parent→child, or only state→state).
- **Decision (user-locked, 2026-05-22):** **Option A — full bidirectional fix.** Aligns with the user's earlier directive to "relax the no-consumer-pressure rule" (chicken-and-egg) and pick the "immediately clean up and most impactful" items. M4.E1 has real impact (auto-hydration + cross-mount deps both go from broken-by-construction to functional) and is bounded scope (~365 LOC + tests, substrate-only).
- **Encoding design (locked):** **owner-relative paths**, not absolute-from-root. Initial draft used absolute paths; mid-implementation review caught the bug — single-segment absolute paths (e.g. cross-mount dep on a root-level node from a deep mount) collide structurally with same-graph bare names ("a" the absolute path of a root node is indistinguishable from "a" the bare local name of any other graph's node). Owner-relative paths using `".."` and `"::"` segments mirror the existing `Graph::try_resolve` syntax (Slice V3 cross-subgraph path machinery) — no marker disambiguation needed, and the decoder can simply call `entry.owner_graph.try_resolve(dep_name)` directly without needing its own segment-walking. Conversion helper: `absolute_to_owner_relative(owner_path, abs_path)` computes the common prefix between owner segments and abs segments, emits `..` for each extra owner segment, then appends the remaining abs segments.
- **Decode design (locked):** **drop the auxiliary `tree_created` IndexMap** in favor of direct `try_resolve` lookups. Initial draft tracked an `IndexMap<absolute_path, NodeId>` populated incrementally; mid-implementation review realized this was redundant — `Graph::state`/`derived` register names in the owner graph's namespace at creation time, so `try_resolve` finds them automatically once created. Net code simplification: ~40 LOC removed.
- **Anonymous-dep fallback unchanged:** dep `NodeId`s not named in ANY graph in the snapshot tree (operator-internal NodeIds, etc.) still serialize as `_anon_<rawid>` and still fail decode with `UnresolvableDeps`. Anonymous-dep restore is a separate concern (would require either binding-assisted ID round-trip or factory-side reconstruction); not in M4.E1 scope.
- **Files touched:**
  - `~/src/graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-graph/src/snapshot.rs` — `snapshot_of` refactor (`build_id_to_tree_path` + `walk_tree_paths` + `absolute_to_owner_relative` + `snapshot_of_with_tree_paths`); `from_snapshot` refactor (`mount_subgraphs_recursive` + `create_state_nodes_recursive` + `collect_derived_recursive` + `DerivedEntry` + `create_derived_with_retry` + `apply_status_recursive`); pre-D276 `hydrate_subgraph` + `hydrate_nodes` deleted.
  - `~/src/graphrefly-rs/crates/graphrefly-graph/tests/snapshot.rs` — 6 new D276 tests (encode child→parent, encode parent→child, round-trip child→parent, round-trip parent→child, deep chain across 3 mount levels, back-compat bare-name shape).
  - `~/src/graphrefly-rs/docs/porting-deferred.md` — M4.E1 row ~~strikethrough~~ + closure block.
  - `~/src/graphrefly-ts/docs/cross-track-ledger.md` — §2 row 2026-05-22 (M4.E1 / D276) capturing TS-mirror obligation.
- **`Impl` / parity-tests / napi widening:** none. Substrate-internal hydration logic; `Graph::snapshot` / `Graph::from_snapshot` public signatures unchanged; on-disk JSON shape unchanged (`deps: Vec<String>` — the encoder just emits richer strings).
- **Cross-impl on-disk shape:** owner-relative path syntax (`..::name`, `child::name`) IS Slice V3's `try_resolve` path syntax — a Rust-encoded snapshot with cross-mount deps is byte-compatible with a future D276-aware TS decoder. Until TS mirrors (TS has the same bidirectional gap per the original M4.E1 entry), Rust ↔ TS snapshots with cross-mount deps diverge: a TS-produced snapshot drops cross-mount refs as `_anon_<rawid>`; a Rust-produced snapshot encoded post-D276 has owner-relative paths that pre-D276 TS would reject as `UnresolvableDeps`.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-graph` crate `snapshot` module. Cross-track: TS `packages/pure-ts/src/graph/graph.ts` `snapshotOf` + `fromSnapshot` should mirror the same bidirectional fix; recommended as a follow-on `/dev-dispatch` slice.
- **Canonical:** Today's `/porting-to-rs` HALT thread (M4.E1 scope locked Option A) + `porting-deferred.md` M4.E1 closure block + cross-track-ledger §2 row 2026-05-22 (M4.E1 / D276).

### D277 — §10.3 + §10.6 bench-evidence pass + D252 (b) panic-msg shape amend

- **Date:** 2026-05-22 (`/porting-to-rs` slice; no obvious next-batch forcing function — user picked options 3 + 4 from the HALT shortlist).
- **Context:** Post-D271/D275/D276 the `porting-deferred.md` open list reduced to (i) bench-gated §10 perf items (10.3 diamond bookkeeping, 10.6 sink iteration) and (ii) D252 (b) panic-msg polish under `cfg(napi)`. Both are bounded substrate-only carries. The user picked a bundle: bench-evidence pass for §10.3 + §10.6 (decide pick-up vs close-as-not-a-win) + D252 (b) amend.
- **Sub-decisions during HALT:**
  - **(Q1) Bench acceptance threshold = ≥5%** (consistent with §10.5's bar; cross-comparable).
  - **(Q2) D252 (b) shape = option (a)** — reduce the JS-targeted paragraph to a single line + keep BenchCore mention as a Rust-dev hint. Option (b) (`#[cfg(feature = "napi")]` softened variant) rejected as speculative scaffolding for an uncommitted panic→JS bridge slice.
  - **(Q3) Gate scope = `mise run gate` (full).** Substrate-internal changes still rebuild the wider workspace.
- **Decision (user-locked, 2026-05-22):**
  - **§10.3 / §10.6:** write two criterion benches paralleling `notification_buffer.rs` (§10.5 precedent). Sweep fan-in N = 1, 4, 8, 16, 32, 64 for §10.3 (diamond resolution); sweep subscribers S = 1, 8, 32, 128, 512 for §10.6 (sink iteration). Verdict per bench: ≥5% projected win at any sample point → convert to a follow-on slice; otherwise close the entry as "validated not a win" with measured numbers (the §10.5 close template).
  - **D252 (b):** reduce the inline JS-targeted paragraph at `crates/graphrefly-core/src/batch.rs` `claim_in_tick` from two paragraphs to a single line. AMEND-D 2026-05-21 reframed the value-add as "Rust-dev clarity only" because `core_actor.rs` M1's `catch_unwind` swallows the panic value before it crosses napi; the polished JS-consumer paragraphs are a cosmetic gap, not a behavioral one. Behavior unchanged (the panic still fires and still carries the same diagnostic load on the Rust panic hook).
- **`Impl` / parity-tests / napi widening:** none. Substrate-internal benches + a panic-message text edit; no on-disk shape, no public API, no cross-track-ledger row.
- **Affects:** `graphrefly-core` crate (`benches/diamond_resolution.rs` + `benches/sink_iteration.rs` added; `src/batch.rs` `claim_in_tick` panic message); `porting-deferred.md` (§10 table updated per bench verdicts); `migration-status.md` (D277 closing block).
- **QA pass refinements (2026-05-22 /qa):** the verdict prose in `porting-deferred.md` + `migration-status.md` was tightened on review. (F1) §10.6 close-block no longer claims "closure-dispatch dominates, not HashMap iteration" as a measurement — the bench measures the SUM of (per-wave subscriber HashMap → SmallVec snapshot build + per-batch SmallVec walk + per-sink `Rc<dyn Fn>` closure call); the ~7 ns/sink marginal is consistent with closure-dispatch overhead and shows no super-linear HashMap pressure, but further component attribution would need a dedicated bench. (F2) The "flush iterates under lock" framing on the §10.6 row is stale: post-D108 Q-beyond, the sink-call loop already runs lock-released via `deferred_flush_jobs`; only the per-wave snapshot BUILD at `batch.rs:3038-3043` still touches `subscribers` under the state lock. The proposed epoch/snapshot-spread refactor would eliminate that build, but the bench shows it is already amortized and shows no super-linear scaling. (F3) S=1 sits on the `SmallVec<[Sink; 1]>` inline branch; S≥8 spills — per-sink slope read from S∈{8,32,128,512}, excluding the S=1→8 inline-vs-spill cliff. (F4) Bench `BindingBoundary::release_handle` is a no-op — measured costs are substrate-internal only; the napi binding's handle-drop crossing is orthogonal to the §10 bookkeeping shape and would not be helped by either refactor. Methodology disclosure added at the §10 table footer in `porting-deferred.md` (covers all three §10 benches: `notification_buffer.rs`, `diamond_resolution.rs`, `sink_iteration.rs`).
- **Canonical:** Today's `/porting-to-rs` HALT thread (D277 scope locked); `porting-deferred.md` §10 table closure blocks + methodology footer; bench files themselves (canonical numbers).

### D278 — E-i + E-ii + E-iv doc-hygiene batch (Commit 1 of the 13-item E-cluster slice)

- **Date:** 2026-05-22 (`/porting-to-rs` HALT after Q1–Q4 user reframing).
- **Context:** Post-D277 the `porting-deferred.md` open list reduced to a long tail of v1-design divergences + best-effort framings that lack consumer pressure. The user asked to attempt the full E-i + E-ii + E-iv cluster (13 items). The HALT applied the user's anti-pattern-#4 framing (no autonomous decisions when spec already answers; no preemptive hypothesized-divergence doc) + D196 consumer-pressure gate + value-#6 pre-design full decision-set, which resolved the 13 items into **4 fixes + 4 doc-only keeps + 5 drops/rejects** across three commits (doc-hygiene → snapshot/storage fixes → R1.4.2 spec-compliance). This entry covers Commit 1 (doc-only keeps).
- **Sub-decisions during HALT:**
  - **(Q1) E-i.1 = R1.4.2 plain-forward** — locked by user as spec-compliance, not a "which semantic?" question (anti-pattern #4). Lands in Commit 3.
  - **(Q2) E-i.4 `pending_pause_overflow` panic-discard = keep current (Option A)** — spec R1.3.8.c is silent on panic-discard semantics; the lift IS a real Rust-impl design call. `BatchGuard` panic-discard atomicity ("the wave didn't happen") is a load-bearing invariant uniformly applied across every retain-holding field; adding an asymmetric ERROR-surfacing exception would weaken atomicity for every other invariant relying on it. The synthesized ERROR is lost on panic; the `ResumeReport.dropped` count IS preserved. Future consumer surfacing ERROR-on-panic should mint a panic-survivable diagnostic side channel as a separate D-number (NOT bolt an exception onto BatchGuard).
  - **(Q3) E-ii.3 `DescribeValue::Rendered(Value::Null)` JSON ambiguity** — deferred to Commit 2 (TS-shape verification side-quest done; Rust converges to TS's existing `sentinel?: boolean` + optional `value?` shape via `#[serde(skip_serializing_if)]`).
  - **(Q4) E-iv.3 + E-iv.4 + E-iv.5 lifts = REJECT all** — each fails D196 consumer pressure. E-iv.3 (unmount-vs-destroy `Message::Unmount` variant OR `RemoveAudit.reason`) is substantial substrate widening for an observability gap with no scenario. E-iv.4 (`tagFactory`/`resourceProfile`) needs parity-scenario-authored-FIRST per D196 — separate `/dev-dispatch`+`/porting-to-rs` paired slice. E-iv.5 (`edges()` cross-graph) is anti-pattern #4 (hypothesized-divergence preemptive-doc; same shape as deferred `try_resolve` cross-graph).
- **Decision (user-locked + my "[No preference]" picks documented):** doc-hygiene commit covers 4 keeps — E-i.4 (Option A panic-discard trade-off + lift-point), E-ii.4 (snapshot torn-read caveat + `Graph::batch`/`signal(Pause)` cross-ref), E-iv.1 (`audit_of` best-effort framing citing D248/D255 single-owner shape), E-iv.2 (`GraphObserveOne` per-tier methods as deliberate divergence from canonical R3.6.2 `up(messages)`, citing `feedback_no_imperative` user memory). Each rustdoc names the specific decision-log or feedback-memory anchor.
- **What is NOT done in Commit 1 (carried to Commits 2+3):** E-i.1 (Commit 3), E-ii.1 (Commit 2), E-ii.2 (Commit 2), E-ii.3 (Commit 2). E-i.2 + E-i.3 + E-iv.3 + E-iv.4 + E-iv.5 dropped/rejected (no doc change either; entries in `porting-deferred.md` left as-is or move to "lift-point gated on consumer pressure" framing if needed in a future doc-sweep).
- **`Impl` / parity-tests / napi widening:** none. Rustdoc-only.
- **Cross-track-ledger row:** none. Substrate-internal documentation; no behavioral change.
- **Gate:** `mise run gate` GREEN — 850 tests passed, 0 skipped (fmt + clippy + nextest --profile ci, 187s, sentinel `<<<RUN-LOGGED:DONE>>> exit=0 reason=ok`).
- **Affects:** `crates/graphrefly-core/src/batch.rs` (`pending_pause_overflow` field + `clear_wave_state` clear comment); `crates/graphrefly-graph/src/snapshot.rs` (`Graph::snapshot` + `snapshot_full` rustdoc); `crates/graphrefly-graph/src/mount.rs` (`GraphRemoveAudit` + `audit_of` rustdoc); `crates/graphrefly-graph/src/observe.rs` (`GraphObserveOne` struct rustdoc).
- **Canonical:** Today's `/porting-to-rs` HALT thread (Q1–Q4 reframing + side-quest verifications + 3-commit split lock); `porting-deferred.md` (4 entries gain back-pointer to D278 doc-hygiene commit on next doc-sweep); `migration-status.md` D278 closing block.
